401 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bunkley


No. 12597


Supreme Court of Connecticut


202 Conn. 629; 522 A.2d 795; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 797


November 4, 1986, Argued  
March 24, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with one count of the crime of engaging police in pursuit, three counts of the crime of manslaughter in the first degree and two counts of the crime of assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before E. O'Connell, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of one count of engaging police in pursuit, three counts of manslaughter in the second degree and two counts of assault in the third degree, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of engaging police in pursuit, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-223(b); manslaughter in the second degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-56, and assault in the third degree, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-61.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in a collision with another vehicle which caused the deaths of three persons. He was convicted of engaging police in pursuit, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-223(b); manslaughter in the second degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-56 and assault in the third degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-61. Defendant sought review of the manslaughter and assault counts. The court held that defendant was properly charged with manslaughter because the legislature included motor vehicles within the definition of "dangerous instrument" under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-56, and specifically excluded deaths caused by vehicles under the negligent homicide statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-58 (a). Further, the court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-57 only applied to vehicular homicides caused by criminal negligence, whereas defendant's conduct, in which he fled from police with rates of speed up to 60 miles per hour, occurred under a more culpable state of mind of recklessness. The court held that the manslaughter statute was not unconstitutionally vague because Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-56 provided defendant with a reasonable opportunity to be aware of the prohibited acts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

 

402 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Texaco Refining & Marketing Co. v. Commissioner of Revenue Services


No. 12966


Supreme Court of Connecticut


202 Conn. 583; 522 A.2d 771; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 793


February 5, 1987, Argued  
March 24, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the defendant commissioner determining that the plaintiff was liable for additional gross earnings taxes, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Shaughnessy, J., pursuant to the stipulation of the parties, reserved a question of law for the advice of the Appellate Court; the reservation was then transferred to this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation appealed to the Superior Court (Connecticut) from a decision of defendant tax commissioner, which held that the corporation had underpaid the gross earning tax imposed by Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 12-587. The superior court granted a motion for reservation upon stipulated facts to determine the propriety of the commissioner's computation of the corporation's gross earnings tax. The reservation was transferred to the court.


OVERVIEW: On its invoices to Connecticut purchasers of its petroleum products, the corporation charged these purchasers separately for the sale price and for the two percent Connecticut gross earning tax that it collected from customers pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 12-587. The corporation did not report the two percent as gross earnings. The corporation argued that moneys collected from consumers for taxes was plainly neither earnings from the sale of petroleum products no did they fall within the "net income" to which § 12-587 applied. The commission argued that the petroleum products tax should have been treated as an item of operating overhead measured in § 12-599(a), by gross earnings derived from the sales of petroleum products in Connecticut. The court determined that moneys collected as a tax from customers was includable in the Connecticut gross earning tax on the sale of petroleum products.


OUTCOME: The court found the commissioner's computation of the corporation's gross earnings tax was proper.

 

403 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Foster


No. 12717


Supreme Court of Connecticut


202 Conn. 520; 522 A.2d 277; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 785


December 2, 1986, Argued  
March 17, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crimes of kidnapping in the second degree, assault in the second degree, manslaughter in the first degree, accessory to kidnapping in the second degree, accessory to assault in the second degree, and accessory to manslaughter in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Barry, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of kidnapping in the second degree, assault in the third degree and accessory to criminally negligent homicide, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) that denied motions for acquittal and arrest of judgment after he was found guilty of kidnapping in the second degree, assault in the third degree, and being an accessory to criminally negligent homicide in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-8 and 53a-58.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that there was no such crime as being an accessory to criminally negligent homicide because it was impossible for him to have intended the consequences of criminally negligent homicide. The court rejected the claim because being an accessory to a crime was not itself a crime. Rather, Conn. Gen. Stat. 53a-8 presented another means by which a substantive crime could be committed. Accessorial liability was predicated on defendant's intentionally aiding an accomplice and with the mental culpability required to commit the crime. The circumstantial evidence was sufficient to prove that crime because it showed defendant was bitter about his girlfriend being raped, he purposefully went looking for the perpetrator, encountered the perpetrator, beat him, and gave his accomplice a knife to keep the perpetrator from leaving. Thus, a jury could reasonably have believed that defendant failed to perceive a substantial and unjustifiable risk that death could occur. Related to the kidnapping charge, the court's review of the jury instructions as a whole showed that the definitions of "restrain" and "abduct" were not misleading or inadequate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

 

404 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Blasko


No. 13003


Supreme Court of Connecticut


202 Conn. 541; 522 A.2d 753; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 786


January 14, 1987, Argued  
March 17, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of sale of cocaine and with two counts of the crime of sale of marihuana, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield, where the court, Pickett, J., in response to a motion filed by the defendant, ordered the suppression of certain evidence obtained by an investigative grand jury; the court subsequently granted the state's motion to dismiss with prejudice the information against the defendant, and the state, on the granting of permission by the trial court, appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Litchfield (Connecticut) that ordered suppression of certain evidence obtained by the investigative grand jury and subsequently granted defendant's motion to dismiss the charges of two counts of sale of cocaine and two counts of sale of marijuana.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with two counts of sale of cocaine and two counts of sale of marijuana. Defendant filed a motion to suppress. The trial court ordered suppression of certain evidence obtained by the investigative grand jury. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss with prejudice. The trial court granted the motion. The State appealed. The court found error and set aside the dismissal. The court held that 1985 Conn. Acts 611, which reformed procedures governing investigatory grand juries and repealed Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-47 under which such grand juries were previously appointed, did not revoke the authority of previously appointed investigatory grand juries. The court found that 1985 Conn. Acts 611 was not intended by the legislature to revoke authority of previously appointed investigatory grand juries. The court noted that 1986 Conn. Acts 317, which declared the preexisting grand juries were to continue until their inquiry was completed, was clarifying rather than curative legislation and did not deprive defendant of any vested rights.


OUTCOME: The court found error, set aside the judgment dismissing the charges against defendant, and remanded for further proceedings.

 

405 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Miller


No. 12490


Supreme Court of Connecticut


202 Conn. 463; 522 A.2d 249; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 790


November 6, 1986, Argued  
March 10, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury and tried to the jury before W. Sullivan, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision by which the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Danbury (Connecticut), upon a jury verdict, convicted defendant of two counts of first degree assault. Defendant claimed, in part: (1) his motion to suppress identification evidence was improperly denied; (2) his right to an impartial jury was violated by the denial of his motion to transfer the case; and (3) the State presented insufficient evidence.


OVERVIEW: A 15-year-old female and a 16-year-old male were viciously assaulted behind a church. The couple was forced at gunpoint by a white assailant to walk to a grassy area where the male victim was handcuffed and his feet were bound. The assailant dragged the female victim down an embankment. During a struggle, the assailant's bandana came off of his face. The assailant beat the female victim with his gun. The assailant choked the male victim until he lost consciousness. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that: (1) the female victim's identification of the assailant as defendant in a chance encounter of defendant in a department store was not the result of a suggestive identification procedure, thus, there was no constitutional infirmity in the identification process; (2) the female victim's out-of-court and in-court identifications were sufficiently reliable under the totality of the circumstances to be admissible at trial; (3) the publicity attending the case did not deprive defendant of an impartial jury and a fair trial; and (4) the cumulative effect of the evidence was sufficient to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was the perpetrator of the assaults in question.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for two counts of first degree assault.

 

406 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Aillon


Nos. 12612, 12613, 12614


Supreme Court of Connecticut


202 Conn. 385; 521 A.2d 555; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 769


January 9, 1987, Argued  
March 3, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment, in each case, charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the cases were consolidated and tried to the jury before Hadden, J.; verdicts and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of three counts of murder, contending that the trial court erred by denying admission of a transcript of an expert witness' testimony at a prior trial, by refusing to suppress evidence obtained during a Terry stop, and by refusing to dismiss the indictments due to grand jury bias.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the stabbing murders of his estranged wife and her parents. The court affirmed defendant's conviction because (1) defendant failed to prove that an expert witness was unavailable so that a transcript of the witness' testimony at a prior trial could be admitted, (2) evidence obtained during a police vehicular stop in the course of investigating an unrelated burglary in the neighborhood was lawfully obtained, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion by refusing to suppress the evidence, and (3) there was no State constitutional right to voir dire prospective grand jurors notwithstanding the grand jury foreman's acquaintance with one of the murder victims and his family.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's decision to convict defendant of murder.

 

407 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mullings


No. 12914


Supreme Court of Connecticut


202 Conn. 1; 519 A.2d 58; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 727


October 10, 1986, Argued  
January 6, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Norcott, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134. Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly denied his motion to exclude the victim's testimony as to the incident under Conn. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 755 based the destruction of a tape recording of his statements to the police.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with robbing a store. Shortly after the robbery, the store clerk gave a full account of the incident to the police. The clerk later gave a statement to the police again recounting the incident. The second statement was tape recorded and the tape was transcribed. The tape recording was erased pursuant to a routine police procedure and the transcript was lost prior to trial. The clerk identified defendant as the perpetrator both in court and when he viewed a photo array. On appeal, the court held that defendant was not entitled to have the clerk's testimony excluded under § 755. The court reasoned that although the State was culpable for the unavailability of the tape and transcript, defendant had suffered little if any prejudice from the loss of the tape recorded statement. The court found that defendant knew before trial that the tape and transcript were unavailable, used the State's inability to produce them in an effort to impeach the clerk's testimony, which was consistent with his other statements, and the jury observed the clerk's in court identification of defendant as well as a partial videotape of the incident.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for robbery in the first degree.

 

408 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Scognamiglio


No. 12221


Supreme Court of Connecticut


202 Conn. 18; 519 A.2d 607; 1987 Conn. LEXIS 728


October 10, 1986, Argued  
January 6, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictments charging the defendant with the crimes of murder and felony murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before J. Healey, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of felony murder, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut), which convicted him of felony murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of felony murder. He appealed and argued that the trial court unconstitutionally expanded the offense charged when it instructed the jury that it could convict him of felony murder if it found that he or another participant in the robbery caused the death of the victim in the course of and in furtherance of the robbery or of flight therefrom. The court found nothing in the record to indicate that defendant would have altered his defense if that theory of liability had been included in the indictment. Defendant also argued that the trial court erred by instructing the jury that it could find him guilty of felony murder if it found that he or another participant caused the death of the victim in the course of or in furtherance of the robbery or of flight therefrom. The court found that it was error for the trial court to charge in the disjunctive, but held that, given the number of correct explanations of the disputed element of felony murder, the correct explanation at the beginning and end of the initial charge and the recharge, and defendant's failure to take exception, the jury was adequately instructed on the elements of felony murder.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in defendant's conviction for felony murder.

 

409 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Helicopter Associates, Inc. v. Stamford


No. 12650


Supreme Court of Connecticut


201 Conn. 700; 519 A.2d 49; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 1015; 61 A.L.R.4th 789


October 3, 1986, Argued  
December 30, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to declare a certain city ordinance unconstitutional, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, and referred to Hon. William L. Tierney, Jr., state trial referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment for the defendant, from which the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation filed an action in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut) to declare a certain city ordinance unconstitutional. The court rendered judgment for the city, finding that the state had not preempted the field and that a valid nonconforming use did not exist on the effective date of the regulation. The corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The corporation and the owner of the tract of land at issue orally agreed that the corporation could use the owner's site for the landing and taking off of helicopters. The zoning board of the city subsequently amended its zoning regulations to delete from the land use schedule as a permitted use the category of "aeroplane field, hangar or ramp." The parties agreed that the regulation included helicopter facilities. The zoning regulations contained a provision which stated that any use of land legally existing at the time of an amendment to the regulations was deemed to be a nonconforming use, and that such use might be continued but might not be extended or expanded. The corporation argued that state statutes governing aeronautics preempted that area of law. The trial court found that the state had not preempted the field and that a valid nonconforming use did not exist on the effective date of the regulation. The court disagreed, and found error in part and remanded the case for further proceedings to evaluate the legality of the corporation's nonconforming use under the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court found error in the trial court's finding that the corporation did not possess a nonconforming use under the city's zoning regulations. The court set aside the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case for further proceedings to determine the validity of the ordinance.

 

410 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. McIver


No. 12590


Supreme Court of Connecticut


201 Conn. 559; 518 A.2d 1368; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 1019


October 3, 1986, Argued  
December 16, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the third degree, kidnapping in the first degree and sexual assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Reynolds, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of larceny in the sixth degree, kidnapping in the first degree and sexual assault in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Superior Court, District of New Haven (Connecticut) for larceny in the sixth degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-125b, kidnapping in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-92(a)(2)(A), and sexual assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant sexually assaulted, kidnapped, and robbed the victim, who was a prostitute, after he agreed to help her find drugs and to give her money in exchange for performing fellatio. He was charged in a substitute information with robbery in the third degree, kidnapping in the first degree, and sexual assault in the first degree. He was convicted. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions. His motion to dismiss based on his alleged illegal warrantless arrest was properly denied because any possible error resulting from the admission of his statements during interrogation was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. Defendant was not deprived of a fair trial because the trial court refused to strike testimony regarding blood and semen stains on the victim's coat, which was not retained. The police did not act in bad faith and the stains did not constitute exculpatory evidence. The state's failure to grant immunity to a defense witness did not deprive him of his right to a fair trial. He was not entitled to have testimony regarding a phone call to his sister stricken because it did not prejudice him. The court declined to address his ineffective assistance of counsel claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

 

411 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Stratford v. Local 134, IFPTE


No. 12779


Supreme Court of Connecticut


201 Conn. 577; 519 A.2d 1; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 1021; 125 L.R.R.M. 2052


October 8, 1986, Argued  
December 16, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application to vacate an arbitration award granting disability benefits to a town employee, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, wherein the named defendant filed an application to confirm the award; the matter was tried to the court, Gerety, J., which rendered judgment denying the application to vacate and granting the application to confirm, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff town appealed from the decision of the Superior Court in Fairfield (Connecticut), which denied the town's application to vacate an arbitration award and granted defendant union's application to confirm the award.


OVERVIEW: The town filed an application to vacate an arbitration award granting disability benefits to a town employee. The union filed an application to confirm the award. The superior court denied the application to vacate and granted the application to confirm. The town appealed from the judgment, attacking on constitutional and public policy grounds the validity of a provision in its collective bargaining agreement, under which the town must provide all members of the bargaining unit with hypertension or heart disease benefits mandated for municipal fire or police personnel. The court held that the challenged bargaining agreement provision and the contested award did not violate public policy or any provision of the state constitution. The court found that the issue submitted to the arbitration panel was whether the town violated the labor contract in refusing to pay benefits. The arbitrators found that the town violated the contract and ordered it to make remedial payments. The court held that the award conformed to the submission. Also, the "special compensation" represented by the hypertension and heart disease benefits was within the realm of acceptable bargaining subjects.


OUTCOME: The court held that there was no error in the superior court's decision to deny the town's application to vacate an arbitration award and granted the union's application to confirm the award.

 

412 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Burak


No. 12351


Supreme Court of Connecticut


201 Conn. 517; 518 A.2d 639; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 1010


October 1, 1986, Argued  
December 9, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crimes of murder and kidnapping in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before O'Donnell, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of murder and kidnapping in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-54 (a), 53a-92 (a) (2) (A).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in restricting his cross-examination of the state's witness concerning the witness' psychiatric records and any possible plea bargains the witness may have entered into with the state, thereby violating defendant's state and federal constitutional rights of confrontation, and admitting prejudicial evidence concerning defendant's flight prior to his arrest and his escape subsequent to his arrest. The court found no error, holding that (1) the trial court was correct in finding Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-146f (4) inapplicable to this case and that the witness' psychiatric records were privileged; (2) although the trial court did err in excluding the question concerning the witness' counsel's communications with the state, the ruling, when examined in the context of the cross-examination of the witness, did not rise to the level of interference with the constitutional right to confrontation; and (3) the details of defendant's escape were admissible to show defendant's consciousness of guilt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder and kidnapping in the first degree.

State v. Simms


No. 12663


Supreme Court of Connecticut


201 Conn. 395; 518 A.2d 35; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 985


October 1, 1986, Argued  
November 25, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of felony murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Corrigan, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which, after a trial by jury, convicted him of felony murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant robbed and killed the night watchman at a cathedral. He was arrested and made several statements to police. He was convicted of felony murder, and he appealed. The court affirmed and held that (1) the constitutional right to a disinterested grand jury did not create a right to voir dire prospective grand jurors before their impaneling; (2) because the relevant information was a matter of public record that defendant could have pursued without the assistance of the State, the State could not be said to have "suppressed" evidence of the witness's psychiatric history; (3) absent some evidence of continued mental impairment at times relevant to this incident or this trial, a trial court might reasonably have decided that the witness's prior psychiatric history was too remote to be admissible, even for impeachment purposes; (4) defendant did not demonstrate that he invoked his right to counsel during his police interrogations; (5) the record failed to support defendant's claim that, by reason of his intellectual impairment, his waivers of his constitutional rights were ineffectual; and (6) defendant's waivers were knowing, intelligent and voluntary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of felony murder.

 

414 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Golino


No. 12639


Supreme Court of Connecticut


201 Conn. 435; 518 A.2d 57; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 987


October 2, 1986, Argued  
November 25, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Kinney, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss; thereafter, the matter was reserved by the court for the advice of this court on the question of whether prosecution of the defendant on the murder charge was barred by the statute of limitations.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a murder case, defendant sought dismissal of the information against him on the ground that the prosecution was barred by the five-year statute of limitations in effect in 1973, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-193. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) reserved the matter for the advice of the court.


OVERVIEW: Section 54-193 prescribed a five-year limitations period for crimes punishable by imprisonment in the state prison, but no limitation period for crimes "punishable by death." Connecticut's death penalty had been adjudged unconstitutional, but it had never been struck from the books. The State argued that because the murder statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54 prescribed a possible death sentence, a violation of § 53a-54(a)(1) was an offense "punishable by death" for purposes of the statute of limitations. Defendant argued that because he could not constitutionally have been sentenced to death in the year the crime was committed, he was not charged with an offense "punishable by death" for purposes of § 54-193. The court agreed with the State, holding that the phrase "punishable by death" was a shorthand used by the legislature to refer to crimes that were so heinous that no limitations period would be appropriate. The court reasoned that the classification of crimes for statute of limitation purposes arose from the relative gravity of the offenses rather than any inextricable tie to the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the statute of limitations did not bar the prosecution.

 

415 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Veal


No. 12588


Supreme Court of Connecticut


201 Conn. 368; 517 A.2d 615; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 998


September 30, 1986, Argued  
November 18, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of murder and amended information charging the defendant with the crime of assault in the second degree with a firearm, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, and presented to the court, Barry, J., on a plea of nolo contendere on the assault charge; the murder charge was tried to the jury before Barry, J., and a verdict of guilty was returned; thereafter, the court rendered judgment of guilty of each crime, and the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) that convicted defendant of murder, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a. Defendant entered a plea of nolo contendere to a charge of assault in the second degree with a firearm, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-60a(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and the court affirmed. The court found that the trial court did not err when it prevented defendant from introducing evidence concerning the murder victim's prior acts of violence and her general reputation for violence. The trial court properly sustained the State's objection to the evidence of the victim's past conduct because of the absence of a claim of self-defense. Although the trial court acceded to defendant's request to charge on manslaughter in the first degree as a lesser included offense in the jury instructions, the trial court properly made no reference to the defense of extreme emotional disturbance. The court also found that the evidence of threats made by defendant was relevant to issues of intent and motive. Thus, the trial court reasonably concluded that the probative value of the testimony outweighed its prejudicial tendency. Defendant's constitutional claims were also unpersuasive, because hearsay claims did not automatically invoke constitutional rights to confrontation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder.

 

416 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Nevers v. Anderson


No. 12607


Supreme Court of Connecticut


201 Conn. 377; 517 A.2d 620; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 999


October 8, 1986, Argued  
November 18, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment to declare a city ordinance invalid, for injunctive relief to enjoin payments made thereunder to the New Britain city aldermen and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain and tried to the court, Maloney, J.; judgment for the plaintiffs, from which the defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city, city aldermen, and city treasurer, appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain (Connecticut), which granted plaintiff taxpayers an injunction against the city paying expense accounts to the city aldermen and ordered the city and treasurer to recover such sums paid to the aldermen.


OVERVIEW: The city's common council approved an ordinance providing for an unrestricted expense account of $ 125 for each position of alderman. They mayor approved the ordinance, and the taxpayers filed action for an injunction restraining the city and its municipal officers from paying the expense accounts. The trial court granted an injunction against the city paying the expense accounts to the city aldermen and ordered the city and treasurer to recover such sums paid to the aldermen. On appeal, the court found no error, holding that the trial court was correct in finding that the expense accounts were compensation and such compensation could not be awarded in the absence of an amendment to the city charter or a timely confirmatory referendum by the electorate of the city. The court found that the city charter fixed the compensation of the aldermen, and provided that no alderman could receive any compensation except as provided in the charter.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

 

417 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ryerson


No. 12698


Supreme Court of Connecticut


201 Conn. 333; 514 A.2d 337; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 960


June 11, 1986, Argued  
September 2, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crime of robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Hadden, J., verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(4).


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred in its instructions to the jury and in denying his motion to dismiss because his warrantless, predawn arrest at his apartment was unconstitutional. The court found no error. Decisional law provided that if the fairness of a subsequent prosecution was not impaired by an illegal arrest, neither the federal nor the Connecticut constitution required dismissal of the charges or a voiding of the resulting conviction. Defendant conceded that the police obtained no evidence as a direct consequence of his arrest. Therefore, the motion to dismiss was properly denied, irrespective of the constitutionality of the arrest. Defendant's arguments against applying decisional law were unavailing. As a rule, judicial decisions applied retroactively. The trial court's refusals to charge on reasonable doubt and on the unreliability of eyewitness identification did not constitute error. Viewing the charges as a whole, the substance of defendant's requested charges was adequately conveyed to the jury. The trial court's charge on alibi witnesses was fair comment to the jury, and the "Chip Smith" charge was valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

Engel v. Bourbeau


No. 12703


Supreme Court of Connecticut


201 Conn. 162; 513 A.2d 688; 513 A.2d 689; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 929


May 8, 1986, Argued  
August 19, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the court, Gerety, J.; judgment denying the petition, from which the petitioner appealed.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner detainee appealed an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which denied his application for a writ of habeas corpus for his release from the custody of respondent state trooper. The trooper arrested detainee pursuant to a rendition warrant to extradite him to Georgia, the demanding state, for his alleged failure to pay for agricultural products in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 5-9914.


OVERVIEW: The detainee was the owner of a distributor of bakery ingredients. A shipment of pecans from a pecan company in Georgia was sent to a warehouse for the distributor's account. The detainee was indicted for failure to pay for agricultural products in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 5-9914 and arrested pursuant to a rendition warrant. The trial court denied the detainee's petition for a writ of habeas corpus. On appeal, the detainee argued that his constitutional right to due process was violated by the trial court's failure to consider the constitutionality of the Georgia statute. The court found no error, holding that the trial court properly declined to review the constitutionality of the offense for which he was arrested. The court found that the detainee was substantially charged as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-159 because the indictment, the requisition warrant, and a clerk's certification charged the detainee with committing acts in another state that resulted in the commission of a crime in Georgia. The court found that although some of the extradition papers stated that the detainee was a fugitive, the documents were sufficiently clear that he was a non-fugitive.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's denial of the detainee's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

Moore v. McNamara


No. 12732


Supreme Court of Connecticut


201 Conn. 16; 513 A.2d 660; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 920


May 6, 1986, Argued  
August 12, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to establish the paternity of the plaintiff's minor child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, where the court, Jackaway, J., denied the defendant's motion for summary judgment; thereafter, the case was tried to the court, Reilly, J., which rendered judgment finding the defendant to be the father of the minor child and ordering certain financial awards, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant father sought review of an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which entered judgment finding the father to be the father of plaintiff mother's minor child and ordered the father to pay child support.


OVERVIEW: The mother initiated a paternity suit against the father pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-160, and sought a determination that the father was the father of the minor child and sought child support. The trial court permitted the introduction of a blood grouping and human leukocyte antigen (HLA) test to establish paternity, found that the father was the father of the child, and ordered the father to pay child support. The father sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held: (1) the paternity statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-160, was no longer the sole basis for a paternity action, thus, the three-year statute of limitations period was not substantive or jurisdictional, but was rather procedural or personal and was properly applied retrospectively; (2) it was not error for the trial court to allow the introduction of the HLA test because the HLA test was not a blood grouping test within the meaning of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-168; and (3) the use of blood grouping tests and HLA testing attained general acceptance in the scientific community as a means of testing for paternity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that entered judgment finding the father to be the father of the minor child and ordered the father to pay child support to plaintiff mother.

State v. Edwards


No. 12436


Supreme Court of Connecticut


201 Conn. 125; 513 A.2d 669; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 928


April 1, 1986, Argued  
August 12, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of larceny in the fourth degree, robbery in the second degree, and forgery in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Corrigan, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of the lesser included offense of larceny in the fifth degree, accessory to robbery in the second degree, and forgery in the second degree, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of larceny in the fifth degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-125a, accessory to robbery in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-135(a)(1), and forgery in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-139.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, among other things, argued that the State failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that he was guilty of being an accessory to robbery in the second degree. Defendant specifically argued that as the driver of the getaway car, he was not actually present when the robbery took place and thus could not be found guilty of robbery in the second degree. On appeal, the court held that was not guilty of robbery in the second degree because robbery in the second degree under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-135(a)(1) required that the principal who committed the robbery be aided by another person actually present. Defendant, as the driver of the getaway car, was not actually present during the robbery. While the evidence was insufficient to sustain the conviction on accessory to robbery in the second degree, it did suffice to sustain a conviction for the lesser-included offense of accessory to robbery in the third degree under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-136 (a).


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case for modification of the judgment so as to convict defendant of the lesser-included offense of accessory to robbery in the third degree, rather than robbery of the second-degree, and for resentencing.

State v. Cavallo


No. 12632


Supreme Court of Connecticut


200 Conn. 664; 513 A.2d 646; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 900


June 5, 1986, Argued  
August 5, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of tampering with a witness, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, geographical area number four, and tried to the jury before Gray, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which found the defendant guilty of the crime of tampering with a witness in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-151.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-151 was void for vagueness; that the State produced insufficient evidence at trial to support his conviction; and that the sentence imposed by the trial court was excessive. The court held that the language of § 53a-151 plainly warned perpetrators that the statute applied to any conduct that was intended to prompt a witness to testify falsely or to refrain from testifying in an official proceeding. The court found that § 53a-151 did give defendant fair warning that his course of conduct was illegal. Furthermore, the court held that § 53a-151 was not unconstitutionally vague because it applied only to conduct intentionally undertaken to undermine the veracity of the testimony given by a witness. The court concluded that a review of the record revealed that the State presented substantial evidence to satisfy its burden. The court did not review defendant's claim the his sentence was excessive because defendant had not followed the proper procedure for seeking reduction of his sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of the crime of tampering with a witness.

 

422 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Whelan


No. 12647


Supreme Court of Connecticut


200 Conn. 743; 513 A.2d 86; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 907


June 10, 1986, Argued  
August 5, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before McKeever, J., verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted him of the crime of murder. Among the trial court's errors, defendant contended that the trial court improperly instructed the jury about the inferences that could be drawn from circumstantial evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant objected to the court's instruction that indicated that jurors could draw inferences from circumstantial evidence if the inference asked to be drawn was not only logical and reasonable but was strong enough that jurors could find that it was more probable than not that the fact to be inferred was true. Defendant argued that such a charge unconstitutionally diluted the state's burden of proving the essential elements of the crime beyond a reasonable doubt. The court agreed. The court determined that the primary issues before the jury were whether defendant intended to cause the victim's death and whether the killing was justified by self-defense. The state argued zealously that defendant intended to kill the victim, asserted that the number and severity of the stab wounds were indicative of intent, and refuted defendant's self-defense claim. The court instructed the jury that the only way to determine intent was to infer it. Having been told that an inference may be drawn when it was more probable than not that the fact inferred was true, the jury was permitted to draw the inference of intent based on the erroneous probability standard.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the trial court's judgment of conviction and remanded the matter for a new trial.

Daily v. New Britain Machine Co.


No. 12661


Supreme Court of Connecticut


200 Conn. 562; 512 A.2d 893; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 893; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P11,191


December 12, 1985, Argued  
July 22, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained by the named plaintiff allegedly caused by a defective machine leased and then purchased from the defendant, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the court, James T. Healey, J., granted the defendant's motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff machinist sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut), which granted summary judgment to defendant machine company in plaintiff's products liability action.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff machinist filed a products liability action against defendant machine company. The trial court rendered summary judgment to defendant, and the court found no error in that judgment. The court held that the claims in the substitute complaint did not raise a genuine issue of fact because defendant had parted with possession and control of the molding machine more than 10 years before the complaint was filed, and such claims were time-barred by Conn. App. P. § 380. The court held that defendant was entitled to judgment as a matter of law. The court found that plaintiff by choice limited the complaint to statutory claims and that common law claims could not be read into the complaint. The court found that plaintiff's request to amend was untimely. The court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-577a was constitutional and that the classification was reasonable, not arbitrary, and rested upon a difference having a fair and substantial relation to the object of the legislation.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's decision to grant summary judgment to defendant machine company in plaintiff machinist's products liability action. The court held that the applicable statute of limitation barred plaintiff's action.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information, in each case, charging the defendant with the crimes of kidnapping in the first degree, larceny in the first degree, robbery in the second degree, conspiracy to commit kidnapping in the first degree, conspiracy to commit robbery in the second degree, and conspiracy to commit larceny in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number one, where the cases were consolidated and tried to the jury before Ford, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, in the first case, of kidnapping in the first degree, larceny in the third degree and larceny in the first degree, and verdict and judgment of guilty, in the second case, of kidnapping in the second degree, larceny in the third degree and larceny in the first degree, from which the defendants filed separate appeals to this court.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, who were jointly tried before a jury on various charges arising out of the abduction of a woman, challenged a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), which convicted both of larceny in the third degree, convicted the first defendant of kidnapping in the first degree, and convicted the second defendant of kidnapping in the second degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were jointly tried before a jury on various charges arising out of the abduction of an 18-year-old woman. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendants of larceny in the third degree, convicted the first defendant of kidnapping in the first degree, and convicted the second defendant of kidnapping in the second degree.

State v. Corchado


No. 12603


Supreme Court of Connecticut


200 Conn. 453; 512 A.2d 183; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 886


May 6, 1986, Argued  
July 15, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with the crime of manslaughter in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Curran, J., granted the defendant's motion to note nolle and or to dismiss, and the state, on the granting of permission, appealed.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed an order from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss a manslaughter charge against him after his previous conviction was reversed on appeal. Defendant had served the entire sentence imposed for his conviction, but the State sought to retry his case.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of manslaughter in the first degree. His conviction was reversed on appeal because of error in the jury instructions on the law of self-defense, and a new trial was granted. By the time the State was ready to retry defendant's case, he had been released from prison and discharged from his parole. The trial court granted defendant's motion to dismiss with prejudice. On appeal, the court found no error. The court concluded that the trial court did not abuse its discretion under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-56 in finding "cause" for dismissal after explicitly weighing all of the competing factors proffered by both sides. Even if defendant had been convicted on retrial, further incarceration was improbable, and the state had waited two years after the reversal to initiate the reprosecution of defendant. Defendant had not only served his sentence and been discharged from parole without incident, but he had no other criminal record and was 53 years old. While the trial court gave deference to the State's decision to reprosecute and considered the seriousness of the crime, the balancing process favored defendant in requiring a dismissal of the charge.


OUTCOME: The court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in granting defendant's motion to dismiss with prejudice.

Griffin Hospital v. Commission on Hospitals & Health Care


No. 12593


Supreme Court of Connecticut


200 Conn. 489; 512 A.2d 199; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 889


March 13, 1986, Argued  
July 15, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the defendant commission ordering the plaintiff to adopt a certain budget which the commission deemed acceptable for the fiscal year 1984, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford and referred to Hon. Thomas J. O'Sullivan, state trial referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment sustaining the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed and the defendant cross appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff hospital appealed a judgment from a state trial referee who, pursuant to a referral from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Ansonia-Milford (Connecticut), upheld with some modifications a budget order by defendant, the Commission on Hospitals and Health Care. The Commission also cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Commission ordered a number of reductions in the hospital's budget. The court on appeal held that some of the determinations made by the referee were erroneous and remanded. The court rejected the hospital's claim that the budget order conflicted with Medicare law and was preempted. The court also sustained decisions made by the referee concerning nonvolume expense reductions and compliance adjustments for two fiscal years. However, the referee erred in approving another compliance adjustment because it constituted an improper regulation of philanthropic funds by the Commission under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19a-153(c). The court held that the referee erred in deciding that a reduction in budget base and certain repair and maintenance expense reductions were improper because the hospital had adequate notice of those issues. The referee's decisions regarding a salary adjustment, long range planning expense, disallowing certain conditions imposed by the Commission, and the modification of a stay order were not erroneous. The court agreed that the referee erred in concluding that the Commission could not regulate the use of unexpended capital authorizations from prior years.

University of Connecticut Chapter AAUP v. Governor


No. 12384


Supreme Court of Connecticut


200 Conn. 386; 512 A.2d 152; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 875


March 5, 1986, Argued  
July 8, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the named defendant from reducing the budgetary allotments to the University of Connecticut and other state universities, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Satter, J.; judgment for the defendants; thereafter, the court denied the plaintiffs' motion to open and set aside the judgment, and the plaintiffs appealed.

The appellants filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff unions appealed a judgment of the Superior Court, Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), in favor of defendants, governor and others, in the unions' action to enjoin the governor from reducing the budgetary allotments to state universities. The unions claimed that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-85(b), which permitted the governor to reduce budgetary allotments by up to five percent under certain specified circumstances, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The unions contended that § 4-85(b) had the effect of permitting the governor to veto part of an appropriation; conferred upon the governor legislative power in violation of the separation of powers provision contained in Conn. Const. art. II; and that, even if such power could have been delegated, § 4-85(b) did not satisfy the requirements for a valid delegation because it allowed the governor unrestrained discretion. Defendants asserted defenses of sovereign immunity and lack of standing. The court found that the case was not barred by sovereign immunity because it presented a significant and substantial question, the determination of which was manifestly in the public interest. The unions had standing to bring the action because they had a colorable claim of direct injury. Section 4-85(b) did not unconstitutionally confer veto power on the governor in circumvention of Conn. Const. art. IV, § 15, nor did it confer legislative power upon the governor in violation of Conn. Const. art. II. The standards specified in § 4-85(b) under which the governor may have exercised his power were as definite as was reasonably practicable.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the judgment of the superior court.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Superior Court of Middlesex (Connecticut) upon a conditional plea of nolo contendere to a substitute information that charged him with heroin-related offenses. Defendant claimed the trial court failed properly to ascertain whether his nolo contendere plea was knowingly, voluntarily, and intelligently made and erroneously denied his motion to suppress evidence.

State v. Mitchell


No. 12484


Supreme Court of Connecticut


200 Conn. 323; 512 A.2d 140; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 881


April 2, 1986, Argued  
July 1, 1986, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied Mitchell v. Warden, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1068 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 26, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of felony murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before McKeever, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted him of felony murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54c.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court should have dismissed the charge against him because the evidence presented at the preliminary hearing was insufficient to support a finding of probable cause. Defendant also contended that he was deprived of his constitutional rights to due process and to confront and cross-examine the witnesses against him. The court did not agree with the State's argument that a finding of probable cause at a preliminary hearing should not be reviewable following conviction at trial. It held that the adversarial probable cause hearing at issue was a critical stage in the prosecution, as well as a jurisdictional prerequisite to continuing prosecution. Absent appellate review of the probable cause determination, the court found that there would be no recourse whatsoever for even the most blatant violation of clear constitutional rights. The court held that there was sufficient evidence to support the trial court's finding of probable cause. The court also held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-46a(b) was constitutional and that defendant's constitutional rights were not impaired thereunder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

430 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Evans


No. 12545


Supreme Court of Connecticut


200 Conn. 350; 511 A.2d 1006; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 883


April 9, 1986, Argued  
July 1, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree and of being a persistent dangerous felony offender, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and tried to the jury before Purtill, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by information with robbery in the first degree and being a persistent dangerous felony offender. He was convicted in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut) and appealed. He claimed error in permitting testimony of a pretrial photo identification and in refusing to suppress the identification, and in denying his motion to dismiss the information as violative of his equal protection rights.


OVERVIEW: As the court found that the totality of the circumstances indicated that the identification testimony was reliable even though the identification procedure was unnecessarily suggestive, the superior court had not erred in permitting the testimony or in not suppressing the identification. As to denial of the motion, the essential difference between Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(4) and § 53a-135(a)(2) was the type of weapon used. The former was limited to firearms; the latter included firearms but was not limited to them. This difference indicated a clear legislative intent to impose a greater penal sanction where robbery was committed with the use of a firearm. Defendant alleged no rational basis for charging him with robbery in the first degree rather than with robbery in the second degree and maintained that such a charge constituted selective and discriminatory prosecution in violation of his equal protection rights. However, as the statutes had not prohibited exactly the same conduct, there was no reasonable basis for a finding that the equal protection clause, Conn. Const. art. I, § 20, had been violated. Thus, the denial of the motion to dismiss the information was correct.


OUTCOME: There was no error.

 

431 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. O'Neill


No. 11990


Supreme Court of Connecticut


200 Conn. 268; 511 A.2d 321; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 863


March 12, 1986, Argued  
June 24, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of arson in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Glass, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which convicted him, following a jury trial, of the crime of arson in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-111(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged after a former girlfriend and her family awoke to flames in the front of the house that the victim's son put out with a garden hose. Police and fire officials smelled gasoline, and a plastic container containing gasoline was found under defendant's truck, which was parked 100 yards away. Defendant was convicted and sentenced to a mandatory term, and he appealed. The court affirmed the conviction and remanded the case for resentencing. The trial court properly admitted evidence of prior bad acts in order to prove motive, and balanced the prejudicial effect with its probative value. There was no error in failing to instruct the jury as requested on lesser included offenses because the evidence that differentiated the lesser from the more serious offense was not sufficiently in dispute, and the prosecution had latitude as to how and in what manner it proceeded against defendant. The "Chip Smith" instruction given did not coerce or mislead the jury. The imposition of the mandatory sentence violated defendant's equal protection rights because it resulted in a more severe sentence being required for arson than was required for arson murder, a more serious offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction, set the judgment aside, and remanded the case only for resentencing.

 

432 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Petyan v. Ellis


No. 12644


Supreme Court of Connecticut


200 Conn. 243; 510 A.2d 1337; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 861; 1 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 665


January 15, 1986, Argued  
June 17, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for libel and intentional infliction of emotional distress, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and tried to the jury before Vasington, J.; directed verdict and judgment for the defendant, from which the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed after the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut) entered a directed verdict in favor of defendant employer in the employee's lawsuit to recover damages for libel and intentional infliction of emotional distress. The employee contended that the employer lied about the reason for her discharge in a form submitted in connection with the employee's application for unemployment benefits.


OVERVIEW: During the job interview, the employee told the employer that her typing skills were not top-notch. About three weeks after she was hired, the employer discharged the employee because she was dissatisfied with the employee's performance, particularly her typing skills. In a statement to the Employment Security Division, the employer stated that she fired the employee because of "unsatisfactory performance and mainly for fraud and lying." The trial court entered a directed verdict. The court held that the employer had an absolute privilege to state her reasons for discharging the employee in the "factfinding supplement" solicited by the Employment Security Division. That conclusion barred any recovery by the employee even if the court were to have concluded that publication of the statement was libelous per se or that a jury could have found malice. A claim for intentional infliction of emotional distress required proof of extreme and outrageous conduct. The employer's conduct could not be considered outrageous. Moreover, because the employer's comment was absolutely privileged, she would not have been liable for the intentional infliction of emotional distress in any event.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

433 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Gorra Realty, Inc. v. Jetmore


No. 12433


Supreme Court of Connecticut


200 Conn. 151; 510 A.2d 440; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 847


February 14, 1986, Argued  
June 10, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendants from posting as unsafe certain of the plaintiff's property, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the court, Santaniello, J., granted the plaintiff's motion for an ex parte temporary injunction; thereafter, the case was tried to the court, Schaller, J.; judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiff appealed.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff building owner brought an action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 against defendants, a city and its building official, alleging that the emergency posting of its property under § 125 of the Connecticut Building Code violated its rights to due process and equal protection, and sought an injunction and damages. The Superior Court in the judicial district of New London (Connecticut) rendered judgment for defendants, and the owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: A municipal building official invoked the code's emergency posting procedures after finding that portions of an historic building were in danger of collapse. The owner contended that the building was not unsafe and that it was entitled to a pre-posting hearing. The owner alleged that the building official had acted in an arbitrary and discriminatory way after it refused to permit inspections. The trial court found that the building as a whole was structurally sound but that staircases were pulling away from the wall and ceilings were in danger of falling. The trial court denied injunctive relief, finding that no constitutional rights were violated and that the official's actions were warranted. The court held that the trial court's factual findings were not clearly erroneous, that there was no constitutional entitlement to a hearing before summary administrative action in emergency situations, and that there was no violation of equal protection where the owner was afforded chances to repair the building and had not shown that other properties in similar condition were not posted.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's decision in favor of defendants.

 

434 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Bieluch v. Bieluch


No. 12605


Supreme Court of Connecticut


199 Conn. 550; 509 A.2d 8; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 805


March 6, 1986, Argued  
May 13, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for the dissolution of a marriage, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and referred to Hon. Irving Levine, state trial referee; judgment dissolving the marriage and granting certain other relief, from which the defendant appealed to this court, which affirmed the trial court's decision; thereafter, the case was transferred to the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where the plaintiff moved to have the defendant held in contempt; the court, Landau, J., granted the plaintiff's motion and the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of the judgment of the trial court (Connecticut), which held the father in civil contempt. A dissolution decree had been issued between appellee mother and the father, which awarded custody of the parties' minor children to the mother and ordered the father to pay the mother child support and alimony on a monthly basis. The mother applied for contempt after significant arrearages had accrued.


OVERVIEW: The father contended on appeal that the trial court was biased, should have heard the father's motion for modification, and improperly relied on ex parte information from the support enforcement unit and from the mother. The court found no evidence was presented by the father to substantiate his claims and affirmed the orders of the trial court. The court further refused to recognize the father's claims to various credits due to him because the father had testified that he had made direct payments to the mother and that the parties had agreed to forgive a portion of the arrearage. The court found that the father was in fact in arrears and had violated the orders of the trial court. The court further found that the trial court was not required to view the mother's failure to present contradictory testimony as a concession that the father's claims of offsetting items were valid. Throughout the proceeding, the mother persisted in her position that the father owed her the full amount of the arrearages and the court did not agree that the trial court's decision to not give credence to the father's statements was clearly erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court found that the trial court committed no error and affirmed the civil contempt finding against the father in the proceedings brought by the mother to obtain payment of arrearages from the father of child support and alimony.

 

435 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Vaughn


No. 11891


Supreme Court of Connecticut


199 Conn. 557; 508 A.2d 430; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 806


January 16, 1986, Argued  
May 13, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of robbery in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, and tried to the jury before Chernauskas, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of robbery in the third degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which denied his motions for a lineup and to suppress identification testimony, which convicted him of robbery in the third degree under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-136, and which sentenced him to five years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his accomplice accosted their victim, assaulted him, and stole money and personal property from his person. As a result, defendant was convicted of third-degree robbery under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-136 and sentenced to five years in prison. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the victim's identification of defendant from a photographic array was not unduly suggestive, because the photographs were in black and white, the persons in the photographs were all black males, as was defendant, and were wearing normal clothes. It was impossible to distinguish between the varying shades of skin color in the photographs, and defendant's skin color was not significantly different from the other individuals in the photographs. Thus, defendant did not prove that the photographic identification violated defendant's due process rights, and the trial court properly denied defendant's Conn. Gen. Prac. Book § 782 motion for a lineup as well as his motion to suppress the identification.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which denied defendant's motions for a lineup and to suppress identification testimony, and which convicted him of robbery in the third degree and sentenced him to five years' imprisonment.

 

436 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Husti v. Zuckerman Property Enterprises, Ltd.


No. 12689


Supreme Court of Connecticut


199 Conn. 575; 508 A.2d 735; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 809


February 14, 1986, Argued  
May 13, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to enjoin the defendants from using certain of their property for concerts and theatrical performances, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford, where the defendants filed a counterclaim, and tried to the court, Rottman, J.; judgment for the plaintiffs on the complaint and on the counterclaim, from which the defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landowners sought review after the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Ansonia-Milford (Connecticut) granted plaintiff zoning enforcement officer's request for injunctive and equitable relief and issued an injunction barring use of the landowners' property for outdoor concerts, in an action that arose under U.S. Const. amend. I, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-2 Conn., and Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 4 and 5.


OVERVIEW: The landowners owned a country club that was located in an area that had been zoned as an R-1 residential zone since 1955. In 1975, the landowners decided to book outdoor musical events at the club. The planning and zoning commission ordered the landowners to cease and desist. The zoning order was upheld. The court denied certification. Despite the order, the landowners continued to offer live entertainment. The trial court issued an injunction. The court found no error. The zoning plan did not regulate speech on the basis of its content. The regulations prohibited all outdoor entertainment in the residential zone that contained the club. The trial court reasonably concluded that performances at an outdoor amphitheater located in a residential area threatened the quality of life and the safety of the inhabitants of the neighborhood. In the absence of a demonstrated danger that the regulation would significantly impinge upon the First Amendment rights of those not before the court, the landowners had no standing to press a claim of overbreadth. The landowners lacked standing to demand relief under the state constitution because they had not exhausted their administrative remedies.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.
