Wilson v. Security Ins. Group


No. 12651


Supreme Court of Connecticut


199 Conn. 618; 509 A.2d 467; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 812


February 5, 1986, Argued  
May 13, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to compel the defendant to submit to arbitration a dispute arising under an uninsured motorist provision of an insurance policy issued to the plaintiff's employer, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the defendant filed a counterclaim which was dismissed, suo motu, by the court, Reynolds, J.; thereafter, the court, S. Freedman, J., granted the plaintiff's motion for an order directing the defendant to proceed with arbitration and rendered judgment in accordance with that order, and the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court, New Haven (Connecticut), granting plaintiff's motion for an order directing defendant to proceed with arbitration and dismissing defendant's counterclaim in an action arising under an uninsured motorist provision in an insurance policy issued to plaintiff's employer by defendant.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed an action to compel arbitration of his claim against defendant based upon an automobile insurance policy issued to plaintiff's employer. Plaintiff alleged that the policy provided uninsured motorist coverage for his benefit with respect to injuries he received while on duty as a police officer .Defendant contended that the policy language did not provide for arbitration of coverage issues with respect to fleet stacking and workers' compensation setoff. On appeal, the court determined that pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 38-175c (a)(1), the coverage issue must be determined by arbitration before review by a court. Additionally, the court did not construe Conn. Gen. Stat. § 38-175c(a)(1) as making a distinction between issues governed wholly by policy language and those, which may also require the application of statutes or regulations in order to resolve them.


OUTCOME: There was no error in judgment in dismissing defendant's counterclaim and absence consent or waiver, it would have been wholly inappropriate to entertain the issues raised by defendant's counterclaim absent an arbitrator's award.

 

438 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Seal Audio, Inc. v. Bozak, Inc.


No. 12579


Supreme Court of Connecticut


199 Conn. 496; 508 A.2d 415; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 789


January 8, 1986, Argued  
April 29, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover amounts allegedly due on a promissory note executed by the defendant, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the defendant filed a counterclaim, and referred to Frederick W. Krug, attorney state trial referee, who filed a report recommending judgment in favor of the plaintiff on the complaint and on the counterclaim; the court, Stoughton, J., rendered judgment accepting the referee's report and the defendant appealed.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant obligor sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut), which accepted the attorney referee's report and rendered judgment for plaintiff obligee in its action upon a note, on the ground that the appointment of attorneys as state trial referees pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-434 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The court concluded that the requirements for the nomination and appointment of judges did not apply to attorney referees because they were confined to the role of factfinders and they were not empowered to function as judges. The fact that the attorney referee went beyond the bare statutory requirement of reporting the facts found by including his opinion upon the legal issues did not transform his role into a judicial one. The trial court was the effective arbiter of the law, and the legal opinions of the attorney referee carried no weight not justified by their soundness as viewed by the trial court. The court determined that consent of the parties was necessary for a reference to an attorney referee, which removed the essential basis for the obligor's due process challenge to the constitutionality of § 52-434. The court found that the failure to obtain the parties' consent was not plain error in light of their failure to protest until the appeal was filed. The court determined that the obligor was precluded from appellate review of alleged errors in the attorney referee's report by its failure to file exceptions to the acceptance of the report by the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment finding no error in the reference of factfinding to an attorney referee.

State v. Franko


No. 12189


Supreme Court of Connecticut


199 Conn. 481; 508 A.2d 22; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 788


March 11, 1986, Argued  
April 22, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number one, and tried to the jury before Curran, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment entered by the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), which convicted him after a jury trial of sexual assault in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in excluding evidence of the victim's virginity prior to the alleged assault, which he argued was relevant to provide an alternative explanation for an injury she suffered during the act of sexual intercourse; in instructing the jury that it could convict him of sexual assault in the first degree if it found that he had compelled the victim by the threat of force; and in refusing his request to charge the jury that sexual assault in the second degree was a lesser-included offense of sexual assault in the first degree. Because defendant failed to establish that the testimony regarding the victim's virginity was relevant to a material issue in the case, he could not complain that his constitutional rights were violated when that testimony was excluded. The court held that defendant's failure to object, coupled with his subsequent failure to except to the disputed instruction, negated his claim of unfair surprise. Because the crime of sexual assault in the second degree was not a lesser-included offense of sexual assault in the first degree, the court held that the trial court did not err in refusing to give the requested instruction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

First Bank v. Simpson


No. 12600


Supreme Court of Connecticut


199 Conn. 368; 507 A.2d 997; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 778


February 4, 1986, Argued  
April 15, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover the balance due on a promissory note executed by the defendants, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Celotto, J., granted the plaintiff's motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, from which the defendants appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant mortgagors appealed the judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which granted plaintiff second mortgagee's motion for summary judgment on its suit to collect on a promissory note secured by a second mortgages on properties that had previously been foreclosed upon by the first mortgagee in an action in which the second mortgagee was joined as a defendant.


OVERVIEW: A first mortgagee sued the mortgagors to foreclose on five condominium units and named the second mortgagee on those units as a codefendant. After the first mortgagee obtained a judgment in its favor and after title to the units became absolute in the first mortgagee, the second mortgagee sued the mortgagors to collect on the note secured by the mortgage. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the second mortgagee. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the first mortgagee's foreclosure suit merely eliminated the second mortgagee's security interest in the mortgaged premises. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-1 barred only the foreclosing first mortgagee from taking any further action on the first mortgagee's note and did not affect the second mortgagee's rights on the underlying note. The second mortgagee's failure to seek a deficiency judgment pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-14 did not preclude the second mortgagee from filing a separate suit against the mortgagees to collect on the note.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in all respects.

State v. Collette


Nos. 11480, 11481


Supreme Court of Connecticut


199 Conn. 308; 507 A.2d 99; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 767


January 14, 1986, Argued  
April 1, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information, in each case, charging the defendant in each case with the crimes of burglary in the third degree and larceny in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number one, and tried to the jury before Ford, J.; verdicts and judgments of guilty, from which the defendants separately appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), which convicted defendants of committing burglary in the third degree pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-103, and larceny in the second degree pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-123.


OVERVIEW: Defendants challenged their convictions, alleging that the trial court erred in denying their motions to suppress the in-court and out-of-court identifications made by the victim. On appeal, the court held that the confrontation was not unnecessarily suggestive because the victim was able to positively identify two of the three men the police apprehended based upon the victim's fairly accurate description. Moreover, the victim had had a reasonable opportunity to view defendants as they left her home. Defendants also alleged that the trial court erred in not dismissing the larceny charge because the State failed to prove that the value of the stolen items exceeded the statutory limit. The court found that the State's expert properly appraised the stolen property at market value, rather than replacement value as contended by defendants. Thus, the State established the elements of larceny. The court rejected defendants' claim that the judge improperly commented on facts in evidence, finding that the judge was merely explaining to the jury their role in weighing the reliability of the victim's identification. The court found that the sentences were not based on false information.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions for committing burglary in the third degree and larceny in the second degree.

State v. Boucino


No. 12068


Supreme Court of Connecticut


199 Conn. 207; 506 A.2d 125; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 752


December 4, 1985, Argued  
March 18, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree and larceny in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Hadden, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty on both counts, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134 (a)(4) and larceny in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-122 (a)(2). He was sentenced to 15 to 40 years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and an accomplice robbed a bank. On appeal of the convictions, the court affirmed. The court held the trial court correctly excluded proffered alibi testimony on the basis that defendant failed to comply with Conn. Gen. Prac. § 762-767, which required him to respond to the State's demand for notice of undisclosed alibi witnesses. The court stated the statutory provisions were properly enforced and did not violate defendant's right to a compulsory process and to present a defense. The court also ruled in-court and out-of-court identifications by a bank teller and a bank patron were reliable. The court stated both witnesses were in a position to focus on detail and exhibited a high degree of certainty. The court ruled the crimes of larceny and robbery required proof of different and distinct elements; therefore he was not subjected to jeopardy for the same offense. The court rejected a contention the trial court erred by not ordering the trial court reporter to record final arguments. The court stated Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-61 did not obligate the reporter to record the arguments. The court stated the defense assented by failing to request recordation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of robbery in the first degree and larceny in the first degree, and sentenced defendant to 15 to 40 years imprisonment.

La Croix v. Board of Education


No. 12544


Supreme Court of Connecticut


199 Conn. 70; 505 A.2d 1233; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 740


January 15, 1986, Argued  
March 11, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for the wrongful termination of the plaintiff's employment, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and referred to Hon. Irving Levine, state trial referee; judgment awarding some damages to the plaintiff but denying his request for reinstatement and additional damages, from which the plaintiff appealed to the Appellate Court, Testo, Hull and Borden, Js.; judgment for the plaintiff ordering his reinstatement and a new trial for determination of additional damages; on the granting of certification, appeal by the defendant to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff teacher brought an action for wrongful termination against defendant board. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut) entered judgment, awarding some damages to the teacher but denying his request for reinstatement and additional damages. On review, the appellate court directed the teacher's reinstatement and a new trial on damages. The board sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The board attempted to terminate the teacher twice. The first attempt was ineffective because the board failed to comply with the procedural requirements prescribed by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-151(b). At issue was the effect of a subsequent letter indicating termination. The trial court found that the letter effectively reinitiated the statutory termination procedure and had resulted in a valid termination when the teacher failed to request a hearing. The appellate court reversed in part, holding that the initial procedurally defective termination rendered ineffective the subsequent attempt to terminate the contract. As such, the appellate court held that the teacher's failure to exhaust his administrative remedies with respect to the letter did not preclude him from seeking judicial relief. On further review, the court held the letter effectively reinitiated the termination process and the teacher deliberately chose to not avail himself of the statutory means of redress. Further, the teacher's challenge did not fall within one of the narrow exceptions to the exhaustion doctrine: his due process attack did not present a colorable constitutional claim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court and remanded the matter with direction to reinstate the judgment of the trial court in its entirety.

State v. Williams


No. 9864


Supreme Court of Connecticut


199 Conn. 30; 505 A.2d 699; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 737


December 10, 1985, Argued  
March 4, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of burglary in the third degree and larceny in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury and tried to the jury before Moraghan, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of burglary in the third degree and larceny in the second degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of burglary in the third degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-103 and of larceny in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-123 (Rev. to 1981), but denied defendant's request for the appointment of counsel during the sentencing phase.


OVERVIEW: Police arrested defendant for breaking into a clothing store and stealing clothing from the racks. Defendant represented himself at trial. The State put in evidence that the value of the stolen clothing was over $ 2,000 in support of the charge of larceny in the first degree. Defendant was convicted of burglary in the third degree and of larceny in the second degree, which required a showing of a theft of items worth more than $ 500. Defendant requested, but was denied, counsel to represent him during the sentencing phase. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions, but remanded for resentencing. The court held that the trial court's jury instruction on specific intent, while deficient in isolation because it stated the jury "must find the intent would infer from conduct" for a finding or guilt on burglary, was not error because the trial court also instructed the jury that if it found that defendant had unlawfully entered or remained in the building, but did not possess the intent to commit a crime therein, defendant could not be found guilty of burglary. However, the court remanded because defendant asked for, but did not receive, counsel during the sentencing phase.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction, but remanded for resentencing where the trial court denied defendant's request for court-appointed counsel during the sentencing phase, even though defendant had represented himself during the trial.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his guilty verdict and judgment for robbery in the first degree rendered in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Danbury (Connecticut).


OVERVIEW: Defendant accosted a 13-year-old girl going to school by holding a knife to her throat and threatening to cut her throat if she did not surrender her pocketbook. A jury found defendant guilty of robbery in the first degree. Defendant was sentenced to seven years' imprisonment. On appeal, defendant claimed that the trial court erred in refusing to suppress an out-of-court photographic identification and a subsequent in-court identification. The court found no error.

No. 10822


Supreme Court of Connecticut


198 Conn. 560; 504 A.2d 1029; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 714


November 15, 1985, Argued  
February 11, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Henebry, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a despite his claim that he did not form the necessary specific intent due to intoxication as defined in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-7.


OVERVIEW: After drinking with another, defendant entered a bar, twice kicked away a man's crutch while it was propped next to the man's seat, exchanged some words, and shot and killed the man. During his trial on murder charges, defendant claimed that he did not form the necessary specific intent because he was intoxicated and that the gun discharged when he slipped or was pushed, but several witnesses testified that he exhibited no noticeable signs of intoxication, did not slip, and was not pushed. The trial court gave an instruction on specific intent that was erroneous, but the jury charge also contained numerous statements that clarified or correctly stated the test for specific intent. Defendant was convicted of murder. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the charge was adequate, despite the error, because defendant did not object to the charge and because the charge as a whole negated any potential for misinterpretation of intoxication under § 53a-7.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which had convicted defendant of murder despite defendant's claim that his alleged intoxication negated a finding of specific intent.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut), which entered judgment on the jury's verdict that found defendant guilty of manslaughter in the first degree with a firearm, in violation of Conn. The court ruled that the trial court did not err in refusing to instruct that the exceptions of provocation, aggression, and combat by agreement had to be considered from the perspective of the defendant.

448 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brown


No. 11470


Supreme Court of Connecticut


198 Conn. 348; 503 A.2d 566; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 692


November 12, 1985, Argued  
January 21, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of larceny in the first degree, forgery in the second degree, criminal impersonation and falsely reporting the theft of a motor vehicle, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Flanagan, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of larceny in the first degree and falsely reporting the theft of a motor vehicle, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) for larceny in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-119(2) and 53a-122(a)(2), and of falsely reporting the theft of a motor vehicle in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-198.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for larceny and for falsely reporting the theft of a motor vehicle. The record showed that defendant's vehicle was found stripped and abandoned in a parking lot. Defendant filed a claim with his insurer and received the fair value of the car. Later, while a police officer was investigating an unrelated matter at defendant's home, the officer discovered that defendant was not home and walked behind the apartment and looked for defendant through the window of a two-car garage rented by defendant. The officer discovered a number of the missing car parts in that garage. The court affirmed the conviction and concluded that the evidence was sufficient to support the jury's verdict. The court found not error in the denial of defendant's motion to suppress the evidence found in the garage since defendant failed to sustain his burden of establishing that he had a legitimate privacy interest in the garage. Defendant presented no evidence showing that his use of the garage was exclusive or that he exercised sole control over it. There was no evidence to establish that defendant could reasonably have expected that objects placed in the garage would remain private.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment of conviction against defendant for larceny in the first degree and for falsely reporting the theft of a motor vehicle. The court held there was no error in the superior court's decision denying defendant's motion to dismiss certain evidence.

State v. Wright


No. 11545


Supreme Court of Connecticut


198 Conn. 273; 502 A.2d 911; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 687


November 6, 1985, Argued  
January 14, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two-part indictment charging the defendant with the crimes of manslaughter in the first degree and of being a persistent dangerous felony offender, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where each charge was tried separately to the jury before Glass, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of each crime, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which in separate jury trials convicted defendant of manslaughter in the first degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-55(a)(1), and of being a persistent dangerous felony offender, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40(a)(1) (1981) .


OVERVIEW: Defendant and the victim struggled; the victim was stabbed twice in the chest and died. Defendant alleged that he had acted in self-defense and that the knife belonged to the victim. Defendant ran from the scene, changed his clothes, and was arrested the next day. Defendant filed a motion in limine to prohibit the State from impeaching him with his prior convictions for manslaughter and assault. The superior court denied the motion and convicted defendant. Defendant appealed. The court reversed. Although the prior convictions were potentially admissible under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-145 (1981), the prejudicial effect of the convictions outweighed any probative value as to credibility and should have been excluded because violent crime convictions had no bearing on honesty and veracity. The superior court's instruction that limited the use of the prior conviction was insufficient to overcome the prejudice. The jury was properly instructed that it was permissible to consider defendant's self-interest in weighing his testimony and the evidence of his flight. Defendant failed to prove that it was unconstitutional to convict him as a habitual offender based on one prior conviction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the superior court, which convicted defendant, and remanded for a new trial.

State v. Amarillo


No. 11903


Supreme Court of Connecticut


198 Conn. 285; 503 A.2d 146; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 688


November 5, 1985, Argued  
January 14, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree, sexual assault in the first degree and kidnapping in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number one, and tried to the jury before Ford, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of robbery in the third degree, sexual assault in the first degree and kidnapping in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), which convicted him of sexual assault in the first degree, kidnapping in the first degree, and robbery in the third degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that his motion for judgment of acquittal should have been granted because there was insufficient evidence to prove that he was the perpetrator of the crimes charged. The court found no error in the trial court's denial of the motion. The evidence was sufficient to support the jury's conclusion that defendant was the victim's assailant. The court further found that the evidence, viewed in a light most favorable to sustaining the verdict, could have reasonably allowed the jury to find that sexual penetration had occurred. Finally, the court found that there was no error in the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress identification evidence. Under the totality of the circumstances, the victim's identification was sufficiently reliable to warrant its admission into evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Kolich v. Shugrue


Nos. 12205, 12206


Supreme Court of Connecticut


198 Conn. 322; 502 A.2d 918; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 690


November 8, 1985, Argued  
January 14, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action, in the first case, to recover damages for the wrongful death of the plaintiff's decedent, and action, in the second case, for damages for personal injuries sustained as a result of a collision with an allegedly defective guardrail, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the cases were consolidated and tried to the jury before Hon. Milton H. Belinkie, state trial referee; verdict and judgment for the defendant in each case, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, victim and administrator, sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court, Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which, by jury verdict, rendered that appellee State was not negligent in a consolidated wrongful death and personal injury action.


OVERVIEW: The two victims were traveling on the highway when their car was struck by a van. The vehicle swerved off the highway and crashed into the median divider. One victim was injured and the other victim died. There was evidence that the guardrail which their car struck was improperly secured and may have contributed to their injuries. The victim and the administrator filed separate actions against the State alleging that the State negligently constructed and maintained its highways. The actions were consolidated. The victim and administrator alleged that a defect in the state highway was the sole proximate cause of their injuries and death. The trial court held, by jury verdict, that the State was not negligent. The victim and the administrator failed to file a motion to set aside the verdict. The court held that it was not plain error for the trial court to provide its instruction to the jury on proximate cause. The court noted that the trial court's instruction on causation was in accordance with the rule that the parties filing an action against the State must prove that the defective highway was the sole proximate cause of their injuries.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which, by jury verdict, rendered that the State was not negligent in a wrongful death and personal injury action.

State v. Findlay


No. 11158


Supreme Court of Connecticut


198 Conn. 328; 502 A.2d 921; 1986 Conn. LEXIS 691


November 8, 1985, Argued  
January 14, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of robbery in the first degree by aiding, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield and tried to the jury before Stoughton, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Litchfield (Connecticut), which entered judgment on a jury verdict that found defendant guilty of robbery in the first degree by aiding in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-134(a)(4) and 53a-8.


OVERVIEW: At approximately 10:10 a.m., a farmer saw a heavyset woman with an "unnatural Shirley Temple hairdo" and a mole on her face in a cream-colored car with dealer vanity plate along the side of a country road. At approximately 10:15 a.m., two men robbed a local bank and escaped in a rust-colored Ford. At approximately 10:20 a.m. a witness saw two men get out of a rust-colored car and walk toward the cream-colored car. The farmer later identified defendant as the woman in the cream-colored car while driving with police in a nearby parking lot and from a single photograph, although both viewings were unplanned and did not reveal that defendant had a mole. At trial, the farmer identified defendant as the woman in court. The jury convicted defendant of robbery in the first degree by aiding in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-134(a)(4) and 53a-8. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the in-court identification was proper because the prior viewings were unplanned and did not disclose the mole. The court also held that the evidence was sufficient, and that the trial court's admission of certain evidence and jury instruction on reasonable doubt were proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which convicted defendant of robbery in the first degree by aiding after admitting an in-court identification and overruling defendant's challenges to the admission of certain evidence and the jury instruction on reasonable doubt.

State v. Preyer


No. 11790


Supreme Court of Connecticut


198 Conn. 190; 502 A.2d 858; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 978


November 14, 1985, Argued

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of kidnapping in the first degree, of sexual assault in the first degree and of assault in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number one, and tried to the jury before Nigro, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of kidnapping in the second degree, of sexual assault in the first degree and of assault in the third degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut), which sentenced him to eight years imprisonment upon his conviction, after a jury trial, of sexual assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a), of kidnapping in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-94, and of assault in the third degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-61.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who lived with the victim, beat her and caused her to use pliers on her genitalia, causing injuries. He was arrested and blood and pliers was found in his car. During the trial, he offered two alternative defenses, a lack of the requisite intent on his part, and consent on the part of the victim. On appeal, he contended that the trial court erred in instructing the jury that the affirmative defense of cohabitation had no bearing as a defense to the charge of sexual assault in the first degree, and in restricting defendant's cross-examination of the victim regarding her prior sexual activities with him. The court held although defendant failed to request a charge, that the sexual assault conviction was reversible because the case fell squarely within the parameters of the plain error doctrine of Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. App. P. § 3063. The trial court's mistaken charge failed to assist the jury in applying the law correctly to the facts which they might find established. Further, the court found defendant had failed to establish that the trial court deprived him of his constitutional right of confrontation since his counsel terminated the inquiry.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court in part, finding error only in the conviction for sexual assault in the first degree. That portion of the case was remanded for a new trial.

State v. Zach


No. 12197


Supreme Court of Connecticut


198 Conn. 168; 502 A.2d 896; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 974


November 8, 1985, Argued  
December 24, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Infractions complaints issued against the defendants for their failure to display a Connecticut registration decal on certain boats in their possession, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, geographical area number nine, and reserved by the court, Edelberg, J., for the advice of this court.



DISPOSITION: Remanded for trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State brought an action in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex (Connecticut) against defendants, 37 recreational boaters, for their alleged failure to comply with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 15-142. The boaters challenged the constitutionality of § 15-142. The cases were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: The recreational boaters received infractions complaints during the summer of 1982 for their alleged failure to comply with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 15-142, which provided for the registration of vessels operating in state waters. The court remanded the action for trial and held that courts were bound never to anticipate a question of constitutional law in advance of the necessity of deciding it and never to formulate a rule of constitutional law broader than was required by the precise facts to which it was to be applied. The court held that it would not review the facial validity of § 15-142, and the only question which remains was whether that statute had been constitutionally applied. The court held that that determination was dependent to an unusual degree on the facts and circumstances of the individual case. The facts of record in the present matter, however, were insufficient to afford a basis for resolution of the issues presented. It was only where the parties fully and fairly disclosed all of the relevant information that it could perform the careful inquiry and thorough examination required in constitutional determinations.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the cases for trial on the issue of constitutionality of the statute.

State v. Perez


No. 11315


Supreme Court of Connecticut


198 Conn. 68; 502 A.2d 368; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 964


November 5, 1985, Argued  
December 17, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree, kidnapping in the second degree, possession of a sawed-off shotgun, forgery in the second degree and criminal impersonation, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and presented to the court, Kline, J., on a plea of guilty to the forgery and impersonation counts; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury which returned a guilty verdict on the remaining three counts; after granting the defendant's motion for acquittal on the kidnapping count, the court rendered judgment otherwise in accordance with the jury verdict and the defendant's guilty plea; the defendant appealed to this court from his conviction of robbery in the first degree and possession of a sawed-off shotgun.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from his conviction, after a jury trial, before the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut) of robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(4) and possession of a sawed-off shotgun in violation of § 53a-211(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the admissibility of an in-court identification. The trial court held that the in-court identification was admissible because it was independent of two earlier identifications and resulted instead from the victim's recollection of the crime itself. The court agreed with the trial court. The victim was taken to defendant's housing complex and identified defendant and his accomplice. Later, defendant was taken to the victim's store where the victim identified defendant. The court held that the initial identification at the housing project was not suggestive because defendant stood among a group of people who resembled him in racial makeup when the victim identified him. The court held that the subsequent show-up at the victim's store did not make the identification suggestive. Furthermore, defendant failed to demonstrate the unreliability of the victim's identification. The court held that any uncertainty the victim might have exhibited at the initial identification went to the weight to be given the in-court identification.


OUTCOME: The court found no error and affirmed defendant's conviction.

State v. Madera


No. 12377


Supreme Court of Connecticut


198 Conn. 92; 503 A.2d 136; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 966


October 2, 1985, Argued  
December 17, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with fourteen counts of the crime of arson murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and presented to the court, Glass, J., on a plea of nolo contendere; judgment of guilty on all counts, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After accepting defendant's conditional plea of nolo contendere to 14 counts of arson murder pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-94a, the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut) entered a judgment of guilty on all 14 counts. Pursuant to the plea, defendant appealed the trial court's denial of his motions to suppress his confession and to dismiss the indictment on constitutional grounds.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's § 54-94a plea agreement permitted him to challenge on appeal the voluntariness of his confession and also the denial of his motion to dismiss the indictment, which was based upon the constitutionality of the arson murder statute and the requisite level of scienter needed to sustain a conviction. The court reversed the convictions and remanded the case with instructions to vacate defendant's conditional plea. The court held that a plea induced by a trial court-approved promise that could not be fulfilled was not voluntary. The court found that the issues that were reserved for appeal in the conditional plea agreement did not fall within the ambit of § 54-94a. Defendant's motion to suppress, which implicated U.S. Const. amends. V and VI, was not included in the statutory language of § 54-94a, which allowed appeals only from the denial of a motion to suppress evidence obtained from an illegal search or seizure in violation of U.S. Const. amend. IV. Regarding defendant's motion to dismiss on constitutional grounds, the court found that defendant's reasons were essentially based on speculation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's judgment of conviction on 14 counts of arson murder, which was entered by the trial court after it accepted defendant's conditional plea of nolo contendere on all 14 counts. The case was remanded with instructions to vacate defendant's conditional plea and for further proceedings.

State v. Harman


No. 10818


Supreme Court of Connecticut


198 Conn. 124; 502 A.2d 381; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 968


October 8, 1985, Argued  
December 17, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of attempt to commit murder and of assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the jury before Spada, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of attempt to commit murder, from which the defendant appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut) that, following the jury trial, convicted him of attempt to commit murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from the conviction for the attempted murder of his wife, citing the lack of appointed counsel during an 11-week period. The court found no error in the superior court judgment, holding that defendant's right to assistance of counsel, as guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. VI and Conn. Const. art. I, § 8, was not violated by the superior court's failure to appoint counsel, in view of the circumstances. The 11-week period occurred after defendant rejected 3 public defenders, brought a federal action in order to replace one of them, and refused to accept other suggested counsel. Defendant's case also was transferred in order to provide him with another pool of available defense attorneys. Finally, defendant accepted the representation of an attorney who practiced in another jurisdiction and the case, again, was transferred. Defendant's conduct justified the delay and he was not harmed by the hiatus. The court then ruled that defendant waived objection to the jury instruction on the insanity defense by failing to raise the matter at trial. Further, the court rejected defendant's claim that testimony by the court-appointed psychiatrist improperly was admitted.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the superior court judgment.

State v. Fernandez


No. 10771


Supreme Court of Connecticut


198 Conn. 1; 501 A.2d 1195; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 959


October 4, 1985, Argued  
December 10, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of burglary in the third degree and larceny in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two, and tried to the jury before Landau, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty on both counts, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut) convicting him of burglary in the third degree, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-103, and larceny in the second degree, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-123.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that the trial judge conducted a cross-examination of the only defense witness that served to deprive defendant of his constitutional right to a fair trial. The witness was defendant's brother who had pled guilty to the same offenses before the same judge. The judge questioned the brother based on statements he made at his plea hearing at a point when the prosecutor was attempting to impeach his credibility. The judge also questioned the brother about an alleged unidentified participant. The court concluded that the judge's examination could have easily given the jury an impression that he doubted the brother's truthfulness. The examination cast a cloud of judicial skepticism over the brother's testimony and undercut defendant's case. The court therefore held that the denial of defendant's right to a fair trial resulted in prejudice requiring a new trial and reversed the convictions. A curative instruction given by the judge was not in this instance sufficient to cure the impact of the prejudice caused by the judge's questioning. The court also held that the evidence of guilt was sufficient. Therefore it ordered a new trial instead of granting an acquittal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions and ordered a new trial.

State v. Aversa


No. 11539


Supreme Court of Connecticut


197 Conn. 685; 501 A.2d 370; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 951


October 10, 1985, Argued  
December 3, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of attempted robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Melville, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court in the District of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted him of attempted robbery in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pulled a gun from his pocket in an empty liquor store, causing the store owner to flee the premises. Approximately 100 yards from the site, defendant and his companion were pulled over in their vehicle after an officer noticed that they matched the description given by the store owner. After being read Miranda rights, the suspects admitted they were standing in front of the liquor store. At the station, defendant admitted he had been in the liquor store. Defendant was convicted of attempted robbery in the first degree. The court affirmed. The initial stop of the car was legal. The police saw the blue sweatshirt in defendant's car that matched the description given by the store owner. The police acted lawfully in briefly holding defendant until the store owner positively identified him. The extension of the initial stop was justified once the police found the blue sweatshirt. The identification made by the victim was reliable under the totality of the circumstances; therefore the in-court identification of defendant was admissible. Defendant knowingly and voluntarily waived his right to remain silent after he was given Miranda warnings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which convicted defendant of attempted robbery in the first degree.

The court also rejected defendant's claim that the trial court erred in excluding from evidence certain newspaper clippings that were offered to show the bias of defendant's father, the State's chief witness. PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information, in the first case, charging the defendant with the crime of escape from custody, and indictment, in the second case, charging the defendant with the crime of kidnapping in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the cases were consolidated and tried to the jury before Hull, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty in each case, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of escape from custody in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-171, and kidnapping in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-92(a)(2)(B) after defendant fled from a courtroom for proceedings relating to a pending felony charge.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was in custody of the trial court for proceedings relating to a pending felony charge. Shortly after defendant's arrival in court, he suddenly ran from the defense table, through the back door of the courtroom, and out of the courthouse. With sheriffs in pursuit, defendant fled to a nearby street where he encountered a woman emerging from her car. Defendant forced her back into the car and drove off with her, threatening to kill her if she did not cooperate. Defednant was later arrested and was convicted of escape from custody and of kidnapping in the first degree. Defendant appealed and claimed that the underlying felony was already complete when the alleged kidnapping began, that defendant lacked the intent necessary for a kidnapping charge, and therefore the kidnapping charge was improper. The court affirmed and held that, where escape from custody was the underlying felony, defendant's intent to continue to elude the pursuit of custodial officers satisfied the intent requirement of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-92. The court held that defendant need not have abducted his victim at the very instant he left custody.


OUTCOME: THe court affiremd defendant's convictions of escape from custody and kidnapping in the first degree.

 

462 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Connecticut Asso. of Bds. of Education, Inc. v. Shedd


Nos. 12455, 12473


Supreme Court of Connecticut


197 Conn. 554; 499 A.2d 797; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 894


May 9, 1985, Argued  
October 22, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for declaratory relief challenging the constitutionality of a public act which provides for mandatory and final binding arbitration to resolve teacher contract disputes, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Kremski, J.; judgment for the defendants finding the act to be constitutional, from which the named plaintiff et al. and the plaintiff West Hartford Board of Education separately appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error; remanded with direction to dismiss.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, municipalities, local boards of education, and a state association of education boards, appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which ruled in favor of defendants, the State Commissioner of Education and others. The court found an act constitutional which provided for mandatory and final binding arbitration to resolve teacher contract disputes.


OVERVIEW: The municipalities, the boards, and the association had sought declaratory relief, challenging the constitutionality of 1979 Conn. Acts 79-405, amended Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-153f, which mandated arbitration of disagreements arising from collective bargaining between local or regional boards of education and school administrators and teachers. The trial court ruled in favor of the Commissioner, finding that the statute was constitutional. On appeal, the court set aside the judgment based on lack of standing. The municipalities failed to exhaust their administrative remedies pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 4-175, 4-176 on their related nonconstitutional issues and, thus, lacked standing to pursue declaratory relief on their constitutional challenge as well. The boards, like the municipalities, had no standing to challenge legislation enacted by their creator, the state, though they could question the interpretation of an enactment. Local charter powers yielded to the superior power of the state regarding a field of statewide concern. The association could have no standing greater than its members that it represented, the boards, who also lacked standing to challenge the legislation.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the trial court's judgment and remanded with directions to dismiss the action.

State v. Ellis


Nos. 12323, 12336


Supreme Court of Connecticut


197 Conn. 436; 497 A.2d 974; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 891

September 10, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictments charging each of the defendants with the crime of capital felony, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Borden, J., granted the defendants' motions to dismiss in the first two cases and denied the defendant's motion to dismiss in the third case; thereafter, the state, on the granting of permission, appealed to this court in the first two cases, and the third case was reserved by the court, Brennan, J., for the advice of this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed an order of the Superior Court, Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut) granting defendants' motions to dismiss indictments charging them with the crime of capital felony.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were initially charged with murder, felony-murder, and kidnapping in the first degree. The charges were subsequently dismissed because they were beyond the statute of limitations. Thereafter, indictments charging each of the defendants with the crime of capital felony were brought. The court granted defendants' motions to dismiss in the first two cases and denied defendant's motion to dismiss in the third case. The State, on the granting of permission, appealed in the first two cases, and the court reserved the third case. The court found error and held that the limitations period for capital crimes in effect at the time of crimes did not bar the prosecution. Also, the previously dismissed prosecution against two of the defendants was not res judicata precluding prosecution on the capital felony charges.


OUTCOME: The court found error because the limitations period for the capital charges in effect at the time of the crime did not bar the prosecutions; and, the previously dismissed prosecutions against two of the three defendants for other charges were not res judicata precluding the capital felony charges.

State v. Sutton


No. 11753


Supreme Court of Connecticut


197 Conn. 485; 498 A.2d 65; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 892


June 5, 1985, Argued  
September 10, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree, kidnapping in the second degree and threatening, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Mulvey, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty on all counts, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which convicted him of sexual assault in the first degree, kidnapping in the second degree, and threatening.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the imposition of a more severe sentence following his reconviction after his successful attack on his first conviction deprived him of his liberty without due process of law. The court remanded for resentencing. The court did not accept the State's assertion that because the earlier sentence was void at defendant's request, the trial court had unrestricted ability to sentence defendant to any lawful sentence. The court found that the sentence imposed on reconviction was illegal in the sense that it did not comport with statutory authority. The court determined that the record of the remarks of the trial judge in sentencing defendant did not affirmatively disclose any legitimate reasons for the increased sentence. Despite a careful examination of the trial court's remarks at the resentencing, the court could not find that the record demonstrated that the increased sentences were based on objective information concerning identifiable conduct occurring subsequent to the original sentencing.


OUTCOME: The convictions of sexual assault in the first degree, kidnapping in the second degree, and threatening were affirmed. The court found error in the sentencing and remanded for resentencing.

State v. Lopez


No. 12274


Supreme Court of Connecticut


197 Conn. 337; 497 A.2d 390; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 885


May 1, 1985, Argued  
September 3, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and presented to the court, J. Healey, J., on a plea of guilty; judgment of guilty, after the court denied the defendant's motion to withdraw his plea, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which convicted him of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty and the trial court concluded that the plea was voluntary. Prior to sentencing, defendant retained new counsel and sought to withdraw his plea. Defendant contended that the plea was involuntary, entered without knowledge of the charge, and that it resulted from ineffective assistance of counsel. The trial court denied the motion to withdraw and sentenced defendant to 25 years imprisonment. The court held that: (1) original defense counsel was not ineffective because based on defendant's signed and voluntary confession, it was unlikely that he could have successfully claimed a lack of intent for the purposes of reducing his conviction to manslaughter; (2) the trial court properly examined the strength of the State's case in order to determine whether defense counsel had acted competently in advising him to plead guilty; and (3) pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. App. P. § 711(1), the trial court's explanations to defendant regarding the offense, the affirmative defense of extreme emotional disturbance, and the State's burden of proof were entirely adequate to ensure that defendant understood the nature of the charge to which his plea was offered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

466 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kimbro


No. 12139


Supreme Court of Connecticut


197 Conn. 219; 496 A.2d 498; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 875


May 9, 1985, Argued  
August 20, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of possession of cocaine, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number six, where the court, Drutman, J., granted the defendant's motion to suppress and his motion to dismiss, and the state, on the granting of permission, appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the order of the Superior Court (Connecticut), which granted defendant's motions to suppress evidence and to dismiss his trial for possession of cocaine, claiming in each that his rights were violated under both the United States and the Connecticut constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested based upon an informant's tip that he was selling drugs. The police located defendant at the place the informant said he would be and conducted a warrantless search, which located drugs. In his motion to suppress, he sought the suppression of items seized from his person as having been taken without a warrant or without probable cause or pursuant to an unlawful arrest. The trial court found that there were no circumstances corroborating the informant, except the fact that defendant was at this particular corner when the police arrived there, which the trial court did not consider paramount because defendant had been seen there a half dozen times recently; moreover, defendant worked in that area. The court found that the trial court's decision was correct under either the Gates totality-of-the-circumstances analysis or the Aguilar-Spinelli test. Using the Aguilar-Spinelli test and rejecting the Gates totality-of-the-circumstances test, the court went on to find that the search was improper under the Connecticut Constitution as well.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because probable cause was lacking for the seizure of the drugs from defendant.

 

467 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fair


No. 11457


Supreme Court of Connecticut


197 Conn. 106; 496 A.2d 461; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 854


June 7, 1985, Argued  
August 6, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of murder, and information charging the defendant with the crime of robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Stodolink, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of each crime, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted him of murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a(a) and robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant lived with the victim and their son. The victim threatened to move away and keep defendant from ever seeing his son again. Defendant then went to the victim's place of work and shot her in the head. She died several days later. Defendant claimed he was suffering from an extreme emotional disturbance at the time of the shooting caused by his fear that he would never see his son again. On appeal, defendant argued that he was unconstitutionally forced to submit to psychiatric examination, and that the State improperly allowed the court-appointed psychiatrist to read a confidential presentence report. Finding no error, the court held that by informing the trial court of his intention to employ the extreme emotional disturbance defense and presenting evidence in support thereof, defendant placed his mental status in issue and the trial court properly directed him to submit to psychiatric examination. The fact that defendant's evidence was not from an expert did not matter. The court found that the psychiatrist's reading of the presentence report was not reversible error because defendant failed to show that it was harmful.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in defendant's conviction.

 

468 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Reddick


No. 11181


Supreme Court of Connecticut


197 Conn. 115; 496 A.2d 466; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 855


May 3, 1985, Argued  
August 6, 1985, decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree, assault of a victim sixty or older in the third degree and assault in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Zoarski, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of robbery in the first degree and assault of a victim sixty or older in the third degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) convicting him of robbery in the first degree, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(4), and assault of a victim 60 or older in the third degree, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-61a(a).


OVERVIEW: There were four witnesses to the robbery. Two of the witnesses made pretrial and in-court identifications of defendant. Defendant alleged that he was denied due process of law because the State failed to disclose, prior to trial, that the other two witnesses failed to identify defendant. In affirming defendant's convictions, the court held that there was no constitutional or Brady violation because the nonidentification information was disclosed when those two witnesses testified at trial. Further, defendant made no showing that the disclosure was so late as to prevent him from receiving a fair trial. The trial court did not violate defendant's Fifth or Fourteenth Amendment rights by allowing a witness to invoke his privilege against self-incrimination during his testimony. Defendant failed to preserve the issue by making timely trial objections and the record did not support a claim of constitutional error. In addition, the trial court did not err by denying defendant's motion for a mistrial after a witness testified that defendant had been incarcerated before trial. The testimony was actually exculpatory because it cast doubt on the key issue of identification.


OUTCOME: Defendant's robbery and assault convictions were affirmed.

State v. Alexander


No. 10342


Supreme Court of Connecticut


197 Conn. 180; 496 A.2d 486; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 860


June 12, 1985, Argued  
August 6, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Windham, and tried to the jury before Dannehy, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Windham (Connecticut), which convicted him upon a jury verdict of murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a.


OVERVIEW: A mutual friend of defendant and of the victim informed the police of a conversation in which defendant acknowledged that he killed the victim. Thereafter, the police provided the friend with transportation to the correctional center, where defendant was being held on charges of arson, to continue his conversations with defendant. Ultimately, defendant told the friend where the victim's body was buried, and defendant was arrested for murder. On appeal, defendant claimed that the trial court erred in refusing to suppress the friend's testimony concerning defendant's incriminating statement. The court found no error. The court held that the trial court did not err in concluding that the incriminating statements were made by defendant to a private citizen and not to a police agent or informer. The court found that police involvement was not so extensive as to create an agency relationship between the friend and the police. Balanced against the factors that tended to show police involvement, was the fact that the police neither initiated contact with the friend nor directed his activities. The court also rejected defendant's challenge to the validity of the grand jury indictment.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the judgment that convicted defendant of murder.

State v. Thompson


No. 12107


Supreme Court of Connecticut


197 Conn. 67; 495 A.2d 1054; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 849


April 11, 1985, Argued  
July 30, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of cocaine in count one, possession of cocaine with intent to sell in count two, and possession and transportation of one ounce or more of cocaine with intent to sell in count three, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Hale, J.; verdict of guilty on all counts; thereafter, the court granted the defendant's motion to set aside the verdict as to count one but denied the motion as to counts two and three, and rendered judgment thereon; from that judgment, the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the trial court (Connecticut), which convicted him of possession of cocaine with intent to sell and of possession and transportation of one ounce or more of cocaine with intent to sell. The trial court sentenced defendant to confinement for a period of three years the possession conviction and five years on the transportation with intent to sell conviction, which were to be served concurrently.


OVERVIEW: Following a jury trial, defendant was found guilty of possession of cocaine, possession of cocaine with intent to sell, and possession and transportation of one ounce or more of cocaine with intent to sell. The trial court granted defendant's motion to set aside the verdict on count one but denied the motion as to the second and third counts. Upon review, the court affirmed. The court found defendant's convictions were not barred by double jeopardy where five days elapsed between the two sales and there was no temporal continuity or clear connection between the sales. The court held it could not be said that each transfer was part of a single instance of criminal conduct. The court concluded that defendant failed to show that the sentencing procedure used by the trial court was constitutionally deficient where he received a full sentencing hearing, was allowed to introduce relevant evidence on his mental capacity, and he was allowed the opportunity to examine witnesses. The court determined that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19-480a(a) gave defendant sufficient notice that it was his burden to present evidence on the impairment of his mental capacity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that convicted defendant of possession of cocaine with intent to sell and of possession and transportation of one ounce or more of cocaine with intent to sell. The court also affirmed defendant's sentences.

 

471 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dupree


No. 12222


Supreme Court of Connecticut


196 Conn. 655; 495 A.2d 691; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 831


April 4, 1985, Argued  
July 16, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of arson murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Berdon, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty on both counts, sentencing the defendant to life imprisonment, suspended after twenty-five years, from which the state, on the granting of permission, appealed and the defendant cross appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which refused to sentence defendant in accordance with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54d and suspended defendant's term of life imprisonment for arson murder after 25 years. Defendant challenged the trial court's judgment, alleging that the trial court erred in declaring § 53a-54d constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Section 53a-54d provided that the trial court was required to impose a mandatory life sentence without eligibility for parole upon any person convicted of arson murder. The State argued that the trial court erred in suspending defendant's sentence. On appeal, the court held that the legislature's revision of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-35a rendered the phrase "shall not be eligible for parole" meaningless because the arson murder statute was placed into a definite sentencing scheme. The court found that the trial court did impose a life sentence. However, there was nothing in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54d prohibiting the trial court from suspending defendant's sentence. Also, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-28(b)(5), a term of life imprisonment suspended after a period was permissible. Moreover, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-25, arson murder was an unclassified felony for which there was no provision prohibiting the suspension of a sentence. The court rejected defendant's challenge to the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54d, finding that it did not create an irrebutable presumption of intent to cause death in violation of defendant's due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment suspending defendant's sentence of life imprisonment. The court affirmed defendant's conviction for arson murder.

State v. Braxton


No. 10475


Supreme Court of Connecticut


196 Conn. 685; 495 A.2d 273; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 834


June 5, 1985, Argued  
July 16, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Hadden, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which, upon a jury verdict, convicted him of robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(4).


OVERVIEW: Three black men robbed a convenience store; one man had a rifle. Defendant was apprehended due to his location, physical appearance, and demeanor and was detained in the police officer's squad car. Defendant subsequently acknowledged that he was the owner vehicle used in the robbery. Defendant was arrested. A search revealed that defendant had on his person the same type of money stolen in the robbery and the keys to the robbery vehicle. Defendant was convicted of robbery and his constitutional claim was dismissed. On review, the court affirmed. The court held that defendant's detention in the officer's patrol car was pursuant to a valid Terry stop. Regarding the sufficiency of the evidence, the court held that the jury could properly have found the defendant guilty of having committed the crime of robbery or of having been an accomplice. Defendant was discovered near the scene of the crime within minutes of its commission. From his appearance, including the fact that he was perspiring profusely and breathing heavily, it was inferable that he had been running. His car had been parked at the scene of the robbery and was used as the attempted getaway car.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in defendant's conviction of robbery in the first degree.

 

473 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Carofano v. Bridgeport


Nos. 9574, 9575, 9578


Supreme Court of Connecticut


196 Conn. 623; 495 A.2d 1011; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 822; 123 L.R.R.M. 2408


April 9, 1985, Argued  
July 9, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action, in each case, to enjoin the defendants from enforcing the defendant city's mandatory residency requirement for city employees, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the court, Jacobson, J.; judgment for the defendants in each case, from which the named plaintiffs et al. appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff police officers sought review of a decision from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut) which denied their request to enjoin defendant city from enforcement of a mandatory residency requirement for city employees that was included in a collective bargaining agreement by way of a binding arbitration award.


OVERVIEW: The police officers asserted that a statutory requirement that city employees maintain a residence within the city as a condition of employment with the city was improper. The lower court found in favor of the city. The police officers challenged the decision, contending that the statute's mandatory arbitration provision represented an invalid delegation of legislative power and that the residency requirement was unconstitutional. The court rejected the police officers' contentions, finding that delegation of power to a panel of arbitrators satisfied constitutional requirements concerning the delegation of legislative authority because the statute provided direction to the arbitrators concerning the exercise of the delegated authority and because the statute provided for judicial review of arbitration decisions. The court ruled that the residency requirement did not deprive the police officers of the equal protection of the laws because the requirement was a reasonable exercise of discretion that was closely tailored to governmental interests and because those interests outweighed the liberty interests of the police officers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court that found in favor of the city. The court held that the regulation requiring residency within the city as a condition of employment was not unconstitutional because no fundamental constitutional right was implicated by the requirement.
