Hartford v. Faith Center, Inc.


No. 12505


Supreme Court of Connecticut


196 Conn. 487; 493 A.2d 883; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 783


April 3, 1985, Argued  
June 18, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover unpaid personal property taxes, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, N. O'Neill, J., granted the plaintiff's motions for summary judgment and rendered judgment for the plaintiff, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owner appealed an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which rendered judgment in favor of plaintiff city in its action to collect property taxes owed by the owner on its property for six years.


OVERVIEW: The city instituted an action pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-161 in six counts against the owner for the collection of property taxes owed on the tax lists of 1976 through 1980. The owner filed a special defense and alleged the unconstitutionality of the tax assessments. The owner filed a counterclaim against the city and sought equitable relief from the allegedly illegal tax. The trial court entered a judgment in favor of the city, and the owner appealed and claimed that the trial court erred in granting the city's motion to strike the special defense and in ordering summary judgment in favor of the city. The court affirmed and held that, in collection actions pursuant to General Statutes § 12-161, the validity of the tax could not be questioned. The court held that the claim of unlawful assessment raised in the special defense could not properly be raised in an action to collect taxes under § 12-161 because the claim could have been redressed through an appeal from the board of assessors under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-111 or an application to the court under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-119 within the specified time limitations, and the owner did not do so.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the city.

 

475 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Manson


No. 11810


Supreme Court of Connecticut


196 Conn. 309; 493 A.2d 846; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 772


February 7, 1985, Argued  
May 28, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus alleging illegal confinement, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, M. Hennessey, J., granted the petition in part, crediting the petitioner with time spent in a Florida jail awaiting extradition, and appeal by the respondent to this court.

The appellee filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment vacated with direction to dismiss the writ.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed an amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, alleging that respondent commissioner of correction was confining him illegally. The commissioner appealed after the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) granted the petition in part. The trial court, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-98, credited petitioner with time spent in a Florida jail awaiting extradition.


OVERVIEW: The issue presented was whether petitioner was entitled to credit under § 18-98 for 109 days spent in a Florida jail while resisting extradition to Connecticut. The court found that the trial court erred in concluding that § 18-98 authorized credit for 109 days on petitioner's Connecticut criminal sentence. Section 18-98, as written, clearly specified that credit was authorized for someone imprisoned while "awaiting trial" or "awaiting sentencing." The statute did not specify that credit was authorized for someone "awaiting extradition." Because the statutory language was clearly expressed, the court found that it had to apply the legislative enactment according to the plain terms and could not read into the statute something that was not there. Given the plain command of § 18-98 that no credit could be given to someone in petitioner's circumstances, and the absence of any legitimate basis suggesting any vindictiveness for petitioner's choice to fight extradition, the court concluded that the commissioner's decision to deny the credit did not contravene petitioners' rights to equal protection or due process of the law under either the federal or state constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that there was error, therefore, the judgment was vacated and the case was remanded with direction to dismiss petitioner's writ of habeas corpus.

Sanders v. Officers Club of Conn.


No. 10575


Supreme Court of Connecticut


196 Conn. 341; 493 A.2d 184; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 773


January 8, 1985, Argued  
May 28, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action, pursuant to the Connecticut Dram Shop Act, to recover damages for personal injuries alleged to have been caused by the intoxication of a person to whom the defendants served alcoholic liquor while intoxicated, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex at Middletown and tried to the jury before Higgins, J.; verdict for the plaintiffs and, after the action by the named plaintiff was withdrawn, judgment for the plaintiff Charles L. Dickinson in the amount of $ 20,000, from which judgment the plaintiff Charles L. Dickinson appealed and the named defendant cross appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant club sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Middlesex at Middletown (Connecticut) in favor of plaintiff injured parties in plaintiffs' action to recover under the Dram Shop Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 30-102. The injured parties sought review of the trial court order that reduced the amount of the judgment.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs were injured when a car driven by one of the club's patrons collided with plaintiffs' cars, which were parked on the side of the road. The gravamen of the club's evidentiary argument was that there was no evidence sufficient to warrant the jury's finding that the driver was intoxicated at the time the club sold him alcoholic liquor. The evidence showed that the driver had two drinks at lunch on the day of the accident and later in the afternoon was served four drinks by the club. The court concluded that the jury reasonably could have found facts to prove that a state of intoxication existed in the driver at the time of a sale of alcoholic liquor to him by the club and that the state of intoxication continued was a proximate cause of the collision. In addition, the trial court properly struck the club's contributory negligence defense because contributory negligence was not a valid defense to a Dram Shop Act suit. Finally, the trial court properly reduced the amount of the award to the injured parties because the maximum amount recoverable under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 30-102 was $ 20,000.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's judgment in favor of the injured parties, or in the reduction of the judgment against the club.

 

477 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Palmer


Nos. 12245, 12509


Supreme Court of Connecticut


196 Conn. 157; 491 A.2d 1075; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 763


February 6, 1985, Argued  
May 7, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information, in the first case, charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree and theft of a firearm, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield at Bridgeport and tried to the jury before McGrath, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty from which the defendant appealed to this court.

Information, in the second case, charging the defendant with the crimes of burglary in the first degree and of carrying a pistol without a permit, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield at Bridgeport and presented to the court, Spear, J., on a plea of guilty; judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant to this court from the sentence imposed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield at Bridgeport (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of robbery, theft of a firearm, burglary and carrying a pistol without a permit.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from his convictions in two cases. In the first case, after a jury trial, defendant was convicted of the crimes of robbery and theft of a firearm. In the second case, defendant entered a plea of guilty to the charges of burglary and carrying a pistol without a permit. Upon review, the court affirmed the judgments of conviction. The court found that defendant was not prejudiced by the State's misplacement of an original composite sketch of the State's suspect in the robbery. The photocopy presented into evidence by the State actually helped defendant's case because the differences between the person portrayed in the photocopied sketch and defendant were more blatant then in the original copy. In addition, the court found that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion for a mistrial based upon alleged improper remarks made by the prosecutor. The trial court did not err in allowing a suspect sketch artist testify for the State to help the jury understand the intricacies of a composite sketch. Finally, defendant's conviction as to the pistol charge did not violate his right to double jeopardy following his conviction on the theft of a firearm charge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of robbery, theft of a firearm, burglary and carrying a pistol without a permit.

Hartford Federal Sav. & Loan Asso. v. Tucker


No. 11189


Supreme Court of Connecticut


196 Conn. 172; 491 A.2d 1084; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 764


February 14, 1985, Argued  
May 7, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for, inter alia, mortgage foreclosure on four properties owned by the named defendant, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Vasington, J., granted the plaintiff's motion for appointment of a receiver of rents; the court, Barall, J., rendered judgment of strict foreclosure on each property; from these and other decisions of the court, the named defendant appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owner appealed an order from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which granted a motion filed by plaintiff bank seeking the appointment of a receiver of rents and rendered judgment of strict foreclosure.


OVERVIEW: Defendant attacked the constitutionality of the procedures for the appointment of rent receivers and claimed error with regard to the final judgments of foreclosure. The court found that defendant's claims were untenable because he was given notice and a meaningful opportunity to be heard if he had objection to the appointment of a rent receiver. The court determined that defendant failed to prove that he was denied due process of law. The court found that it was not an unreasonable or arbitrary exercise of discretion which led the trial court to appoint a rent receiver and not to allow defendant to collect the rents. The issue of who should be the receiver of rents was an issue of fact. The court found that the foreclosure action constituted a valid exercise of a mortgagee's acceleration right and that defendant had failed to make a tender offer which was unconditional and unqualified. Under the circumstances, the court held that the trial court's finding that no legal tender was made was not clearly erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed finding no error in the order because there was no abuse of discretion in the appointment of a receiver of rent and because attorney's fees were warranted under the circumstances of defendant's persistent and longstanding pro se attack on the receivership.

 

479 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Sullivan v. Board of Police Comm'rs


No. 11896


Supreme Court of Connecticut


196 Conn. 208; 491 A.2d 1096; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 767; 47 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 538


March 8, 1985, Argued  
May 7, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action seeking to enjoin the defendants from enforcing the city's involuntary mandatory retirement age for police officers, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the court, Meehan, J., entered an ex parte temporary injunction preventing the removal of the plaintiff from his position until rendition of judgment upon the merits; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Missal, J.; judgment for the plaintiff from which the defendants appealed and the plaintiff cross appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error on the appeal; cross appeal dismissed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, commissioner and board, appealed the decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut), which entered an injunction in favor of plaintiff employee in his action seeking to enjoin defendants from enforcing the city's involuntary mandatory retirement age for police officers.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff employee brought an action against defendants, commissioner and board, to enjoin defendants from forcing him to retire at age 65 from his position as superintendent of the police department. The trial court entered an injunction barring plaintiff's involuntary retirement and held that mandatory retirement would violate the Age Discrimination in Employment Act (ADEA); 29 U.S.C.S. § 621 et seq. and the Connecticut Fair Employment Practices Act (CFEPA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-51 et seq. Defendants appealed, and the court reversed, holding that the trial court had no jurisdiction to hear plaintiff's claim because of his failure to invoke his federal or state administrative remedies, and that failure barred him from judicial remedy under both the ADEA and the CFEPA. The court found that plaintiff's complaint did not allege that he gave notice of his age discrimination claim to the Equal Employment Opportunity Commission, and the ADEA made such notice a prerequisite to a private action. The court concluded that plaintiff's claim under the CFEPA was flawed because of his failure to file a claim of discrimination with the Connecticut commission on human rights and opportunities.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment prohibiting defendants from enforcing mandatory retirement provisions against plaintiff employee and remanded for dismissal because plaintiff failed to notify the Equal Employment Opportunity Commission and to bring his complaint to the Connecticut human rights commission, and this failure foreclosed his access to judicial relief. The plaintiff's cross appeal was dismissed as moot.

 

480 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Peck v. Jacquemin


No. 12154


Supreme Court of Connecticut


196 Conn. 53; 491 A.2d 1043; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 740


December 12, 1984, Argued  
April 23, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries suffered in an automobile accident alleged to have been caused by the defendants, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield and, after the suit against the named defendant only was withdrawn, tried to the jury before Pickett, J.; verdict and judgment of $ 35,000 against the defendant Ira J. Roy, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.

The appellee filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a personal injury suit, plaintiff sought review of the order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Litchfield (Connecticut), which entered judgment on a jury verdict for plaintiff that was lower than that sought by plaintiff in his suit against defendant. Plaintiff contended that the trial court erroneously permitted evidence as to plaintiff's settlement agreement with another defendant, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-216a.


OVERVIEW: In a suit arising from a motor vehicle accident, after plaintiff settled his suit against one of two defendants, the other defendant was permitted to question plaintiff in front of the jury on the amount of his settlement. The trial court instructed the jury to subtract the settlement amount from any verdict in favor of plaintiff. Thereafter, the jury returned a verdict for substantially less than the amount plaintiff sought. In reversing, the court held that § 52-216a, which proscribed bringing to the jury's attention any settlement agreement and which set forth the course to be undertaken by the trial court after a jury's verdict, was applicable even though plaintiff's cause of action arose before the applicable date of the statute. Further, the court held that § 52-216a was constitutional under the court's earlier decision declaring the previous version unconstitutional. The court found that by enacting the present statute, the legislature expressed what it intended the trial court to do after a jury verdict by directing the trial court to consider any settlement money paid in making its post-verdict determination on the issue of any claimed excessiveness or inadequacy.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the trial court's judgment and ordered a new trial limited to the issue of damages.

 

481 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Rogers v. Commission on Human Rights & Opportunities


No. 12453


Supreme Court of Connecticut


195 Conn. 543; 489 A.2d 368; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 727


February 5, 1985, Argued  
March 26, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the defendant commission's dismissal of the plaintiff's administrative complaint alleging racial discrimination against the defendant United Technologies Corporation, and of his subsequent requests for reconsideration, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Barall, J., rendered judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee challenged a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which dismissed the employee's appeal from defendant Commission on Human Rights and Opportunities' dismissal of his administrative complaint alleging racial discrimination against defendant employer as well as his subsequent requests for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: The employee, a black man, was given notice that he was to be laid off from his position as senior research technician with the employer. He filed a complaint alleging racial discrimination, which was subsequently referred to the commission but not filed until approximately seven months later. The commission dismissed the complaint because it was filed more than 180 days after the date of the alleged discrimination. The employee's petition for reconsideration was denied by the commission, and the trial court dismissed the petition for appeal as having been untimely filed. The employee was mailed the notice of dismissal of his complaint by certified mail, which was sufficient. The method of delivery was more accurate than that which was required. The employee's own inaction in response to actual notice could not be made the basis of a claim that he was not afforded due process. The employee's claim was terminated for failure to comply with the instructions he received at his home to collect an important document from the postal service. He received adequate notice of the dismissal of his complaint; therefore his equal protection claim was unfounded.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which dismissed the employee's appeal.

 

482 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Pineman v. Oechslin


No. 12529


Supreme Court of Connecticut


195 Conn. 405; 488 A.2d 803; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 704; 6 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 1443


December 13, 1984, Argued  
March 12, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Class action challenging the constitutionality of the 1975 revision of the Connecticut Employees Retirement Act which raised the retirement eligibility age for female employees, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford where the court, N. O'Neill, J., rendered judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiffs appealed and the defendants cross appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state employees and defendant state officials cross appealed from a judgment for defendants by the Superior Court, Harford-New Britain (Connecticut) in plaintiffs' action for, inter alia, a judgment declaring that the pre-1975 State Employees Retirement Act (Act) created a contractual obligation for Connecticut to maintain the pre-1975 retirement ages for female employees who had not begun receiving benefits when the Act was revised.


OVERVIEW: The Act had originally permitted female employees to retire at age 50 with 25 years of service. To achieve equal treatment of female and male employees, the Act was amended to permit female employees to retire at age 55 with 25 years of service. The trial court concluded that the legislature never intended the Act to create contractual rights in state employees. The employees argued that promissory emanations from the Act of deferred compensation designed to induce state employees to accept and retain public employment, together with reliance on such "promises" by the employee, were sufficient to create a contractual relationship between the state and its employees. The court held that the Act conferred no contractual rights in the statutory pension plan on state employees. A statute did not create vested contractual rights absent a clear statement of legislative intent to contract. There was no clear expression by the legislature that the Act was intended to create vested contractual rights in state employees prior to the satisfaction of all eligibility requirements.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's judgment.

Farmington v. Westland Co.


Nos. 12072, 12073


Supreme Court of Connecticut


195 Conn. 418; 488 A.2d 810; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 705


January 17, 1985, Argued  
March 12, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action, in each case, to foreclose real property tax liens on certain parcels of land located in the town of Farmington, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Brennan, J., after granting the plaintiff's motion for default in each case, rendered judgment of foreclosure by sale for the plaintiff and the named defendants appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owners appealed a decision from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which granted plaintiff town's motion for default and rendered judgment of foreclosure by sale for the town in two actions brought by the town to foreclose real property tax liens on certain parcels of land located in the town.


OVERVIEW: One action was for the foreclosure by sale of certain tax liens in favor of the town, and the other action was for the foreclosure by sale of certain tax liens and liens for an assessment of benefits from the construction of a sewer line in favor of the town. A default for failure to disclose a defense was entered against the owners. The trial court denied the owners' motions to dismiss and refused to hear other motions filed by the owners. Judgment for foreclosure by sale was rendered in each case in favor of the town. On appeal, the court found no error and remanded the cases. The court found that the questions included in the owners' statements of issues related to their motions for dismissal and the motions with requests for rulings. The court held that because owners did not object to the trial court's denial of the motion to dismiss and refusal to rule on the other motions, there was nothing from which to appeal. The court concluded that because the questions raised in the motions were the only issues stated in the reasons for appeal, there was nothing before the court for consideration.


OUTCOME: The court found no error on appeal in the trial court's grant of the town's motion for default and judgment of foreclosure rendered in favor of the town. The court remanded the cases to the superior court for the setting of new sale dates and other necessary orders.

State v. Marra


No. 11214


Supreme Court of Connecticut


195 Conn. 421; 489 A.2d 350; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 706


December 11, 1984, Argued  
March 12, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of larceny in the first degree, larceny in the second degree and forgery in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield at Bridgeport and tried to the jury before Cretella, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty on all counts, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield at Bridgeport (Connecticut), which convicted him of larceny in the first degree, larceny in the second degree, and forgery in the second degree and sentenced him to imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sold a stolen car to the victim and was convicted of larceny and forgery. Defendant appealed from the judgment of conviction on several grounds, claiming that the trial court erred in refusing to grant appropriate relief from the allegedly prejudicial effects of publicity; in denying his request for a continuance; in restricting his cross-examination of a witness for the state; and in charging the jury. The court found no error. The publicity did not concern the offenses for which defendant was on trial and did not approach the level where prejudice could be presumed. The trial court's extensive use of voir dire and the detailed instructions to the jurors were reasonably effective in protecting defendant's right to a fair trial. Defendant failed to demonstrate any specific prejudice to his defense arising from the trial court's denial of his motion for a continuance of one week. Defendant sought to question the victim, a foreign exchange student, about working while a student. The trial court's exclusion of this questioning was not error. The jury instructions that deviated from the requirements were those submitted by defendant and thus were not in error.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in defendant's trial and convictions and sentenced him to imprisonment.

 

485 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Tucker v. Alleyne


No. 12171


Supreme Court of Connecticut


195 Conn. 399; 488 A.2d 452; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 698; 1985-1 Trade Cas. (CCH) P66,548


January 11, 1985, Argued  
March 5, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Complaint charging the defendant employees of the department of social services with failure to make direct rental payments on behalf of city welfare recipients to the plaintiff landlord, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, N. O'Neill, J., rendered judgment for the defendants and the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed judgment entered in favor of defendants by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), in action brought under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 for alleged equal protection violations and under the Connecticut Anti-Trust Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 35-28.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff landlord sued defendants, employees of the city welfare department, alleging they had violated plaintiff's equal protection rights and the Connecticut Anti-Trust Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 35-28. The basis of the complaint was defendants' practice of not making rent payments for welfare recipients directly to plaintiff. The court affirmed judgment in defendants' favor. First, plaintiff provided no basis for examining the equal protection claim on anything other than the rational basis test. Thus, although rent was sometimes paid directly to landlords, such payments were rare and the trial court was not clearly erroneous in finding that plaintiff's requests for direct payment were treated no differently than the requests of other landlords, and there was no equal protection violation. Likewise, no violation of the Anti-Trust Act was shown as there was no evidence of a conspiracy by defendants that benefitted other landlords and harmed plaintiff.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed, as trial court was not clearly erroneous in concluding that plaintiff landlord's requests for direct rental payments from welfare recipients were treated no differently from other landlords' requests by defendants welfare employees; thus, there were no equal protection or anti-trust violations.

In re Juvenile Appeal


No. 12391


Supreme Court of Connecticut


195 Conn. 303; 488 A.2d 778; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 691


November 7, 1984, Argued  
February 26, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motion by the state to transfer the juvenile defendant to the regular criminal docket of the Superior Court, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, Juvenile Matters at New Haven, where the court, Brenneman, J., granted the motion, from which order the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile sought review of a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven, Juvenile Matters (Connecticut), which granted the State's motion to transfer the juvenile to the regular criminal docket.


OVERVIEW: The crimes of sexual assault in the first degree, kidnapping in the first degree, larceny in the second degree, and robbery in the second degree resulted from an incident where a woman was abducted, raped, and robbed. The crimes were alleged as the basis for the charges of delinquency against the juvenile. The court granted the motion of the State to transfer the case to the regular criminal docket pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-126. On appeal, the court dismissed the appeal. The court held that since the prerequisite of imposition of sentence had not yet occurred, the transfer order in the case could not be deemed a final judgment. Strict adherence to the final judgment rule was necessary in criminal cases because the delays and disruptions attendant upon intermediate appeal were especially inimical to the effective and fair administration of the law. The court was not persuaded that the potential for harm to juvenile offenders from erroneous transfer orders was so much greater in kind or degree than that which a 17-year-old, improperly denied the benefits of youthful offender treatment, could suffer awaiting redress on appeal from a final judgment.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal of the juvenile in his appeal of the decision of the trial court, which granted the State's motion to transfer the juvenile to the regular criminal docket.

State v. Tyson


No. 10764


Supreme Court of Connecticut


195 Conn. 326; 487 A.2d 1091; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 692


January 9, 1985, Argued  
February 26, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two part indictment charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crime of robbery in the first degree, and, in the second part, with being a persistent dangerous felony offender, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and, after the court, Reynolds, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss the indictment and after the defendant pleaded guilty to the charge of robbery in the first degree, tried to the jury before Zoarski, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of being a persistent dangerous felony offender, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of New Haven (Connecticut), which found defendant guilty of robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(2) based upon his guilty plea, and of being a persistent dangerous felony offender as provided by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40 following a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to first degree robbery but challenged the charge of being a persistent dangerous violent felony offender pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40. A jury in the superior court convicted him of the second charge. The court affirmed. The court noted that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40(a) defined a persistent dangerous felony offender as a person who stood convicted of robbery in the first or second degree and had been, prior to the commission of the present crime, convicted of and imprisoned, under a sentence to a term of imprisonment of more than one year or of death, in Connecticut or in any other state or in a federal correctional institution. The court found that the language of the statute was clear, and defendant had been previously convicted of first degree robbery and sentenced to more than one year in prison. The court found that there was no viable basis for defendant's challenge to the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40(a) upon the ground of vagueness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court finding that defendant was properly convicted of being a persistent dangerous felony offender.

Gunther v. Dubno


No. 11862


Supreme Court of Connecticut


195 Conn. 284; 487 A.2d 1080; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 690


December 11, 1984, Argued  
February 26, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Class action challenging the constitutionality of the state's Unincorporated Business Tax and an amendment to the Corporation Business Tax, seeking a refund of monies paid pursuant to said act and other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield at Bridgeport and referred to Hon. Irving Levine, state trial referee; judgment for the defendants and the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant class sought review of the order of the Superior Court of Fairfield (Connecticut), which entered judgment for appellee, the Connecticut Commissioner of Revenue Services, in an action challenging the constitutionality of the state's Unincorporated Business Tax and an amendment to the Corporation Business Tax and seeking a refund of monies paid.


OVERVIEW: The principal issue on appeal was the constitutionality of the 1981Connecticut tax on the net income of unincorporated businesses, Conn. Gen. Stat. ch. 28, §§ 12-610 - 12-629 and Conn. Gen. Stat. ch. 208, § 12-219. The trial court held the tax was constitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment, holding that the statutory classifications were reasonable, that there were not arbitrary, and that the distinctions enumerated bore a reasonable relationship to the object of the legislation. The statute clearly and precisely afforded a person of ordinary intelligence a reasonable opportunity to know what was permitted or prohibited, it was not void for vagueness, and the retroactive operation of the tax statute did not per se violate the due process rights of taxpayers adversely affected thereby.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

489 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rothenberg


No. 11883


Supreme Court of Connecticut


195 Conn. 253; 487 A.2d 545; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 701


December 13, 1984, Argued  
February 19, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and unlawful restraint in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, and tried to the court, Kinney, J.; judgment of guilty on both counts from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which convicted him of sexual assault in the first degree and unlawful restraint in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of sexual assault in the first degree and unlawful restraint in the first degree, he appealed. On appeal the court held that the trial court's finding that defendant could initially have misconstrued the victim's conduct as indicative of a willingness to engage in explicit sexual conduct did not prove that defendant was mistaken about the victim's consent or that he lacked the mental state necessary to commit the charged offenses. The evidence showed that, when the victim sought to withdraw from the situation, defendant was unwilling to permit her to do so and that he thereafter forced himself on the victim and compelled her to engage in sexual intercourse against her will. The court stated that the victim's unambiguous request to leave defendant's condominium removed from defendant any misinterpretation as to her wishes. Defendant's conduct was thereafter knowingly coercive. The court found that a temporary misunderstanding about consent did not give irreversible license to compel sexual intercourse. The court concluded that defendant's motion for a new trial was untimely and that allegedly new evidence could have been made available at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

490 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Devino


No. 11548


Supreme Court of Connecticut


195 Conn. 70; 485 A.2d 1302; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 669


November 6, 1984, Argued  
January 22, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of possession of cocaine and two counts of the crime of sale of cocaine, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Hull, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which convicted him of two counts of possession of cocaine in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19-481(a) and two counts of the crime of sale of cocaine in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19-480(a) and sentenced him to concurrent terms of one to four years on each count.


OVERVIEW: An undercover police officer purchased drugs from defendant on two separate occasions. Defendant was convicted on a substitute information charging him with two counts of possession of cocaine and two counts of sale of cocaine. He was sentenced on each count to concurrent terms. On appeal, the court found no error. Defendant failed to object to the trial court's instructions on entrapment at trial. Because the instructions did not fail to submit to the jury an essential element of the offense or constitute plain error, defendant's claim was not preserved for review. The court employed a two-step analysis to examine the double jeopardy claim in the context of a single trial. First, the court found that each pair of possession and sale charges arose from a single act or transaction. Secondly, however, the court determined that a conviction for illegal possession of narcotics required proof of a fact that a conviction for illegal sale did not. Therefore, defendant was convicted of different offenses and therefore, the punishments that he received did not place him in double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the judgment convicting defendant of possession of cocaine and sale of cocaine.

Horton v. Meskill

Supreme Court of Connecticut


195 Conn. 24; 486 A.2d 1099; 1985 Conn. LEXIS 665


October 3, 1984, Argued  
January 15, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motions for orders to show cause why, inter alia, the defendant Meskill et al. should not be enjoined from distributing state funds for education in violation of the state constitution, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford; the motion of the town of Greenwich et al. to intervene as parties defendant, and the motion of the city of Hartford et al. to intervene as parties plaintiff were granted; the actions were tried to the court, Spada, J., which rendered judgments determining certain portions of the state program for distribution of education funds to be unconstitutional and ordering certain remedial relief from which the defendant Meskill et al. and the defendant town of Greenwich et al. appealed and the plaintiff Horton et al. and the plaintiff city of Hartford et al. cross appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error in part on the appeals; no error on the cross appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a city, a board of education, and individuals, and defendants, the governor, the state treasurer, the comptroller, the commissioner of education, members of the state board of education, and various towns, challenged an order from the Superior Court, Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which found a statutory financing system for education to be constitutional in design but unconstitutional in part.


OVERVIEW: The city, the board of education, and the individuals filed an action against the governor, the treasurer, the comptroller, the commissioner of education, members of the state board of education, and the towns, challenging the constitutionality of the statutory financing system for free public elementary and secondary school education in the state. The trial court found the financing system constitutional in design but unconstitutional in part. Defendants appealed and plaintiffs cross-appealed. The court found that the financing legislation was constitutional as originally enacted. The court further found that the trial court correctly decided that assigning a fixed share of expenditures to the state did not provide a sound basis for assuring a proper distribution of responsibility or of funding for substantially equal educational opportunities. However, the court disagreed with the substantive standard by which the trial court tested the validity of the statutes and with the procedural failure of the trial court to afford all the interested parties an opportunity to be heard on the remedial implications of the court's decisions on unconstitutionality.


OUTCOME: The order finding the statutory financing system for education to be constitutional in design but unconstitutional in part was affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.

Laurel Park, Inc. v. Pac


Nos. 12467, 12468


Supreme Court of Connecticut


194 Conn. 677; 485 A.2d 1272; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 738


October 9, 1984, Argued  
December 25, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application for injunctive relief from a cease and desist order prohibiting the operation of the named plaintiff's sanitary landfill facility, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Ripley, J., issued a temporary injunction restraining the enforcement of the cease and desist order, from which the defendants appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Commissioner of the Department of Environmental Protection (DEP) and a citizens group, appealed the order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which granted the motion of plaintiffs, a landfill and a municipality, for a temporary injunction staying the DEP's order to close the landfill.


OVERVIEW: The DEP found contaminated ground water at the landfill and issued an order requiring the landfill to cease operation and the acceptance of solid wastes until a full hearing was held. The landfill appealed the order of the DEP, and the trial court issued a temporary injunction staying the DEP's order to cease and desist. On appeal, the court held that the landfill and the municipality failed to exhaust their remedies under the administrative rules of the DEP. The court held that the landfill and the municipality should have appealed the DEP's order under the Uniform Administrative Procedures Act (UAPA), Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 4-166 to 4-189, before seeking an injunction. The UAPA adequately responded to the concerns about continued operation of the landfill pending an adjudication on the merits by the DEP. Because the landfill's complaint alleged a violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, the trial court correctly refused to grant the DEP's motion to dismiss. Inclusion of a § 1983 claim was of no avail in supporting the issuance of the injunction.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the decision of the trial court and remanded the case for further proceedings.

Lombardi v. Bridgeport


No. 11935


Supreme Court of Connecticut


194 Conn. 601; 483 A.2d 1092; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 718


October 4, 1984, Argued  
November 20, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield at Bridgeport and tried to the court, Celotto, J.; judgment for the plaintiff, from which the defendants appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a city and two of its supervisory employees, challenged the decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield at Bridgeport (Connecticut) that found that plaintiff, a nonprobationary employee, was entitled to a hearing before being laid off for budgetary reasons in his action for a mandatory injunction to compel defendants to comply with the civil service commission's rulings requiring the employee's reinstatement.


OVERVIEW: The issue in the case was whether the employee, who worked in the noncompetitive division of the classified service, had a right under the city charter or the state or federal constitutions to appeal a layoff for fiscal reasons to the city's civil service commission. The trial court found in favor of the employee, holding that Bridgeport, Conn., Charter § 11 was unconstitutional because it treated noncompetitive and competitive employees differently by granting the competitive employees a hearing before discharge. Defendants appealed and the court reversed. The court held that the commission was without the statutory authority to sustain the employee's appeal. Absent any disparity in treatment of competitive and noncompetitive employees regarding appeals from layoffs for economic reasons under the city charter, the employee's equal protection claim could not stand. The court rejected the employee's claim that he was entitled to a hearing before the commission as a matter of due process.


OUTCOME: The court found error in the trial court's judgment, set aside that judgment, and remanded the case with direction to render judgment for defendants.

State v. Couture


No. 11294


Supreme Court of Connecticut


194 Conn. 530; 482 A.2d 300; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 695


May 9, 1984, Argued  
October 2, 1984, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Connecticut v. Couture, 469 U.S. 1192, 105 S. Ct. 967, 83 L. Ed. 2d 971, 1985 U.S. LEXIS 728 (1985)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crimes, in count four, of intentional murder and felony murder, in count five, of felony murder and, in count six, of intentional murder and felony murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Hull, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty in counts four and five, and verdict and judgment of guilty of felony murder in count six, and appeal by the defendant to this court.
State v. Couture, 37 Conn. Supp. 705, 435 A.2d 369, 1981 Conn. Super. LEXIS 184 (Conn. Super. Ct., 1981)



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court (Connecticut), which, after a jury trial, convicted defendant of three counts of murder and sentenced him to three terms of imprisonment of 25 years to life, such sentences to run consecutively, for a total effective sentence of 75 years to life.


OVERVIEW: On appeal the defendant claimed that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence seized in violation of his Fourth Amendment rights; that the trial court erred in amending the indictment; that the composition of the grand jury and the conduct of its proceedings were improper; that the prosecutor's summation was prejudicial; and that the consecutive sentences were illegal. The court rejected the Fourth Amendment challenge, noting that the search warrant at issue and its supporting affidavit were legally sufficient, and that additional items not described in the warrant, but in plain view, were properly seized. The court also rejected the challenges to the grand jury composition and proceedings and to the court's amendment of the indictment. In addition, the court held that imposing multiple punishments for multiple crimes was not a double jeopardy violation and that defendant's sentence was legal. However, the court reversed the conviction, holding that the prosecutor's repeated references to defendant as a "murderous fiend" and a "rat," combined with the court's refusal to instruct the jury to ignore the remarks constituted grounds for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and ordered a new trial.

Gaines v. Manson


Nos. 12460, 12461, 12462, 12463, 12464, 12465, 12466


Supreme Court of Connecticut


194 Conn. 510; 481 A.2d 1084; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 682


June 14, 1984, Argued  
September 11, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Seven petitions for writs of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Gaffney, J.; judgment dismissing the petitions, from which the petitioners appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmates appealed a judgment that was entered by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut). The judgment dismissed their petitions for a writ of habeas corpus, which they filed after appointed counsel from the public defender's office substantially delayed the processing of their respective appeals.


OVERVIEW: The parties stipulated that the two to four and one-half year delays in processing the inmates' criminal appeals was caused by understaffing in the appellate public defender's office. The inmates contended that the delays violated their rights to due process, equal protection of the laws, and effective assistance of counsel contrary to Conn. Const., art. I, §§ 8, 10 and 20 and U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court reversed the dismissal of the petitions. The court held that: (1) the trial court erred in dismissing the writs of all of the inmates except for two inmates whose cases were moot by virtue of the hearing of their appeals, and (2) in applying the federal speedy trial violation test in the context of institutionally engendered appellate delays, a court was obligated to balance the relevant factors so as to take into account the remedial alternatives that were available as well as the constitutional rights that were implicated. The court concluded that the inmates established that they have suffered extensive delays due to the understaffing of the public defender's office, and the delays discriminated against them because of their poverty.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the inmates' petitions for a writ of habeas corpus was reversed, except for the petitions of two inmates whose petitions were moot in light of the status of their criminal appeals. The matters were remanded to the trial court with direction to determine whether any of the inmates were prejudiced by the extended delay of their appeals, and to fashion an appropriate remedy.

State v. Castonguay


Nos. 10554, 11166


Supreme Court of Connecticut


194 Conn. 416; 481 A.2d 56; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 687


April 5, 1984, Argued  
September 4, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of capital felony and with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before D. Shea, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, and appeal by the defendant to this court; thereafter, the defendant's motion to correct the sentence was granted, and the state, on the granting of permission, appealed.

The appellant-appellee (state) filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error in part on defendant's appeal; further proceedings. State's appeal dismissed sua sponte.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which convicted him of capital felony and of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of capital felony for the intentional murder of a police officer engaged in performing his duties and of felony murder for causing the death while in the course of and in flight from a burglary or attempted burglary. Defendant claimed that the underrepresentation of Hispanics on the grand jury denied him his due process rights and that the jury was improperly instructed that it could discuss the case prior to the close of all the evidence and the trial court's charge. The court held that defendant failed to establish a prima facie violation of the fair-cross-section requirement because he did not prove that there was a substantial underrepresentation of Hispanics that affected the composition of the grand jury. The court applied the substantial impact test and determined that only slightly more than one additional Hispanic should have been included on every other grand jury. The court agreed that the instruction was erroneous because it undermined the jury's ability to remain impartial and remanded the case for an evidentiary hearing to provide the State with the opportunity to prove that the error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court found error on defendant's appeal regarding his judgment of conviction and remanded the case to the trial court for an evidentiary hearing on harmless error.

State v. Pellegrino


No. 9958


Supreme Court of Connecticut


194 Conn. 279; 480 A.2d 537; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 694


June 12, 1984, Argued  
August 21, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of arson in the first degree and of manslaughter in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield at Bridgeport and tried to the jury before Hull, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, and appeal by the defendant to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut) convicting him of arson in the first degree and manslaughter in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and an accomplice were involved in burning down a shopping complex. The accomplice was killed in the fire and defendant was convicted of arson and manslaughter in connection with the accomplice's death. Defendant contended that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-111 (1977) was not intended to include accomplices. He also contended that the court erred by denying his motion to suppress certain statements he made to a police officer and that the prosecutor improperly commented that he refused to talk to the police. The court held that (1) § 53a-111 included situations where defendant burned a building with the intent to destroy it while he was aware that an accomplice was in or near the building; (2) defendant, who spoke to a police officer while medicated on morphine, waived his right against self-incrimination when he spoke to police because he was aware of the right and voluntarily relinquished it; and (3) the prosecutor's comments on defendant's exercise of his right to remain silent constituted reversible error because, in making the comments, the prosecutor implied that the jury should draw an unfavorable inference from defendant's decision to remain silent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and ordered a new trial for defendant.

In re Juvenile Appeal


No. 11964


Supreme Court of Connecticut


194 Conn. 252; 479 A.2d 1204; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 678


June 5, 1984, Argued  
August 14, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for termination of parental rights, brought to the Superior Court for Juvenile Matters for the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the court, Lavery, J.; judgment terminating parental rights, from which the mother appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant mother sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court for Juvenile Matters, Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which granted the state's petition to terminate her parental rights with respect to her son pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 17-43a (a). The mother argued that two of the three statutory provisions under which her parental rights were terminated were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The state filed a petition seeking to terminate the mother's parental rights under Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 17-43a(a). The state based its petition for termination on the grounds of abandonment, failure to rehabilitate, and no ongoing parent-child relationship. The district court granted the state's petition and terminated the mother's parental rights. On appeal, the mother challenged the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 17-43a(a)(1) and (4), specifically challenging the district court's first and third grounds for termination. The court affirmed. Specifically, the court held that because the mother did not attack the sufficiency of the evidence supporting the district court's finding of failure to rehabilitate under Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 17-43a(a)(2) and never attacked the constitutional validity of that section, it was unnecessary to consider whether the remaining grounds were unconstitutional. The court found that where the mother left unchallenged one of the statutory bases on which her parental rights were terminated, it did not have to decide the constitutional issues raised in connection with the remaining two grounds.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment.

 

499 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Schieffelin & Co. v. Department of Liquor Control


Nos. 12363, 12364, 12077, 12078, 12079


Supreme Court of Connecticut


194 Conn. 165; 479 A.2d 1191; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 668


May 4, 1984, Argued  
August 7, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] In the first case, appeal by the plaintiff from a decision of the named defendant on the plaintiff's termination of certain defendant distributors of alcoholic beverages, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, M. Hennessey, J.; judgment sustaining the plaintiff's appeal as to the defendants Brescome Distributors Corporation et al. and dismissing the appeal as to the defendant Connecticut Distributors, Inc., from which the named defendant et al. appealed to this court.

In the second case, action for a declaratory judgment on the constitutionality of a certain public act and appeal by the plaintiff from a decision of the named defendant on the termination of certain defendant distributors of alcoholic beverages, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, M. Hennessey, J.; declaratory judgment for the plaintiff and sustaining the appeal, from which the defendants appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings. Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Department of Liquor Control appealed the judgments from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which sustained plaintiff distributor's appeal of a liquor license termination under 1981 Conn. Acts 81.367, and which declared the Act invalid in plaintiff licensee's suit against the Department.


OVERVIEW: The Act reduced a period for just cause terminations of liquor licenses from 24 months to 6 months. After the Department terminated their licenses, the distributor appealed the termination and the licensee sued the Department for a declaratory judgment that the Act was unconstitutional. When the superior court sustained the appeals and held the act invalid, the Department appealed. The cases were consolidated. The court reversed the judgment for the licensee and directed a judgment for the Department. The court reversed the judgment for the distributor and remanded. The court found error in both cases. The Act applied and was constitutional. The Act did not violate the Contracts Clause, or the Fourteenth Amendment's Due Process or Equal Protection Clauses. Although the Act applied prospectively to terminations of distributorships, the criteria for termination might have arisen either before or after its effective date. The Act applied to distributorships existing when it became effective. It was therefore reasonably foreseeable that a distributorship requirement for just cause termination would not have remained static and would have been reduced.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment for the distributor in its suit against the Department after the termination of its license and remanded for further proceedings. The court set aside the judgment for the licensee and remanded to render a judgment for the Department in the licensee's declaratory judgment suit after the termination of its license.

 

500 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


No. 10834


Supreme Court of Connecticut


194 Conn. 213; 479 A.2d 814; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 672


June 7, 1984, Argued  
August 7, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Separate informations charging the defendant with the crimes of burglary in the third degree and criminal impersonation, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two, and tried to the jury before Geen, J.; verdicts and judgments of guilty, and a combined appeal by the defendant to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of burglary in the third degree and criminal impersonation by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield, Geographical Area Number Two (Connecticut), from which he appealed. Defendant claimed the superior court erred: (1) in its instructions to the jury on the burglary charge; and (2) in its denial of defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal of criminal impersonation because of insufficient evidence.


OVERVIEW: The court found no error in the burglary instruction. Taken as a whole and related to the facts, it was not reasonably possible that the instruction failed to guide the jury to a clear understanding of the offense. Given the careful relation of the evidence to the elements of the burglary charge, it was not reasonably possible that the jury was misled by the court's failure to read the statutory name and definition of larceny. As for the challenge to the criminal impersonation conviction, defendant alleged that giving a false name was not impersonation of another unless the name given was that of a real person. As no evidence proved the existence of a real Sam James, defendant argued his conviction could not stand. The plain meaning of "another" was an additional one of the same kind, one other than oneself. To impersonate another was to act as some other real person. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-130 had not prohibited giving a false name; it only prohibited impersonating another. Therefore, it was error to deny defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal on the criminal impersonation charge, as there was insufficient evidence for the jury to have found that he committed that crime.


OUTCOME: There was no error in defendant's conviction of the crime of burglary in the third degree. There was error in defendant's conviction of the crime of criminal impersonation, so that judgment of conviction was set aside. The case was remanded to the superior court with direction to render a judgment of acquittal on that charge.

Warner v. Leslie-Elliott Constructors


No. 11927


Supreme Court of Connecticut


194 Conn. 129; 479 A.2d 231; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 645


April 5, 1984, Argued  
July 31, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for wrongful death, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Windham, where the court, Dannehy, J., granted the defendant Hale Manufacturing Company's motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon; the court further granted the other defendants' motion to strike the complaint and, on the plaintiff's failure to plead over, rendered judgment for those defendants; from those judgments the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant administratrix challenged a decision from the Superior Court in the District of Windham (Connecticut), which granted summary judgment to appellee corporate landowner and dismissed appellee individual landowner and construction company in the action by the administratrix for wrongful death.


OVERVIEW: A motorcyclist was killed on a private road on land that belonged to a group of corporate and individual landowners that were having work performed by the construction company. The administratrix brought a wrongful death action against the landowners and construction company. The trial court granted summary judgment and dismissed the action because Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 52-557j excepted landowners from liability for the use of the motorcycle except where the landowner charged a fee, gave permission, or acted wilfully or maliciously. The administratrix asserted that the trial court erred in barring her action unless she showed that: (1) a fee was charged or the actions were wilful or malicious; (2) the construction company was not a landowner; and (3) the complaint failed to allege malice. The court affirmed the decision that dismissed the individual and corporate landowner because the statute was proper in abrogating the common law by excepting certain acts from liability, but reversed and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings the dismissal of the construction company since that company was not an owner of title to the land.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision from the trial court that granted summary judgment and released the corporate and individual landowners, but reversed the decision that dismissed the construction company and remanded that claim for further proceedings.

 

502 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Pellegrino v. O'Neill


No. 12369


Supreme Court of Connecticut


193 Conn. 670; 480 A.2d 476; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 628


March 2, 1984, Argued  
July 17, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining that the financing provided for the state judicial system is unconstitutional because of congestion and long delays in reaching trial in civil jury cases in certain judicial districts, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Ripley, J.; judgment dismissing the action, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, litigants in various civil cases, appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which dismissed their action seeking a declaratory judgment that the financing provided for the state judicial system was unconstitutional because of congestion and long delays.


OVERVIEW: The complaint alleged that inadequate financing of the state judicial system had produced a backlog of civil jury cases in certain judicial districts. The trial court concluded that the question of whether the state's financing of the judicial system violated the litigants' constitutional rights because of delay in the disposition of their cases was nonjusticiable. The court affirmed, holding that although the courts had inherent authority to require the legislature to provide sufficient funding to operate the court system in accordance with constitutional requirements, such authority did not extend to requiring the appointment of additional judges. Increases in the number of judges, as well as appointments to the additional positions created, were not within the province of the judiciary. The exercise of such legislative power was forbidden to the judiciary under Conn. Const. art. II, the separation of powers provision. Accordingly, the case involved a nonjusticiable political question.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the declaratory judgment action.

 

503 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Ryszkiewicz v. New Britain


No. 11134


Supreme Court of Connecticut


193 Conn. 589; 479 A.2d 793; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 633


February 28, 1984, Argued  
July 10, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for injuries sustained in a fall on an icy sidewalk, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain and tried to the jury before N. O'Neill, J.; verdict and judgment for the plaintiff, and appeal by the plaintiff to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff pedestrian appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at New Britain (Connecticut), in which the jury found defendant city liable and awarded the pedestrian damages, which were limited by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 2709 (1961), in a slip and fall case. The pedestrian contended that § 2709 was unconstitutional as applied and violated equal protection principles.


OVERVIEW: The pedestrian claimed that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 2709 violated constitutional guarantees of equal protection. The court agreed and held that § 2709 violated equal protection principles and that it was therefore error to limit the damage award in the pedestrian's lawsuit. It was the city's duty to keep the sidewalk in good repair. The court explained that when the city's benefit of immunity began to burden a certain class of citizens, those persons injured on the city's sidewalks because of snow or ice accumulation, however, some identifiable reason for the city to receive that special benefit of immunity was required. The problem with § 2709 was that the legislature, in enacting Conn. Gen. Stat. § 13a-149, made a clear policy statement that municipal liability for damages caused by defective sidewalks was not to be limited. Given that clear pronouncement, there was no rational basis behind imposing a liability limit in damages for all such torts that happened to occur in the city. The court concluded that there was no reason why those injured by the city's tortious acts were denied full recovery of compensatory damages for resulting injuries.


OUTCOME: The court found error and set aside the judgment, and the case was remanded for a hearing in damages only. The statute that limited the city's liability to a certain amount was unconstitutional as applied and there was no reason why those injured by the city's tortious acts were denied full recovery of compensatory damages for resulting injuries.

State v. Shine


No. 11987


Supreme Court of Connecticut


193 Conn. 632; 479 A.2d 218; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 636


April 5, 1984, Argued  
July 10, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of manslaughter in the first degree and assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before O'Donnell, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut) convicted defendant of manslaughter in the first degree and assault in the first degree. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, the decedent, and the decedent's sister were all patrons of a bar. Just prior to the bar's closing, defendant and decedent resumed an earlier argument in the parking lot. When defendant got into his car and accelerated, decedent fell from the car and injured his knee. Defendant then drove his car around the parking lot and returned to where decedent and his sister were standing. The car struck them both, thereby killing decedent and injuring his sister. Thereafter, defendant was charged with manslaughter and assault. Defendant filed a motion in limine seeking to introduce evidence of his voluntary intoxication to dispute that he had acted recklessly. The trial court denied the motion. On appeal, the court found that the trial court did not err in excluding the evidence of voluntary intoxication because it would not have negated defendant's recklessness. The court also found that defendant was not deprived of the opportunity to contest recklessness. In addition, the court determined that the trial court properly instructed the jury concerning mental state and the drawing of inferences. Defendant's convictions were upheld.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for manslaughter and assault.

Shelton v. Commissioner of Dep't of Environmental Protection

SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT

May 9, 1984, Argued  
June 26, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the city of Shelton from the decision of the defendant Commissioner of the Department of Environmental Protection to issue certain permits to the Connecticut Resources Recovery Authority to operate and expand an existing landfill, and two actions for declaratory and injunctive relief claiming that use of the property by the authority violated local zoning and required written consent of the plaintiff's board of aldermen, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, O'Neill, J.; judgments sustaining the administrative appeal, enjoining the Connecticut Resources Recovery Authority from operating the expanded landfill and declaring that local zoning regulations prohibited the expansion of the landfill, from which the defendants appealed and the plaintiffs cross-appealed.



DISPOSITION: Judgments directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, Connecticut Resources Recovery Authority (CRRA) and Department of Environmental Protection (DEP), appealed from judgments of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) that sustained plaintiff city's administrative appeal of the issuance of a DEP landfill permit, granted an injunction, and ruled that the city's zoning regulations prohibited the landfill expansion.


OVERVIEW: The city filed three separate actions seeking to prevent the CRRA from implementing its plan to operate a regional landfill on a site where a smaller landfill was operated. Council on Probate Judicial Conduct re Kinsella


No. 12123


Supreme Court of Connecticut


193 Conn. 180; 476 A.2d 1041; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 587


February 29, 1984, Argued  
May 15, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Complaint by the Hon. Glenn E. Knierim, probate court administrator, concerning the conduct of James H. Kinsella, probate judge, relating to the estate of Ethel F. Donaghue, brought to the Council on Probate Judicial Conduct which, after a hearing, recommended public censure for violations of certain canons of the Code of Probate Judicial Conduct, from which Judge Kinsella appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Council on Probate Judicial Conduct (Connecticut) (Council) recommended appellant judge's public censure for his violations of the canons of ethics in connection with his handling of the estate of an incapable person. The judge filed an appeal in the court, as authorized by Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 45-11g (c).


OVERVIEW: As a result of the judge's handling of the estate of an incapable person, the Council recommended public censure of judge. On review, the court found no error. The court held that, in the totality of the circumstances manifested by the entire record before the court, public censure was warranted. The court held that the Council did not err in denying the judge's request for a more particular statement of the charges against him, requests for discovery, motion for dismissal of the charges on grounds of estoppel or res judicata, motion for disqualification of the Council for bias or prejudice, and requests for a continuance. The court found no abuse of discretion in the Council's evidentiary rulings. The court held that the judge failed to establish that the Council impaired his statutory right of confidentiality. Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 45-11f. The court rejected the judge's contention that the sole remedy for misconduct by an elected probate judge is for the electorate to deny the judge another term in office. Lastly, the court found no merit in the judge's contention that the Council's proceedings violated his right to procedural due process of law.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.
