Campbell v. Board of Education


No. 11507


Supreme Court of Connecticut


193 Conn. 93; 475 A.2d 289; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 567


March 1, 1984, Argued  
May 1, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Class action for injunctive relief, mandamus, and a judgment declaring the defendants' attendance and grading policies in violation of the General Statutes and of the state and federal constitutions, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield and tried to the court, Kremski, J.; judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a class action brought by plaintiff class against defendant school board in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Litchfield (Connecticut), the class sought injunctive and declaratory relief, mandamus, and compensatory damages. The trial court rendered judgment for the school board and the class appealed.


OVERVIEW: The class challenged the validity of the school board's policy that imposed academic sanctions for nonattendance upon high school students and alleged that the policy was both ultra vires and unconstitutional. The court held that: (1) the school board's decision to adopt uniform school-wide rules for academic sanctions for non-attendance was not ultra vires; (2) there was insufficient evidence to show that the policy operated in a manner that conflicted with state statutes governing compulsory school attendance or student discipline; (3) the policy did not jeopardize any fundamental rights under the state constitution; (4) the class failed to meet its burden of proof that the challenged policy had no reasonable relationship to any legitimate state purpose; (5) the class had not proven infringement of its liberty or property interest in a fair grading system; (6) no member of the class misunderstood the waiver policy or was deprived of a waiver because of ambiguity; (6) the class failed to show that the challenged program adversely affected a constitutionally protected right; and (7) the class failed to present a valid equal protection claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

509 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Cheshire Taxpayers' Action Committee, Inc. v. Guilford


No. 11415


Supreme Court of Connecticut


193 Conn. 1; 474 A.2d 97; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 571


January 5, 1984, Argued  
April 24, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a writ of mandamus compelling the defendant members of the Cheshire town council to put a proposed ordinance to a referendum, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, Smith, J.; judgment for the plaintiff Eric Schrumm ordering the issuance of a writ of mandamus and dismissing the action as to the named plaintiff, and appeal by the defendants to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant town council sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which ordered the issuance of a writ of mandamus compelling it to put plaintiff taxpayer's proposed ordinance to a referendum. The town council argued that the proposed ordinance exceeded the legislative power of the electorate and, therefore, the writ of mandamus should not have been issued.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer sought a writ of mandamus to compel the town council to submit a proposed ordinance to the electors of the town. The proposed ordinance would have required that each budget be submitted to the electorate and be approved by a majority vote of the electors voting at referendum. The district court ultimately issued a writ of mandamus compelling the town council to submit the proposed ordinance by initiative petition to referendum. The court set aside the district court's judgment and ordered a new trial. Specifically, the court held that prior to issuing the writ of mandamus, the district court should have considered whether the taxpayer's proposed ordinance clearly exceeded the power of the electorate, as contended by the town council. The court found that whether the taxpayer had a "clear legal right" to mandamus depended upon whether the proposed ordinance clearly exceeded the legislative power of the electorate because it was forbidden to compel the town council to perform an act that was contrary to law.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment of the district court and ordered a new trial.

Bakelaar v. West Haven


No. 11519


Supreme Court of Connecticut


193 Conn. 59; 475 A.2d 283; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 577


January 13, 1984, Argued  
April 24, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the named defendant from an order of the workers' compensation review division, brought to the Appellate Session of the Superior Court and tried to the court, Covello, Corrigan and O'Donnell, Js.; judgment directing an entry of judgment in accordance with the finding and award of the compensation commissioner, from which the named defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer challenged a judgment from the Appellate Session of the Superior Court (Connecticut), which affirmed a decision of the Workers' Compensation Review Division in favor of plaintiff employee.


OVERVIEW: The employee, a policeman, suffered chest pains while pursuing a suspect. While recovering at home, the employee suffered a heart attack. The employee filed a claim for workers' compensation. Along with the employer, the employer's current and former insurance carriers were named as defendants. The hearing officer found that the employee was entitled to benefits pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-433c, which provided special benefits for police injured in the line of duty, but remanded to determine if the employee was also entitled to benefits under the Workers' Compensation Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. ch. 568. One of the former insurers appealed, and the appellate court reversed and remanded for entry of the hearing officer's order. The employer appealed. The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment. The court held that because the former insurer was named in the judgment, it was an aggrieved party and had standing to appeal. The court held that although the Workers' Compensation Act was an exclusive remedy for employees injured in the course of employment, it did not preclude the employee from seeking benefits under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-433c.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment which reversed the Review Division's judgment, which had remanded the employee's workers' compensation claim to the hearing officer, and reinstated the hearing officer's judgment.

 

511 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jones


No. 10644


Supreme Court of Connecticut


193 Conn. 70; 475 A.2d 1087; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 578


February 7, 1984, Argued  
April 24, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of felony murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before McKeever, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, and appeal by the defendant to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) for felony murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the indictment was fatally defective because he was deprived of the unanimity required for conviction where the felony murder permitted the jury to convict if it found him guilty of either robbery "or" attempted robbery. The court rejected the claim because those two crimes were not mutually exclusive and thus the jury to convict had to all at least agree that defendant committed attempted robbery. Defendant claimed that evidence that was seized from his bedroom should have been suppressed. The search was reasonable, however, because defendant, a minor, lived in his parents' home, his father believed he had a right to enter his son's room, and both parents consented to the search. In addition, denial of a motion to suppress his confession was proper because defendant's refusal to answer specific questions did not require the police to cease all interrogation. The court also rejected the claim that the wrong insanity defense instruction was given and that this required defendant's conviction to be set aside. The court reasoned that the trial court gave a curative and proper jury instruction to which defense counsel did not take an exception to as inadequate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for felony murder.

Kinsella v. Jaekle


Nos. 12270, 12356


Supreme Court of Connecticut


192 Conn. 704; 475 A.2d 243; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 553


January 17, 1984, Argued  
April 17, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action by the plaintiff for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of proceedings of the Select Committee of the House of Representatives to consider impeachment of the plaintiff and for injunctive relief restraining further such proceedings, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the issues were reserved by the court, Satter, J., for the advice of this court; appeal by the defendants, on certification by the chief justice, from certain orders of the trial court.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed as moot.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff probate judge field an action against defendant Select Committee of the House of Representatives (committee) for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of impeachment against the probate judge and for injunctive relief restraining further proceedings. The superior court denied the committee's motion to quash a subpoena and the members sought an appeal.


OVERVIEW: The committee started an investigation of impeachment proceedings against a probate judge. The probate judge claimed that the committee lacked jurisdiction to institute the proceedings because a probate judge was not a judicial officer. The committee filed a motion to quash subpoenas claiming both lack of court jurisdiction over the subject matter of the action and immunity from compulsory court testimony under the speech or debate clause of the Conn. Const. art. III, § 15. The court dismissed the probate judge's complaint and the committee's appeal as moot because (1) the General Assembly had both civil and criminal jurisdiction in the superior court, (2) the committee's investigation was squarely within the legislature's jurisdiction under Conn. Const. art. IX, § 3, (3) the probate judge had not alleged the existence of egregious and irreparable constitutional violation to compel the superior court's intervention under its judicial power, (4) the General Assembly had the power to impeach the probate judge under Conn. art. IX, § 3, and (5) the committee's investigation into the probate judge's conduct was within its constitutional jurisdiction under the impeachment clause.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the probate judge's declaratory judgment action against the committee. The court also dismissed the committee's appeal of the trial court's denial of the motion to quash a subpoena.

 

513 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sanabria


Nos. 12344, 12114, 12345, 12346


Supreme Court of Connecticut


192 Conn. 671; 474 A.2d 760; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 565


November 8, 1983, Argued  
April 10, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] In the first matter, indictments in separate cases charging the defendants, Efrain Sanabria, Deborah Holder, Avelino Rivera, Patricia Richardson, David Worthington, Guillermo Ramos, Lorenzo Williams and Robert Madison, with crimes punishable by death or life imprisonment, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the defendants' motions to dismiss or for a hearing in probable cause were denied; the cases were combined by the court, Brennan, J., and the issues were reserved for the advice of this court.

In the second matter, information charging the defendant Jose Alberto Casul with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the grand jury indicted the defendant for murder; the court, Kinney, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss the grand jury, from which the defendant appealed to this court; the court subsequently denied the defendant's motion for a hearing in probable cause and that issue was reserved for the advice of this court.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed as moot.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Various defendants in criminal cases involving charges on crimes punishable by death of life imprisonment appealed from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut) and the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which had denied motions to dismiss or for hearings on probable cause based on Conn. Const. amend. XVII.


OVERVIEW: The cases involved all presented common questions requiring a determination of the effective date of Conn. Const. amend. XVII, which required probable cause hearings for persons held to answer on crimes punishable by death or life imprisonment. The key matters involved a determination of whether the amendment had been fully self-executing and whether the legislature had exceeded its authority in enacting the enabling legislation, Conn. Pub. Acts 1983, No. 83-210. The court found that: (1) the amendment was not fully self-executing, although it had eliminated the state constitutional grand jury provisions; (2) the legislature had partly exceeded its authority in defining the persons in whom the right to such probable cause hearings would vest; (3) the amendment only fully came into effect on the date of its enabling legislation, which finally repealed the statutory grand jury provisions and prescribed appropriate procedures for such probable cause hearings; and (4) all persons held on such crimes who had not yet been indicted by a grand jury on the enabling legislation's effective date were entitled to probable cause hearings.


OUTCOME: The court found that the amendment was not sufficiently self-executing to confer a right to probable cause hearing on the date of its certification, but instead became effective only on the effective date of its enabling legislation; further, the court dismissed the appeal of one defendant as moot.

 

514 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Reed


No. 10947


Supreme Court of Connecticut


192 Conn. 520; 473 A.2d 775; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 544


December 8, 1983, Argued  
April 3, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action seeking reimbursement for the care and maintenance of the named defendant while he was confined at Connecticut Valley Hospital, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, Fracasse, J.; judgment for the plaintiff, from which the defendants appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, an individual confined in a state mental hospital and his conservator, appealed a decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which entered a judgment in favor of plaintiff, the State of Connecticut, in an action by the State seeking reimbursement for the care and maintenance of the individual while he was confined at the hospital.


OVERVIEW: The individual was found not guilty of a murder charge by reason of insanity and was committed to the hospital. In finding for the State, the trial court relied on Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-321, which provided that the expenses of a person committed as a result of a criminal trial should be reimbursed just as the expenses of a civil commitment would be. Defendants challenged the constitutionality of § 17-317 on the ground that it arbitrarily and irrationally made those confined after an acquittal liable for hospital expenses while other persons similarly deprived of their liberty, such as prison inmates serving sentences, were not required to pay. The court agreed and declared § 17-317, as well as Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-47(h), invalid as violating the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment and Conn. Const. art. I, § 20. Applying the "rational basis" standard, the court found that there existed no reasonable ground to support the distinction in regard to liability for hospital expenses that the legislature had chosen to make between insanity acquittees and prisoners convicted of crimes.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that the trial court's decision was an error and set aside the judgment in favor of the State. The court remanded the case to the trial court with direction to render the judgment for defendants.

State v. Miller (Estate of Miller)


No. 11150


Supreme Court of Connecticut


192 Conn. 532; 472 A.2d 1272; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 545


December 7, 1983, Argued  
April 3, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action seeking reimbursement from the defendant for the support of the defendant's son confined at Whiting Forensic Institute, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the court, Covello, J., sustained the defendant's demurrer to the first count of the complaint; the second count of the complaint was tried to the court, Lexton, J., which rendered judgment for the plaintiff on that count; the defendant appealed and the plaintiff cross appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error in cross appeal; error in defendant's appeal; remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant executrix appealed a judgment of the Superior Court, Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), that was made in favor of the State for the cost of the decedent's past confinement since the date of the executrix's appointment as representative payee for her son. The decedent had been confined at a state institution for the mentally ill. He had been committed as an insane person pursuant to the criminal law, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-47.


OVERVIEW: The court's affirmance of the trial court's judgment was based on a declaration that the different burdens of proof between Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-47, which provided for criminal commitment, and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-178, which provided for civil commitment, violated equal protection of the law when it was taken into consideration that commitment via either statute gave rise to liability for hospitalization costs. Under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-47, clear and convincing evidence was required for civil commitment while pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-47 the State's had the burden to prove dangerousness for commitment only by a preponderance of the evidence. On a separate issue, the court ruled that it was capable of reaching the equal-protection issue in the case sub judice although the issue had not been raised in the trial court; this was because there was an exceptional circumstance in that the court had just announced a decision in a separate case that gave the executrix the new equal-protection right.


OUTCOME: The court ruled that there was no error on the appeal of the executrix and no error on the cross appeal of the State.

Fetterman v. University of Connecticut


No. 11333


Supreme Court of Connecticut


192 Conn. 539; 473 A.2d 1176; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 546


December 9, 1983, Argued  
April 3, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the constitutionality of the defendants' action in terminating her employment at the University of Connecticut, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Corrigan, J., granted the defendants' motions to dismiss the action and rendered judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.

DISPOSITION: Error in part; further proceedings.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff professor sought review of a decision of the Superior Court (Connecticut), which dismissed plaintiff's action for failure to exhaust administrative remedies against defendant university officials in a declaratory action seeking damages for the loss of salary and other benefits.

State v. Gabriel


No. 11360


Supreme Court of Connecticut


192 Conn. 405; 473 A.2d 300; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 530


November 3, 1983, Argued  
March 13, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with two counts of larceny in the first degree by receiving stolen property and with one count of larceny in the second degree by receiving stolen property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield at Bridgeport and tried to the jury before Herman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of one count of larceny in the first degree by receiving stolen property, and appeal by the defendant to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Fairfield (Connecticut), which convicted him of one count of larceny in the first degree by receiving stolen property in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-119(8), -122(a)(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's father had a scrap metal license and defendant knew how to operate the scale and calculate the value of items. Three men were in defendant's business, left to burglarize a home, and returned with certain jewelry items that defendant weighed for them. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court found that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-119(8) was not totally defective for not requiring any criminal intent for the offense of larceny by receiving stolen property. The court also found that the phrase, "receiving stolen property knowing that it was probably stolen," fulfilled the requirement of guilty knowledge and that the word "probably" did not lessen the State's burden to prove knowledge beyond a reasonable doubt. The court determined that the jury charge properly placed the burden on the State to prove all of the essential elements of the crime beyond a reasonable doubt and did not confuse the jury on the issue of possession. Because there was evidence from which the jury could have found that defendant retained stolen property valued over $ 2,000, the court concluded that the evidence was legally sufficient to support the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against defendant for larceny by receiving stolen property.

Tucker v. Maher


No. 11374


Supreme Court of Connecticut


192 Conn. 460; 472 A.2d 1261; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 537


December 1, 1983, Argued  
March 13, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in four counts for damages resulting from an alleged violation of law by the defendant in not making, on behalf of welfare recipients, direct payment of rent to the plaintiff landlord, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Purtill, J.; judgment for the named defendant from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landlord appealed a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which dismissed the landlord's action against defendants, the Commissioner of Income Maintenance and a former tenant who was a welfare recipient. The landlord claimed the Commissioner wantonly and wilfully refused to pay the tenant's rent directly to the landlord.


OVERVIEW: The tenant, a welfare recipient, owed the landlord rent. The landlord claimed that the law obligated the Commissioner to make direct payments of the tenant's rent to the landlord. The landlord brought an action against the Commissioner and the tenant for damages. The trial court dismissed the tenant from the case because she had not been served, found that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-82k was constitutional and prohibited the direct rent payments, and determined that the Commissioner did not purposely and intentionally discriminate against the landlord in violation of § 1983. On appeal, the court held that the trial court's conclusion was not clearly erroneous. The court agreed with the Commissioner's claim that the landlord could not prevail because he failed to comply with Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 390(d). Welfare recipients who were tenants and perhaps landlords had a legitimate interest in the outcome of the case and they were entitled to notice. Because all persons having an interest in the complaint were not made parties or given reasonable notice of the action, the trial court lacked jurisdiction to rule on the landlord's constitutional challenge or § 1983 claim.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's judgment that dismissed the landlord's claim against the Commissioner for wantonly and wilfully refusing to pay the landlord his tenant's rent. The court found the trial court erred by ruling on the merits of the landlord's constitutional and § 1983 claims. The court set aside those judgments and remanded with direction to dismiss the claims for lack of jurisdiction.

Bruno v. Civil Service Com.


No. 11446


Supreme Court of Connecticut


192 Conn. 335; 472 A.2d 328; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 523


December 9, 1983, Argued  
February 28, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for injunctive relief restraining the named defendant from refusing to appoint the plaintiff to the position of recreation superintendent of the city of Bridgeport, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield at Bridgeport, where the defendant Leonard L. Crone filed a cross complaint seeking a declaratory judgment determining whether the plaintiff's name was legally placed first on the employment list for that position; the court, Landau, J., rendered judgment for the named defendant et al. and for the defendant Crone on his cross complaint, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court; the trial court, Ryan, J., on remand by this court, granted permission to the plaintiff to file a substituted complaint on the constitutionality of durational residency requirements; the issues were referred to Hon. Kenneth J. Zarrilli, state referee, who rendered judgment for the plaintiff, from which the defendant Crone appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action brought by plaintiff applicant one against defendant civil service commission and defendant applicant two for injunctive relief from the commission's refusal to appoint him to the position of recreation superintendent, applicant two sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield at Bridgeport (Connecticut) in favor of applicant one in a counterclaim brought by applicant two.


OVERVIEW: Applicant one applied for the position of city recreation superintendent; he did not live in the city. Applicant one scored highest on an examination for the position and applicant two scored second highest. The commission did not hire applicant one because he did not meet a one-year residency requirement. Applicant one sought a declaratory judgment that he was entitled to the position. Applicant two filed a counterclaim seeking appointment. The trial court ordered that applicant two be placed first on the list, holding that applicant one was not qualified to take the examination and that he was foreclosed from attacking the constitutionality of the residency rule. The court remanded, holding that the record was deficient. On remand, the trial court held that the residency requirement unconstitutionally implicated applicant one's right to travel and that there was no compelling governmental interest to justify the law. On appeal, the court found no error. The right to travel, even within a single state, was a protected fundamental right. There were alternatives available to the commission such that the residency requirement was not necessary to meet the commission's interests.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

In re Juvenile Appeal (84-AB)

Rules Committee of Superior Court v. Freedom of Information Com.


Nos. 11081, 11082


Supreme Court of Connecticut


192 Conn. 234; 472 A.2d 9; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 512


November 9, 1983, Argued  
February 14, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the plaintiff Rules Committee of the Superior Court from a decision of the defendant commission ordering that the Rules Committee provide the defendant Raphael L. Podolsky with notice of and access to its meetings, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Bernstein, J.; judgment sustaining the appeal, from which the defendant Podolsky, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant citizen challenged an order of the appellate court (Connecticut), which reversed an order of the Connecticut Freedom of Information Commission requiring plaintiff Rules Committee of the Superior Court to provide the citizen with notice of and access to its meetings.


OVERVIEW: The citizen requested that the Rules Committee of the Superior Court provide him with notice of and access to its meetings. The rules committee denied the request. The Connecticut Freedom of Information Commission issued an order requiring the committee to provide the citizen with the requested information. The appellate court reversed and the court affirmed finding that rules committee did not fall within the purview of the Connecticut Freedom of Information Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-18a(a). Essentially, the citizen claimed that the rules committee was a "public agency" within the meaning of § 1.18a(a). The court rejected this argument finding that the played no role in the management of the internal institutional machinery of the court system. It was charged with the responsibility of formulating rules of practice and procedure that directly control the conduct of litigation. Accordingly, the court held that the rules committee did not perform "administrative functions" within the meaning of § 1-18a (a) and was therefore not subject to the provisions of the Freedom of Information Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order reversing the Connecticut Freedom of Information Commission's order requiring the Rules Committee of the Superior Court to provide defendant citizen with notice of and access to its meetings.

 

523 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Dukes v. Durante


Nos. 11425, 11479


Supreme Court of Connecticut


192 Conn. 207; 471 A.2d 1368; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 652; 49 A.L.R.4th 469


November 10, 1983, Argued  
February 7, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Class action for permanent mandatory injunctive relief under the Connecticut Uniform Relocation Assistance Act, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, Foti, J., which rendered judgment for the plaintiffs and found the defendants, on motion by the plaintiffs, in contempt of court, and appeal by the defendants to this court.

The appellants filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff low-income tenants filed a class action against defendant state housing authorities for permanent injunctive relief under the Connecticut Uniform Relocation Assistance Act (URAA), Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 8-266 through 8-282. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut) granted the injunction. The state housing authorities appealed.


OVERVIEW: The low-income tenants were forced to move from their apartments when the state housing authorities condemned the buildings in which they lived pursuant to a city housing code. The URAA established a policy of fair treatment of persons displaced by state and local programs of code enforcement and voluntary rehabilitation of buildings. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-266 of the URAA. Displaced person meant a person who moved because of a code enforcement activity or program of rehabilitation pursuant to the governmental supervision. Conn. Gen. Stat. 8-267(3) of the URAA. Because the generic term, building code, in the URAA included all codes dealing with building safety and health requirements, the city housing code used by state housing authorities that caused the low-income tenants to move constituted a code enforcement program, and therefore the low-income tenants were displaced persons within the URAA. The URAA did not violate Conn. Const. art I, § 1, because the URAA served a public purpose and there was a rational relationship to the different classification of the low-income tenants as those deserving of assistance.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the state housing authorities' appeal of a contempt order because it ultimately complied with the order, and no sanctions were imposed. The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the low-income tenants but remanded the granting of injunctive relief so that it could be clarified so as not to require the state housing authorities to engage in a building program and to give it time to provide necessary rehabilitation.

Common Condominium Assos. v. Common Associates


No. 11322


Supreme Court of Connecticut


192 Conn. 150; 470 A.2d 699; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 504


December 7, 1983, Argued  
January 31, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for, inter alia, alleged breaches of express and implied warranties as to the condition of certain condominium homes, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk at Stamford, where the court, Curran, J., granted the motion of the named defendant et al. to modify the prejudgment remedy and, on the plaintiffs' motion to modify the prejudgment remedy, denied, on the plaintiffs' further motion for clarification, specific reference to the reestablishment and full funding of an escrow account, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.

The appellants filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff condominium owners appealed a decision by the Superior Court at Stamford (Connecticut) granting defendant condominium developers' motion to reduce an ex parte real estate attachment and denying the owners' motion to enhance it by increasing the attachment amount and/or ordering the developers to set up an escrow account. The action alleged breach of warranties, negligence, violations of escrow requirements, and conspiracy to defraud.


OVERVIEW: Both parties brought motions to modify the prejudgment remedy, which was an ex parte real estate attachment, that the superior court had granted against the developers in the owners' action alleging breaches of express and implied warranties, negligence, violations of escrow requirements imposed on condominium developers via Conn. Gen. Stat. § 47-74d, and conspiracy to defraud in connection with the parties' condominium project. The court affirmed the superior court's grant of the developers' motion to reduce the amount of the prejudgment attachment and found that the superior court did not abuse its discretion in allowing the developers' expert to testify as to the condition of the condominiums and the estimated cost of repairing them. Under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-278l, the owners did not have a right to appeal the denial of their motion to modify their own previously obtained ex parte prejudgment remedy. Moreover, the superior court's pretrial determination that the owners were unlikely to meet the enhanced burden of proof on their fraud claim was not clearly erroneous, and so the pro tanto reduction in the prejudgment remedy was justified.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's order denying the owners' motion to strengthen the prejudgment real estate attachment remedy formerly issued against the developers and granting the developers' motion to diminish that attachment remedy.

 

525 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Perruccio


Nos. 11524, 11525


Supreme Court of Connecticut


192 Conn. 154; 471 A.2d 632; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 505


October 12, 1983, Argued  
January 31, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant, in the first case, with the crimes of injury or risk of injury to, or impairing the morals of, a child and sexual assault in the fourth degree; and, in the second case, with three counts of the crime of injury or risk of injury to, or impairing the morals of, a child; both cases were brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and tried to the jury before Hendel, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of injury or risk of injury to, or impairing the morals of, a child and sexual assault in the fourth degree in the first case; verdict and judgment of guilty of three counts of injury or risk of injury to, or impairing the morals of, a child in the second case, and appeal by the defendant in both cases to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error in the first case; error in the second case; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut), which in a consolidated trial convicted defendant of risk of injury pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21 and sexual assault in the fourth degree pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-73a(a)(1)(A). The trial court denied defendant's motion for reargument. The trial court granted defendant's motion for consolidation of the appeals.


OVERVIEW: The charges in the case stemmed from separate incidents involving defendant's sexual contact with two females under the age of 16. In the first case, the court determined that defendant's "touching" of the breast was an act directly perpetrated on the person of the minor and injurious to her moral well being. Defendant's claim that he had no fair warning that breast fondling was a prohibited act was without merit. Equally without merit was defendant's claim that he had been charged twice for the same offense in violation of the double jeopardy prohibition. Because sexual assault in the fourth degree and risk of injury each required proof of an element not required by the other, defendant's claim failed. Accordingly, no error was found in the first case. In the second case, the trial court committed error in denying defendant's request at trial for a jury instruction on consent. At the new trial, if the jury determined that consent was given, the trial court was instructed to dismiss the risk of injury charges since Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21 would then not be violated as applied to the particular facts of the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court in the first case. The court found an error in the second case, and remanded the case to the trial court for a new trial.

 

526 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Beccia v. Waterbury


No. 11084


Supreme Court of Connecticut


192 Conn. 127; 470 A.2d 1202; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 510


November 4, 1983, Argued  
January 24, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action by the plaintiff in quo warranto to determine the right of the defendant Edward B. St. John to the position of fire marshal, and application by the plaintiff for an order of mandamus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the court, Lexton, J., rendered judgment ousting the defendant Edward B. St. John from the position of fire marshal and denying the plaintiff's application that he be appointed to that vacated position, from which the defendant St. John appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff applicant brought an action in quo warranto seeking to oust defendant fire marshal from that position and an action in mandamus seeking to secure his own appointment to the position of fire marshal. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut) ousted the fire marshal from the position and denied the applicant's request that he be appointed to the vacated position. The fire marshal appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ousted the fire marshal from his position because he had been appointed through a process that concededly accorded no preference whatsoever to members of the local fire department, in direct violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-45. The fire marshal challenged the constitutionality of the statutory preference for members of a local fire department in the selection of a local fire marshal on the grounds that it created a privileged class in violation of Conn. Const. art. 1, § 1. The court disagreed and held that an act served a public purpose under art. 1, § 1 when it promoted the welfare of the State, or when the principal reason for the appropriation was to benefit the public. Counsel for the fire marshal conceded that the enhancement of morale in the local fire departments was a legitimate public purpose to be served by legislation, and that promotion of a fire marshal from within the local department was a rational method of enhancing morale. The court held that absent a particularized showing that any preference applied in this case would be irrational, the fire marshal failed to meet his heavy burden of proving Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-45 was constitutionally infirm.


OUTCOME: The court held that there was no error in the judgment that ousted the fire marshal from his position and refused to appoint the application to the vacant position.

 

527 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Eason


No. 11459


Supreme Court of Connecticut


192 Conn. 37; 470 A.2d 688; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 500


October 12, 1983, Argued  
January 10, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of injury or risk of injury to, or impairing the morals of, a child, and of sexual assault in the fourth degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the defendant entered a plea of guilty before Henebry, J.; the defendant's motion to dismiss the information was denied by the court, and the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which denied his motion to dismiss an information charging him with risking injury to a child, and with fourth degree sexual assault, to which he pleaded guilty.


OVERVIEW: The victim's mother entrusted the care of her daughter to defendant, who was her live-in boyfriend. When the mother returned from work, she noticed that her child's face and vaginal area were injured. An information charged defendant with risking injury to or impairing the morals of a child and of fourth degree sexual assault. After pleading guilty, defendant filed a motion to dismiss the indictment. The lower court denied that motion. On appeal, the court affirmed the lower court's judgment, concluding that the bill of particular conjunctive charges cured the defects in the information's charge. According to the bill, defendant with impaired the child's health and morals by beating her and subjecting her to sexual contact. Even if defendant did not admit to the latter, his factually supported plea was valid because Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21 permitted conviction for beating the child. Moreover, defendant's plea was knowingly, voluntarily, and intelligently offered after he was apprised of the consequences of doing so. Finally, § 53-21 was not unconstitutionally vague as to what was an impairment of a child's health in light of defendant's conduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's order, which denied defendant's motion to dismiss.

 

528 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Grievance Committee for Hartford-New Britain Judicial Dist. v. Trantolo


No. 10775


Supreme Court of Connecticut


192 Conn. 15; 470 A.2d 228; 1984 Conn. LEXIS 498


October 5, 1983, Argued  
January 3, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Presentment by the plaintiff alleging that the defendants had violated a certain disciplinary rule of the code of professional responsibility by advertising on television, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Hammer, J.; judgment reprimanding the defendants for a violation of that rule, from which the defendants appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action brought by plaintiff grievance committee, the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) reprimanded defendant attorneys for violating Conn. Rules of Prof. Conduct 2-101, which restricted advertising. The attorneys appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The attorneys launched an advertisement campaign involving commercials that were broadcast by an area television station. The grievance committee alleged that Conn. Rules of Prof. Conduct 2-101 prohibited legal advertising on television and that the advertisements were false and misleading. The attorneys claimed that the advertisements were protected speech. Finding that the attorneys did not violate the rule, the court set aside the judgment reprimanding the attorneys. The state could impose some restrictions on legal advertising but could not impose a blanket suppression of that speech. Because the rule did not address electronic advertising, it was ambiguous. The court found that the rule did not intend a blanket prohibition on advertising through electronic media. In order to satisfy constitutional standards, the rule had to be reasonably designed to prohibit only those statements that threatened a legitimate interest. Restriction of legal advertising to those who read published materials would deny nonreaders important information with no corresponding benefit to them or any other segment of society. The commercials were informative and in no way misleading or deceptive.


OUTCOME: The court found that there was error in the judgment reprimanding the attorneys for violation of a disciplinary rule regarding advertising, set aside the judgment, and remanded the case with direction to render a judgment for the attorneys.

State v. Vass


No. 11025


Supreme Court of Connecticut


191 Conn. 604; 469 A.2d 767; 1983 Conn. LEXIS 619


October 14, 1983, Argued  
December 20, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and kidnapping in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Hammer, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which convicted him of sexual assault in the first degree and kidnapping in the second degree.


OVERVIEW: The principle issue on appeal was the validity of defendant's identification. The court held that the trial court did not err in admitting the victim's photographic and in-court identifications of defendant over his objection that the photographic array was unnecessarily suggestive and that the identifications were unreliable because the victim testified that she had not previously seen the photograph, defendant failed to meet his threshold burden of proving the identification procedure was impermissibly suggestive, and the State was not required to conduct additional corroborative identification procedures. The court also held that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's request for a mistrial so that his attorney could testify as a witness to impeach the credibility of defendant's girlfriend because the cross-examination of the girlfriend and the testimony of an investigator elicited substantially the same impeachment as the proffered attorney's testimony and because defendant failed to articulate that the denial of his motion deprived him of a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

State v. Lovelace


No. 10910


Supreme Court of Connecticut


191 Conn. 545; 469 A.2d 391; 1983 Conn. LEXIS 624


October 7, 1983, Argued  
December 13, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and tried to the jury before Hendel, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London (Connecticut), which convicted him of murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a.


OVERVIEW: Defendant fatally shot his wife and confessed minutes later to the police. At trial, defendant alleged the defense of extreme emotional disturbance. The trial court ordered defendant to undergo two different psychiatric evaluations before trial as defendant told the first evaluator that he could not discuss the case. The second evaluator agreed with defendant's defense. The trial court ordered a third evaluation mid-trial because the first evaluator could not be called in rebuttal due to illness. Defendant appealed his conviction on the ground that the third evaluation was error. Finding no error, the court held that by pleading extreme emotional disturbance, defendant waived his privilege against self-incrimination and could not reassert it after the second evaluation. The court found that defendant did not claim harassment or undue burden and ordering the third evaluation so that the State could present rebuttal evidence was proper.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in defendant's conviction.

State v. McKnight


No. 9838


Supreme Court of Connecticut


191 Conn. 564; 469 A.2d 397; 1983 Conn. LEXIS 626


October 11, 1983, Argued  
December 13, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with five counts of the crime of robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield at Bridgeport and tried to the jury before Cioffi, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield at Bridgeport (Connecticut), which convicted him of five counts of robbery in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the trial court did not err in refusing to suppress out-of-court and in-court witness identifications. The circumstances in the case indicated that the identifications were reliable. Both witnesses had a sufficient opportunity to view defendant. The court further found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's motion for a two-day continuance to locate a witness. When considering the State's interest in an orderly trial process, as well as the potential for the jurors to place undo emphasis on the evidence, if admitted, the trial court did not violate defendant's due process rights by denying his motion to reopen the case after it was submitted to the jury. Finally, the court found that while the trial court's jury charge did not follow the specific language of defendant's request, it was correct in law, it adapted to the issues, and it was sufficient for the guidance of the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Southern Connecticut Gas Co. v. Housing Authority of New Haven


Nos. 9587, 11838


Supreme Court of Connecticut


191 Conn. 514; 468 A.2d 574; 1983 Conn. LEXIS 615


October 7, 1983, Argued  
November 29, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition, in the first case, for the appointment of a receiver of rents, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Dupont, J., rendered a judgment granting the petition, and motion, in the second case, by the named respondent to vacate that judgment and to dismiss the petition, also brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Dupont, J., rendered judgment terminating the receivership and dismissing the petition; appeal to this court by the respondent in the first case and by the petitioner in the second case.



DISPOSITION: No error in the first case; error in the second case, further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent housing authority appealed a decision of the Superior Court, the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which entered a judgment granting petitioner gas company's request for the appointment of a receiver of rents, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16-262f. The company appealed the superior court's second judgment, granting the authority's motion to vacate the previous judgment and to dismiss the gas company's petition.


OVERVIEW: Because the company was precluded from terminating service to residential dwellings, under § 16-262e, it was entitled to summarily seek a receiver of rents. The superior court found an outstanding indebtedness and, therefore, appointed a receiver for the rental income of the authority. While that was on appeal, the authority paid under protest the amount allegedly due to the receiver, although the appointment of the receiver was stayed pending the appeal. The superior court then terminated the receivership. The court held that: (1) the summary rent receivership proceedings did not require the filing of a companion civil action; (2) the authority's claim of immunity under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-65 made no provision for immunity for public housing authorities as to statutory liens, including rent receiverships, and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16-626f made no distinction between public and private ownership; (3) the legislature could constitutionally provide for a summary receivership proceeding; and (4) the receivership should not have been terminated because there were outstanding issues as to proper allocation of the moneys collected.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the superior court's judgment appointing a receiver of rents. The court found error in the judgment that vacated the prior judgment and dismissed the gas company's petition. The court ordered a new trial for the resolution of various points of contention between the parties.

 

533 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Caldor, Inc. v. Thornton


No. 11002


Supreme Court of Connecticut


191 Conn. 336; 464 A.2d 785; 1983 Conn. LEXIS 602; 36 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1832; 101 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P55,486; 35 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P34,641


March 29, 1983, Argued  
September 6, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application by the plaintiff to vacate an arbitration award, and cross application by the defendant to confirm the award, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Brennan, J.; judgment denying the application for an order vacating the award and granting the cross application for an order confirming the award, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employer appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut) that denied its application to vacate an arbitration award in favor of defendant employee and granted the employee's cross-application to confirm the arbitration award. The employee had brought an underlying administrative claim that alleged he was wrongfully discharged in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §53-303e.


OVERVIEW: The employee alleged that he could not observe his Sabbath because the employer required managers to work one Sunday per month. The employer claimed the arbitrators exceeded their power by finding in violation of § 53-303e because the employee resigned and that § 53-303e was unconstitutional. The court held that § 53-303e violated the Establishment clause. The parties freely submitted the disputed applicability of the statute's "discharge" language, and all other issues on the validity of the employee's claim under § 53-303e, to arbitration. The award conformed to this unrestricted submission and was therefore binding. Nonetheless, § 53-303e did not satisfy the three-part establishment clause test. Section 53-303e did not have a "clear secular purpose" because the term "Sabbath" used in § 53-303e(b) was not synonymous with a "day of rest." Subsection (b) conferred its "benefit" on an explicitly religious basis and had the primary effect of advancing religion. The authority granted to the board by § 53-303e(c) to resolve disputes arising under § 53-303e(b) violated the third part of the establishment clause analysis forbidding excessive governmental entanglements with religion.


OUTCOME: The judgment that denied the employer's application to vacate the arbitration award in favor of the employee was set aside because the statute under which the employer was charged violated the Establishment Clause. The matter was remanded to permit a judgment granting the employer's application to vacate to be entered.

Duguay v. Hopkins


No. 10796


Supreme Court of Connecticut


191 Conn. 222; 464 A.2d 45; 1983 Conn. LEXIS 593


March 9, 1983, Argued  
August 23, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries, alleged to have been caused by the negligence of the defendants, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the court, J. Healey, J., on motion by the defendant Gareth D. Thorne, commissioner of mental retardation, et al., rendered judgment dismissing the action, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured person sought review of a decision by the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut), which granted a motion to dismiss filed by defendants, State, school, and Commissioner of Mental Retardation (Connecticut), in the injured person's action to recover damages for personal injuries.


OVERVIEW: The injured person sustained injuries while he was a student at the school when a tractor ran over him while he was sleeping in overgrown grass. The injured person brought an action against the State, the school, and the Commissioner for injuries sustained. The State, the school, and the Commissioner filed a motion to dismiss, arguing that sovereign immunity applied and that the injured person had failed to get permission to bring the action, as required by Conn. Stat. § 19a-24 had to be very narrowly done. The court found that the statute expressly excepted the Commissioner from the application of sovereign immunity in civil actions. Since sovereign immunity had been waived with respect to the Commissioner, the court ruled that the action against him could not be dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's dismissal of the State and the school from the injured person's action and reversed the dismissal of the Commissioner, remanding the matter for further proceedings with respect to the Commissioner.

 

535 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Beckenstein v. Potter & Carrier, Inc.


No. 11061


Supreme Court of Connecticut


191 Conn. 150; 464 A.2d 18; 1983 Conn. LEXIS 587; 37 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. (Callaghan) 158


April 7, 1983, Argued  
August 16, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for the defective installation of a roof on a building owned by the plaintiffs, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Aspell, J.; the court rendered judgment on a directed verdict for the defendant General Aniline and Film Corporation, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff building owner challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which directed a verdict in favor of defendants, roofing installer and roofing material manufacturer, in an action for damages resulting from an alleged failure of the product on plaintiff's building and from an alleged breach of contract. The trial court held that plaintiff's actions were barred by the applicable statutes of limitations.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff building owner built a new manufacturing facility and contracted with defendant roofing installer to build the roof of the structure with materials manufactured by defendant roofing material manufacturer. The roof failed and plaintiff brought a products liability action against defendant roofing material manufacturer and a breach of contract action against defendant roofing installer. The trial court directed verdicts on plaintiff's claims in favor of defendants, based on statutes of limitations. Plaintiff appealed. The court affirmed, holding that the injury inflicted in the case was inflicted when the roof was completed. The court held that the contract between plaintiffs and defendant roofing installer was for the performing of a specific, definable act, i.e., the construction of a roof. At that time neither defendant had any continuing, indivisible responsibility for the attainment of an end result. Plaintiff's claim that the statute was tolled by the conduct of defendants in fraudulently concealing the fact that plaintiffs had a potential cause of action against them was without merit because the claim had not been specifically pled in response to the defense.


OUTCOME: The directed verdicts granted in favor of defendant roofing installer and defendant roofing material manufacturer were affirmed. Because the nature of the contract between plaintiff and defendant roofing installer was for a specific act without further provisions, the statutes of limitations for the products liability claim and for the breach of contract claim began on the date that the roofing construction was completed.

OVERVIEW: Both plaintiffs and the Commission sought review of the trial court's judgment modifying the Commission's prior order providing the requested employee sick leave records be identified only by using random numbers, based on the court's determination that the use of the employees' names would constitute an invasion of the employees' right to privacy. West Hartford Taxpayers Asso. v. Streeter

July 26, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a writ of mandamus or for a mandatory injunction to compel the defendants to call an election in the town of West Hartford on an initiative petition for an ordinance limiting increases to the annual town budget, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Hammer, J.; judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.

Heslin v. Connecticut Law Clinic of Trantolo & Trantolo


No. 10892


Supreme Court of Connecticut


190 Conn. 510; 461 A.2d 938; 1983 Conn. LEXIS 535


March 10, 1983, Argued  
June 28, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Application for an order requiring the defendant to comply with an investigative demand seeking information and documents about certain legal advertising and representations, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Borden, J., on motion by the defendant, rendered judgment dismissing the application, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) dismissed plaintiff commissioner's action that sought to compel defendant law clinic and defendant attorneys to comply with the commissioner's investigative demand issued pursuant to the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110a et seq.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner began an investigation into the law clinic's fee practices and its advertising under the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act. The commissioner claimed that the law clinic deceived consumers because it was essentially a front for a law firm. Consumers would seek legal help from the law clinic and then would be referred to the law firm. The commissioner issued an investigative demand on the law clinic. The attorneys refused to comply with the demand, so the commissioner initiated an action that sought to compel compliance. The trial court dismissed the commissioner's application finding that the regulation of attorney conduct was exclusively within the control of the judicial branch. On appeal, the court found that the Act authorized the commissioner's investigation of the law clinic and its attorneys. The court reasoned that the state rules governing attorneys' professional conduct and the Act could coexist. The Act was a statute of general applicability and could overlap with the state rules regarding attorney conduct.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment and remanded for further proceedings.

 

540 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Ivey, Barnum & O'Mara v. Indian Harbor Properties, Inc.


No. 11050


Supreme Court of Connecticut


190 Conn. 528; 461 A.2d 1369; 1983 Conn. LEXIS 536


March 10, 1983, Argued  
June 28, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for nonpayment of legal fees, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk at Stamford, where the defendants filed a counterclaim; the court, Curran, J., on motion by the plaintiff, rendered judgment striking the defendants' counterclaim, from which the defendants appealed to this court.

The appellants filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff law firm commenced an action to recover legal fees and disbursements from defendant clients. Defendants counterclaimed and alleged that plaintiff's attempt to collect interest violated the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110a et seq. Plaintiff moved to strike the counterclaim, which the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut) granted, and defendants sought review.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff law firm commenced suit against defendant clients to recover upon unpaid legal fees and disbursements. Defendants counterclaimed, alleging that plaintiff's claims for interest violated the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act (CUTPA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110a et seq. Plaintiff moved to dismissed the counterclaim, which the trial court granted and defendants sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that while CUTPA generally permitted a private cause of action, suits undertaken pursuant to CUTPA had to demonstrate some nexus with the public interest. The court found that there was no evidence that the instant dispute was established through advertisement or the public media or that plaintiff's billing practices were abusive or coercive. The court concluded that the dispute between the parties was a private dispute, thus CUTPA was not implicated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's striking of defendant clients' counterclaim that plaintiff law firm engaged in unfair trade practices in contravention of the state statute.

 

541 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Hartford Div., Emhart Industries, Inc. v. Amalgamated Local Union 376, etc.


No. 11752


Supreme Court of Connecticut


190 Conn. 371; 461 A.2d 422; 1983 Conn. LEXIS 533; 119 L.R.R.M. 2860; 99 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P55,411


March 4, 1983, Argued  
June 14, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to obtain injunctive relief restricting the defendants from picketing, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Kremski, J.; judgment granting injunctive relief and appeal by the defendants to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a union and its officers (union), appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which granted plaintiff employer's request for a temporary injunction and enjoined the union from participating in certain activities while picketing.


OVERVIEW: The union commenced a strike against the employer. The employer filed an action seeking, among other things, a temporary injunction and alleging that the union was engaged in unlawful conduct. The trial court granted the employer's request for a temporary injunction and placed limits on the picketing. With the exception of one paragraph, which the court ordered to be stricken because it was overly broad, the court affirmed the issuance of the injunction. The judgment was set aside, and the case was remanded so that judgment could be entered without the stricken paragraph. The trial court was not clearly erroneous in determining that unlawful acts had been committed and that the union actually participated in or authorized the picketing. The conduct of the picket line could not be considered peaceful, and there was no adequate remedy at law because only the issuance of an injunction could prevent the continuing injury. The employer satisfied its burden under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 31-114, 31-115, and the trial court was within its discretion in issuing the injunction. Except for the stricken paragraph, the injunction was not vague.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment that issued a temporary injunction against the union. The court remanded the case with direction to render judgment of the temporary injunction with the exception that a certain paragraph was to be stricken.

 

542 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Davis


No. 11248


Supreme Court of Connecticut


190 Conn. 327; 461 A.2d 947; 1983 Conn. LEXIS 529


February 9, 1983, Argued  
June 14, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of kidnapping in the second degree, of sexual assault in the first degree, and of robbery in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield at Bridgeport where the defendant pleaded nolo contendere before Ment, J.; judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield at Bridgeport (Connecticut), which denied his motion to open a prior judgment of conviction for second degree kidnapping, first degree sexual assault, and third degree robbery. The trial court had accepted his guilty plea and after a hearing on whether defendant qualified for psychiatric treatment based on an examination, he was sentenced.


OVERVIEW: An examination concluded that defendant did not meet the statutory criteria for commitment and the trial court denied his request for a continuance for a hearing on the issue. He appealed his sentence and moved the trial court to open the judgment based on violations of his due process rights. That motion was denied. On review, he questioned the report's failure to recommend probation and whether the failure of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-245(b) to mandate a full hearing was a capricious classification, making it unconstitutional. The court held that the trial court did not err in its refusal to grant a continuance for a hearing on the report because no constitutional basis was advanced and there was no statutory requirement that such hearing be held. The sentence imposed was not illegal. Therefore, the trial court's authority to open the judgment was limited by the application of Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. 934. As a result, the court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 17-244 and 17-245 did not create a liberty interest. Lastly, the considerations involved when a defendant was not going to be confined were totally different and justified the omission of holding any hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

543 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Roque


No. 10260


Supreme Court of Connecticut


190 Conn. 143; 460 A.2d 26; 1983 Conn. LEXIS 512; 39 A.L.R.4th 1158


January 13, 1983, Argued  
May 17, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with one count of the crime of rioting at a correctional institution and with three counts of the crime of assault in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the jury before J. Shea, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of rioting at a correctional institution, and appeal by the defendant to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review after the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut) convicted him, after a trial by jury, of the crime of rioting at a correctional institution, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-179b (1977).


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that he had been convicted of rioting on the basis of an uncharged statutory theory of criminal liability based on the wording of the statute, which he contended set forth nine theories of criminal liability. The use of nine verbs, in what defendant called the "moving or proscriptive clause" of the statute with the word "or" before "takes part in," showed with "substantial certainty" that the legislature intended the parts of the statute to be separate and not cumulative. The jury convicted defendant of rioting and acquitted him of assault. The court affirmed. Although nine separate verbs were used, their common meanings and their association with each other caused them to fall into two groups: those that covered the leaders or planners and those who followed them in the proscribed occurrence, whether it was organized or spontaneous. Defendant was convicted upon a constitutionally available theory of which he had notice, against which he was defended, and upon which his jury was instructed.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

 

544 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


New Haven Sav. Bank v. West Haven Sound Dev.


No. 10639


Supreme Court of Connecticut


190 Conn. 60; 459 A.2d 999; 1983 Conn. LEXIS 502


February 9, 1983, Argued  
May 10, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to foreclose a mortgage, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven before Callahan, J., who rendered a judgment of strict foreclosure; on motion by the plaintiff, the Hon. A. Frederick Mignone, state trial referee, rendered a deficiency judgment in favor of the plaintiff, from which the defendants appealed and the plaintiff cross appealed.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant debtors challenged an order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which, after a judgment ordering strict foreclosure, rendered a deficiency judgment in favor of plaintiff creditors.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the debtors argued that the trial court erred in utilizing the income approach to valuation because the subject realty was sold six months after foreclosure. The court disagreed, noting that, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-14, the issue of valuation was to be determined by the trial court. The trial court employed the income method of valuation, the approach primarily relied upon by all of the appraisers, including the debtors' witness. In determining valuation, the trial court accepted and rejected portions of each appraiser's testimony in an effort to reach a compromise between the conflicting evidence presented. Further, the trial court's valuation efforts were muddied because the sale was at a price inflated by atypical financing arrangements. Although a recent sale resulting from fair negotiations between a desirous buyer and a willing seller, neither under any undue compulsion to make a deal, would ordinarily be the most reliable indicator of fair market value, the extremely favorable financing obtained by the buyer and his limited liability combined to warrant the conclusion that the price did not fully reflect the consideration exchanged in the transaction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

545 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Varley v. Varley


No. 9729


Supreme Court of Connecticut


189 Conn. 490; 457 A.2d 1065; 1983 Conn. LEXIS 465


October 7, 1982, Argued  
March 15, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for the sale of certain real property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, N. O'Neill, J., rendered a final supplemental judgment ordering and confirming a sale of the property, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action brought by plaintiff ex-husband for the sale of a former marital home and division of the proceeds, defendant ex-wife sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which granted the ex-husband's motion for partition by sale and subsequently approved, accepted, and confirmed a committee's report and a proposed sale.


OVERVIEW: The parties were divorced and the ex-husband was awarded a one-half interest in the former marital home; the ex-husband had quitclaimed his interest in the home to the ex-wife during the parties' marriage. The ex-husband subsequently brought an action for the sale of the home and division of the proceeds. The trial court granted the ex-husband's motion for partition in accordance with the parties' stipulation. The home was sold at public auction to the ex-wife. The trial court entered a supplemental judgment ordering distribution of the sale proceeds. On appeal, the court found no error. There was no error in the entry of the judgment authorizing the sale of the property because the ex-wife's attorney stipulated to such authorization and the ex-wife was bound by the acts of her attorney. The ex-husband was not barred from reacquiring an interest in the home by virtue of language in the quitclaim deed whereby the ex-wife originally received the property; the deed language barring the ex-husband from claiming any right or title in the premises did not act as a bar to the future acquisition of an interest in the property from the decree incident to the parties' divorce action.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.
