Williams v. Bartlett


No. 10889


Supreme Court of Connecticut


189 Conn. 471; 457 A.2d 290; 1983 Conn. LEXIS 463


December 9, 1982, Argued  
March 15, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction restraining the defendants from engaging in any transaction affecting title to certain real property, to convey real property, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, where the defendants applied for a discharge of a notice of lis pendens which had been filed upon the bringing of the action; the court, Sullivan, J., denied the application, from which the defendants appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, partner and corporation, appealed a decision of the Superior Court of the Judicial District of Danbury (Connecticut) that issued a notice of lis pendens against them pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-325 and 1981 Conn. Pub. Acts No. 81-8 following an action brought by plaintiff limited partners. The partner and corporation asserted that § 52-325 was unconstitutional under the Fourteenth Amendment and Conn. Const. art. I, § 10.


OVERVIEW: Some limited partners brought an action against a partner and corporation in which they accused them of fraudulent misrepresentation and conveyance of real property. The trial court issued a notice of lis pendens against the partner and corporation pursuant to 1918 Conn. Pub. Acts No. 81-8 and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-325. The court refused to discharge the notice of lis pendens. Although the partner and corporation asserted that § 52-325 was unconstitutional under the Fourteenth Amendment and Conn. Const. art. I, § 10, the court disagreed. The court reached this decision by weighing the interests affected by lis pendens, the risks of erroneous deprivation, and the governmental interests involved. 547 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


In re Juvenile Appeal (83-CD)


No. 9972


Supreme Court of Connecticut


189 Conn. 276; 455 A.2d 1313; 1983 Conn. LEXIS 443; 38 A.L.R.4th 736


October 12, 1982, Argued  
February 15, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition by the commissioner of children and youth services for a temporary order of custody of the defendant's minor children, brought to the Superior Court for juvenile matters in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, M. Hennessey, J., ordered temporary custody of the children to the commissioner, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the mother of five children, appealed from an order of the Superior Court for juvenile matters in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which granted temporary custody of the children to plaintiff, the Commissioner of the Department of Children and Youth Services.


OVERVIEW: The mother's youngest child died suddenly. No cause of death could be determined at that time, but a pediatrician noticed some unexplained superficial marks on the child's body. As a result, the commissioner seized custody of the five remaining children. The juvenile court later found "probable cause" and, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-129(b), ordered temporary custody of the children to remain with the commissioner. On appeal, the court remanded the case. The court held that § 46b-129(b) was constitutional because, when it was read together with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-38a, as it had to be, it was justified by a compelling state interest and was narrowly drawn to express only that legitimate state interest. The court also held, however, that the juvenile court erred when it decided that "probable cause" was the standard of proof in a temporary custody proceeding. The standard of proof to be used in temporary custody hearings under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-129(b)(2) was the normal civil standard of a fair preponderance of the evidence. The court further held that the burden of proof was always on the state when it sought to remove children from the home.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the juvenile court with direction to set aside the orders of temporary custody.

State v. Avcollie


No. 10089


Supreme Court of Connecticut


188 Conn. 626; 453 A.2d 418; 1982 Conn. LEXIS 624


October 7, 1982, Argued  
December 14, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Cohen, J.; the trial court set aside the jury's verdict of guilty and rendered a judgment of acquittal; this court, on appeal by the state, set aside the judgment, reinstated the jury's verdict, and remanded the case to the trial court with direction to render judgment that the defendant was guilty and to impose sentence; on denial of certiorari by the United States Supreme Court, the trial court, Stoughton, J., rendered judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut), which, upon remand, convicted him of murder. The case had been remanded to the trial court following the State's appeal of the trial court's initial order setting aside the guilty jury verdict and entering a judgment of acquittal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for the murder of his wife. The court rejected defendant's claim that the trial court erred in its charge to the jury by instructing them that they should consider defendant's interest in the outcome of the case when weighing his credibility as a witness. The trial court was correct in not going beyond the scope of the remand and in refusing to hear juror testimony regarding the verdict.

549 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Luf v. Southbury


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


188 Conn. 336; 449 A.2d 1001; 1982 Conn. LEXIS 599


June 11, 1982, Argued  
September 14, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action by abutting landowners to recover from the defendant for its discontinuance of a public road, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where James H. W. Conklin II, administrator, estate of Francis H. Harris, and others sought damages from the defendant as co-plaintiffs; the issues were tried to the court, Lexton, J.; judgment for the plaintiffs, from which the defendant appealed and the named plaintiff et al. cross appealed to this court.

The appellees-appellants filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant town sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which awarded damages to each of appellee landowners for appellant's lawful discontinuance of an unimproved public highway.


OVERVIEW: When a residential village was developed a portion of the road in question was purposely left undeveloped. The residents of the village voted to discontinue all of the unimproved portion of the road. Appellee landowners, whose property abutted the discontinued road, contended that they suffered a substantial and material impairment of their legal access to the public highway system because of the discontinuance of the road and the lower court agreed. The court noted that both before and after its discontinuance, the road was not only unimproved but also impassable by vehicle. Contrary to appellees' contention, the court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 13a-55 was constitutional. Appellees also argued that the easement § 13a-55 preserved was so unworkable that there had been a constitutional taking of their right of access. The court stated that both before and after the discontinuance of the road, appellees had an unabated right to use that roadbed in its unimproved condition, or with whatever improvements they found it profitable to make, to get to and from their unimproved land. The court stated that the physical rights to traverse the road were unaffected by its discontinuance.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court, which granted appellee landowners' monetary relief after a road was discontinued, was reversed. The discontinuance of the road was not a taking and appellees retained an unabated right to use the roadbed in its unimproved condition.

Mozzochi v. Glastonbury


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


188 Conn. 276; 449 A.2d 173; 1982 Conn. LEXIS 592


June 9, 1982, Argued  
September 7, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Mozzochi v. Rogers, 1994 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 21674 (D. Conn., July 6, 1994)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the validity of the actions of a charter revision commission and the town council of the town of Glastonbury with respect to a proposed charter revision, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Kline, J., granted the defendants' motion to strike the action and the court, N. O'Neill, J., upon the plaintiffs' failure to plead over, rendered judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff electors of the town sought review of the order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) that granted defendant town council's motion to strike the action and rendered judgment for the town in the electors' declaratory judgment action to determine the validity of the actions of a charter revision commission and the town council.


OVERVIEW: Electors in the town sought to create a charter revision commission, but before they completed their circulation of petitions, the town council created a commission. After review of the commission's report, the town council voted only on the items that the commission had recommended favorable action on, not on every item and did not vote on the items the electors supported. The trial court struck the electors' action for declaratory judgment and on appeal, the electors argued that the proposals that the council did not vote on were then barred from being presented to the general electorate and that was contrary to the legislature's intent. The court affirmed and held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-191 provided no requirement for the council to accept or reject each item originally submitted to the commission. The court further held that the statute was clear and unambiguous and did not direct that all proposals that were submitted to the council by the commission must have been accepted or rejected.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the electors' declaratory judgment action.

Rodriguez v. Mallory Battery Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


188 Conn. 145; 448 A.2d 829; 1982 Conn. LEXIS 577


June 3, 1982, Argued  
August 17, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for fraud allegedly committed by the defendant in terminating the plaintiff's employment and in appealing an unemployment compensation award, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the court, Fracasse, J., granted the defendant's motion for nonsuit, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which granted the defendant employer's motion for nonsuit in the employee's action for alleged fraud related to the employee's termination and unemployment compensation. The sole issue on appeal was whether the trial court abused its discretion by entering a nonsuit after the employee failed to revise his complaint.


OVERVIEW: The trial court had strongly advised the pro se employee to obtain legal assistance and gave him an opportunity to do so and to revise a rambling complaint that did not comply with Conn. Gen. Prac. Book § 108. The court trial pointed out that the pleadings were not sufficient to support a judgment, that the employee had not followed the rules, and that the case would be dismissed if the employee did not take steps to change the situation. On appeal, the court held that while pro se litigants were given more leniency in the formalities of pleading and practice, the employee was still bound to follow the applicable court rules. The court declined to consider a claim that stated that the trial court action was unconstitutional under the first and fourteenth amendments, because the employee never briefed the issue in any way. The court held that in view of the employee's repeated failure to comply with the trial court's order to revise his complaint, the court could only conclude that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in granting the employer's motion.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the judgment of nonsuit entered by the trial court against the employee after he failed to revise his complaint.

Sands v. Sands

DISPOSITION: No error.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff husband appealed from a judgment of the New Haven Superior Court (Connecticut) that granted plaintiff's request for dissolution of marriage on the grounds of irretrievable breakdown, but that awarded defendant wife alimony pursuant to Conn. OVERVIEW: Plaintiff husband sought and was granted dissolution of his marriage with defendant wife on the grounds of irretrievable breakdown. Loda v. H. K. Sargeant & Associates, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]

188 Conn. 69; 448 A.2d 812; 1982 Conn. LEXIS 565

August 10, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action claiming title to funds in the possession of the named defendant, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford and tried to the court, Chernauskas, J.; judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; case remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff purchasers challenged the judgment of the Superior Court (Connecticut), which found in an interpleader action that plaintiffs had breached a contract of sale, and awarded damages, attorney fees, and costs to defendant realtor and sellers from plaintiffs' deposit.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff purchasers sought review of the trial court's judgment in an interpleader action that found plaintiffs had breached a contract of sale, awarded damages, attorney fees, and court costs to defendant realtor and sellers from plaintiffs' deposit. The court set aside the judgment and remanded for an award of damages and counsel fees to defendant realtor and sellers that addressed errors in calculating damages in order to put the parties in the position they would have been had the contract been performed. The court found that defendant sellers had waived a mortgage contingency clause in the contract, plaintiffs breached the agreement by not going forward with the purchase, defendants were entitled to compensatory damages, and it was within the trial court's discretion under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-484 to award attorney fees and costs.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment and remanded for an award of damages and counsel fees to defendant realtor and sellers that addressed errors in calculating damages because defendant sellers had waived a mortgage contingency clause, plaintiff purchasers breached the agreement, defendants were entitled to compensatory damages, and it was within the trial court's discretion to award attorney fees and costs.

Harwinton Drilling & Engineering Co. v. Public Utilities Control Authority


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


188 Conn. 90; 448 A.2d 210; 1982 Conn. LEXIS 566


March 12, 1982, Argued  
August 10, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction restraining the defendants from implementing a proposed telephone exchange, for an order nullifying a decision of the named defendant approving the telephone exchange, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield, where the court, Pickett, J., granted the defendants' motions to dismiss the action and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff business owners appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Litchfield (Connecticut), which granted the motion to dismiss of defendant Public Utilities Control Authority in the business owners' action for an injunction restraining the Authority from implementing a proposed telephone exchange and for an order nullifying the Authority's decision to approve a telephone exchange.


OVERVIEW: A department of the Authority created a single new telephone exchange for two towns that were covered by one school district. The new exchange eliminated toll calls between the towns. The Authority gave notice of its proposed change and held a hearing. The Authority created the exchange conditioned on a favorable response from the customers of the new exchange, which it subsequently found. More than a year later, the business owners petitioned the Authority to reconsider its decision. The Authority rejected the petition. The business owners filed the action and the trial court dismissed it. On appeal, the court found no error. The court found that the business owners had failed to exhaust their remedies available under the Uniform Administrative Procedure Act (UAPA). The court found that the business owners had adequate notice of the Authority's proposed action under the UAPA, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-177(b). The court found that the business owners alleged damages were adequately protected by the UAPA. The court concluded that without a showing of immediate and irreparable harm, the business owners could not institute an independent action to challenge the administrative decision.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the judgment of the trial court dismissing the business owners' action.

 

557 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Logan v. O'Neill


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


187 Conn. 721; 448 A.2d 1306; 1982 Conn. LEXIS 573


May 13, 1982, Argued  
August 3, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action in each case for a declaratory judgment determining the validity of a reapportionment plan, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the court, Corrigan, J., granted the defendants' motion to dismiss the first count in each case, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff voters appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which found in favor of defendant state officials, including the governor, the secretary of state, the treasurer, the comptroller, the president pro tempore of the senate, the speaker of the house, and the minority leaders of both houses, in an action to determine the validity of a reapportionment plan.


OVERVIEW: The voters brought separate declaratory judgment actions to challenge the validity of a reapportionment plan adopted by the general assembly. The cases were consolidated, and the trial court ruled that the voters did not establish a prima facie case that the plan violated the town integrity principle in Conn. Const. art. III, § 4. The voters appealed, and the court noted that they claimed essentially that the principle required the general assembly to adopt the number of districts of the house of representatives which most effectively minimized the cutting of town lines. The court found the voters' claim to be incorrect because it was based on a lack of understanding that the federal one-person, one-vote principle mandated equality of population to the extent practicable. The general assembly was not required by the town integrity principle to adopt a particular number of districts for the house. The court also noted that the problem with the voters' reliance on the existence of a better plan to demonstrate the invalidity of the adopted plan was that the purported demonstration depended upon the incorrect assumption that a plan was unconstitutional if there was a better plan.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's determination that the voters did not establish a prima facie case that the town integrity principle had been violated by the reapportionment plan.

 

558 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Arey v. Warden, Connecticut Correctional Institution


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


187 Conn. 324; 445 A.2d 916; 1982 Conn. LEXIS 527


March 3, 1982, Argued  
June 8, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Habeas corpus alleging unlawful imprisonment, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Henebry, J.; judgment dismissing the petition, from which the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which dismissed his request for habeas corpus relief. Petitioner claimed that the conditions in the segregation unit at the correctional institution in which he was incarcerated constituted cruel and unusual punishment within the meaning of the Eighth Amendment.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued that the totality of the conditions and procedures was so counter-rehabilitative and oppressive as to constitute cruel and unusual punishment. His specific claims were: (1) insufficient outside recreation, (2) insufficient showers per week, (3) consumption of meals in same cell where other bodily functions are performed, and (4) inadequate access to the institution's library. On appeal, the court held that did not consider the fourth specification, because although it involved fundamental constitutional rights, it did not implicate the Eighth Amendment. With respect to the remaining Eighth Amendment claims, the evidence did not support the conclusion that the specified conditions, whether viewed individually or in combination, added up to cruel and unusual punishment. Petitioner failed to establish that his health was jeopardized or adversely impacted, that there was insufficient hygiene or indifference to his basic hygienic needs, or that the food served was deficient in quantity, quality or nutrition. Petitioner's claim that the totality of conditions in the segregation unit offended the Eighth Amendment founds no support in the record and therefore had to fail.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Orsini


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Middlesex (Connecticut) convicting defendant of larceny in the second degree and conspiracy to commit larceny in the second degree. In a later proceeding the trial court found defendant guilty of being a persistent felony offender. Defendant filed a motion for reargument, which the trial court denied.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his right of cross-examination was unconstitutionally infringed by rulings sustaining objections to his questions about State witnesses' prior misconduct. Defendant also argued that his convictions were invalid due to improper venue, and that his conspiracy conviction was null due to a defect in an information. Defendant also argued that his conviction as a persistent felony offender was vitiated because the previous felony relied upon was a violation of Conn. Gen. The court held that: (1) the exclusion of evidence regarding the witnesses' prior misconduct did not deprive defendant of any constitutional rights; (2) under Conn. Gen. OUTCOME: Holding that there was no error in the judgment from the trial court sufficient to warrant a new trial, the court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Nardini


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


187 Conn. 109; 445 A.2d 304; 1982 Conn. LEXIS 505


February 4, 1982, Argued  
May 11, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of conspiracy to commit arson and of arson in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to a jury before Schaller, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty; the defendant's sentence was modified pursuant to an order of the sentence review division and the defendant was resentenced by the court, Kinney, J.; from the judgment resentencing the defendant the state, on the granting of permission, appealed to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a decision from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which modified defendant's sentence and resentenced him pursuant to the Connecticut Sentence Review Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 51-194 through 51-197 following his conviction for conspiracy to commit arson in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-48 and arson in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-111 (a)(1) and (2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of conspiracy to commit arson and arson in the first degree, and sentenced to a total effective sentence of 18 to 36 years. He filed an application to the sentence review division, which ordered that his sentences be served concurrently for a total effective sentence of 10 to 20 years. The State appealed pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-96, asserting that the Act violated the separation of powers and the judicial articles of the state constitution, and the trial court's assertion that it was bound by the mandate of the sentence review division. In response, defendant challenged justiciability, appealability, and the State's standing. The court affirmed the resentencing order, holding that the judicial department could vacate its judgment without violating the separation of powers provisions of the constitution. The trial court lacked any appellate authority to review actions of the sentence review division. Justiciability criteria were satisfied, the state's attorney general had a personal interest in criminal controversy on behalf of the State, and that the issue of the Act's constitutionality was appealable as it was raised before the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's resentencing on his convictions for conspiracy to commit arson and arson in the first degree.

Keogh v. Bridgeport


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


187 Conn. 53; 444 A.2d 225; 1982 Conn. LEXIS 501


February 10, 1982, Argued  
May 4, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for the death of the plaintiff's decedent, allegedly caused by the negligence of the defendants, and action for indemnity against the defendant city, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield at Bridgeport, where the court, Jacobson, J., granted the defendants' motion to dismiss and rendered judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff estate administratrix (administratrix) filed a wrongful death action against defendant fellow employees of the decedent (employees) and the decedent's employer (employer) that alleged that the employees and the employer were negligent and liable pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-555. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield at Bridgeport (Connecticut) granted the employees and employer's motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted the motion to dismiss the complaint for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and held that the remedy against the employer was provided by the Workers' Compensation Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 31-275 - 31-355 and that Conn. Gen. Stat. §7-308 barred the claims against the employees. The administratrix claimed that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-308 did not apply or was unconstitutionally vague, that the court should have overruled its previous holdings and permitted the action, that the construction of § 7-308 violated equal protection, and that the employer waived its right to assert defenses. The court held that § 7-308 applied and that it was not unconstitutionally vague because it was capable of a reasonable interpretation. The court also held that it would not overrule its prior holdings; therefore, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-293a did not supersede the immunity of a fellow employee provided by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-308. The court further held that § 7-308 did not violate equal protection, that it was immaterial whether the employer waived its defenses, and that it was unnecessary to resolve the administratrix's claim of error regarding the defenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Papa v. New Haven Federation of Teachers


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]

DISPOSITION: Error in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, teachers' association, appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which imposed contempt penalties after finding the teachers' association in contempt for violating a temporary injunction prohibiting the continuance of a strike.


OVERVIEW: The teachers' association contended that the contempt judgment was based on an invalid injunction, that the trial court erred in the civil contempt penalties that were imposed, and that the trial judge erred in denying their motions for recusal. The court held that the statute that authorized the injunction, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-153e, was constitutional because it did not violate the due process and equal protection guarantees. The court also held that the trial court did not err in the civil contempt penalties that were imposed. The court also held that the trial court did not impose penalties for days on which the individual teachers could not purge themselves of contempt. Finally, the court held that the trial judge erred in denying the teachers' association's motions for recusal because the trial judge improperly made public comments to a newspaper reporter about the teacher associations' pending proceeding in the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment of the trial court and remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Miller


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


186 Conn. 654; 443 A.2d 906; 1982 Conn. LEXIS 487


January 14, 1982, Argued  
April 13, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Wall, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut), which convicted him of assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant admitted that he shot the victim with a handgun but claimed at trial that either the handgun discharged accidentally, or that he acted in self defense. In seeking review, defendant claimed that the trial court erred (1) in charging the jury on the elements of self defense in two respects, on specific intent in two respects, and on the credibility of defendant's testimony, and (2) in denying his motion to prevent the State from impeaching defendant's credibility by introducing evidence of a prior felony conviction, and (3) in permitting the State to question defendant on cross examination about his prior gun ownership. On appeal, the court determined that the trial court properly instructed the jury in the statutory language on the charge and in stressing that the State had the burden of disproving self defense beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held that the credibility of the witness could be impeached by proof of prior convictions of felony crimes. The court found that defendant failed to properly preserve at trial the introduction of evidence about his prior gun ownership for purposes of appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant.

 

565 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kurvin


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


186 Conn. 555; 442 A.2d 1327; 1982 Conn. LEXIS 477


January 13, 1982, Argued  
March 30, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crimes of robbery in the first degree and with weapons in a vehicle and, in the second part, with being a persistent offender, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Cioffi, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of the crimes charged in the first part and appeal by the defendant to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction, which was entered by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), for robbery in the first degree with weapons in a vehicle and for being a persistent offender. Defendant challenged the jury instructions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction was affirmed on appeal. The court held that any error in the jury instructions did not warrant reversal. In instructing the jury on the elements of robbery, the trial court improperly failed to explain that the deprivation or appropriation intended must be permanent. However, defendant did not object to the omission, and the issue was not in dispute. The issue before the jury was whether the taking was wrongful; that the retention was permanent and intended to be so was undisputed, as evidenced by defendant's testimony that he told someone that he was going to keep the drugs and that he used half of the heroin that was taken. There was no reasonable possibility that the jury was misled by the trial court's charge. Defendant also claimed that the jury charge improperly referred to his interest in the outcome of the trial, but the court declined to consider the claim because defendant failed to object and similar constitutional challenges were rejected in the past.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's conviction of defendant.

 

566 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mason


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


186 Conn. 574; 442 A.2d 1335; 1982 Conn. LEXIS 478


November 10, 1981, Argued  
March 30, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield at Bridgeport and tried to the jury before Callahan, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, and appeal by the defendant to this court.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his murder conviction from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield at Bridgeport (Connecticut). Defendant claimed error in: (1) the denial of his right to effective assistance of counsel; (2) the decision of the trial court not to admit evidence concerning one of the deceased's convictions; and (3) the instructions to the jury on intent.


OVERVIEW: Defendant fired a single gunshot at the victim, which resulted in his death. The incident arose from a dispute concerning the right to run an outdoor dice game. Defendant did not deny the shooting, but he maintained that he had fired in self-defense and only with the intent to incapacitate. The court found no error and affirmed defendant's conviction. Regarding ineffective assistance of counsel, the court held that the record on appeal was inadequate to allow the court to decide whether the performance of trial counsel was neither reasonably competent, nor within the range of competence exercised by attorneys with ordinary training and skill in criminal law. Second, defendant assigned error to the trial court's refusal to allow him to introduce evidence concerning the victim's conviction for the unlawful discharge of a firearm. The court found that the exclusion of evidence concerning the conviction was harmless. Inclusion would have been cumulative. Finally, regarding the trial court's instructions on intent, the court held that the charge cured the otherwise ambiguous use of the word "presume," as it involved inference and presumption.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in defendant's murder conviction and affirmed it. As for defendant's challenge to the trial court's definition of "intent," the court held that the trial court's instructions on intent were adequate to explain the meaning of "intent" to the jury. Although it would have been preferable for the trial court to have read the statutory definition to the jury, it made clear that "intent" was synonymous with "purpose."

State v. Cosgrove


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


186 Conn. 476; 442 A.2d 1320; 1982 Conn. LEXIS 472


January 13, 1982, Argued  
March 16, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield and tried to the jury before Pickett, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Litchfield (Connecticut), which convicted defendant of the crime of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that the trial court: (1) erred in denying his motion to transcribe the grand jury proceeding; (2) erred in charging the jury; and (3) failed to take the appropriate steps to overcome the prejudice resulting from the State's tardy delivery of certain exculpatory material. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of conviction. The court found that defendant did not have a constitutional right to record or transcribe the grand jury proceedings, and thus, the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to transcribe the proceeding. In addition, the court held that the trial court did not err in charging the jury that "every person is presumed to intend the natural consequences of his acts." The trial court adequately clarified the use of the word "presumed" to preclude any misunderstanding on the part of the jury. Finally, defendant was not prejudiced by the State's tardy delivery of certain exculpatory material requested by defendant prior to trial. Defendant was granted a continuance to review the material, and the extreme act of dismissing the charges against defendant was not warranted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of the crime of murder.

Hill v. Blake


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


186 Conn. 404; 441 A.2d 841; 1982 Conn. LEXIS 465


December 1, 1981, Argued  
March 9, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the court, Henebry, J.; judgment dismissing the petition, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff detainee appealed an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), which denied his application for a writ of habeas corpus for release from the custody of defendant state trooper who arrested him pursuant to a New Jersey warrant that was issued after he was indicted for conspiracy to obtain, possess, and distribute a controlled dangerous substance.


OVERVIEW: The detainee was indicted in New Jersey for conspiracy to obtain, possess, and distribute a vast quantity of marijuana. The governor of New Jersey made an extradition request to the governor of Connecticut, who issued an extradition warrant for the return of the detainee under the Uniform Criminal Extradition Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-162. The trial court dismissed the detainee's application for a writ of habeas corpus and the court found no error. Although the detainee was extradited as a non-fugitive, the fact that the requisition papers inaccurately referred to him as a fugitive did not warrant his release because the requesting papers were deemed sufficient by Connecticut. The court found that the requesting papers were sufficient to charge the detainee with a crime under New Jersey law. The indictment adequately described the detainee's participation in a conspiracy to purchase and transport marijuana by his meeting with co-conspirators to plan the transport of the drugs and by his driving of the co-conspirators to the airport. Although the detainee did not participate in the final portion of the conspiracy, he was involved in agreement to violate the laws of New Jersey.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's denial of the detainee's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

 

569 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Seals v. Hickey


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


186 Conn. 337; 441 A.2d 604; 1982 Conn. LEXIS 455


November 5, 1981, Argued  
March 2, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained in a one-car automobile accident, alleged to have been caused by the negligence of the named defendant, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Berdon, J.; verdict and judgment for the plaintiffs as against the defendant John Errichetti Company, and appeal by the named plaintiff to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, father and son, filed suit against defendants, company and restaurant, to recover damages for personal injuries sustained in an automobile accident. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut), as permitted by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-216a, reduced the jury award in favor of the father and son by the amount that they had received in settlement with other alleged tortfeasors. The father and son sought review.


OVERVIEW: Section 52-216a authorized the trial court to deduct from a jury verdict the amount of money a party had received in settlement from other parties. The father and son argued that § 52-216a was unconstitutional because it did not provide any guidance to the court in giving it authority to reduce a jury verdict. The corporation and restaurant argued that it was unconstitutional because it denied them their right to a jury trial. The court found that § 52-216a gave the trial court authority to reduce an award in its discretion and that this limitation, in conjunction with case law that permitted a reduction in the verdict when the verdict and the settlement amount combined was excessive, provided a standard sufficient to satisfy procedural due process. The court found, however, that § 52-216a permitted the trial court to arbitrarily substitute its judgment for that of the jury and, as a result, denied the parties their constitutional right to have the extent of the damages decided by a jury. Because the unconstitutional portion of § 52-216a could not be severed from the remaining portions of that section, the court held that § 52-216a was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court set the judgment aside and remanded the case for a hearing regarding damages.

Baldwin Piano & Organ Co. v. Blake


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


186 Conn. 295; 441 A.2d 183; 1982 Conn. LEXIS 460


November 2, 1981, Argued  
February 23, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Motion by the plaintiff for an order holding the defendants in contempt for violation of a prejudgment remedy order, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, O'Brien, J., which found the defendants in contempt, and appeal by the defendants to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant buyers challenged an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which granted plaintiff seller's motion for an order holding the buyers in contempt for violation of a prejudgment order for replevy of a piano. The buyers argued that the court lacked jurisdiction to issued the order because the writ, summons, and complaint were not timely served as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-278j(a).


OVERVIEW: The buyers entered into a retail installment contract and security agreement with the seller for the purchase of a piano. When the buyers' defaulted in their payments and failed to pay the entire balance on demand as required by the default clause in the contract, the seller applied for a prejudgment remedy to replevy the piano. The court granted the application; however the buyers refused entry into their home to allow the sheriff to replevy the piano. The trial court granted the seller's motion for an order holding the buyers in contempt. On appeal, the court held that: 1) although the record had not shown whether the sheriff attempted to serve the writ, summons, and complaint in the matter, it was clear that the writ, summons, and complaint were never served; and 2) as the trial court failed to address the jurisdictional issue raised by the buyers' motion to dismiss, which alleged that the writ, summons, and complaint had not been served on them within 90 days as required by § 52-278j(a), it erred in granting the seller's motion for contempt.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment of the trial court that found the buyers in contempt for violation of a prejudgment remedy order in the seller's action for recovery of a piano sold to the buyers. The court remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

 

571 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pina


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


186 Conn. 261; 440 A.2d 967; 1982 Conn. LEXIS 445


January 12, 1982, Argued  
February 9, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of attempted murder, attempted robbery in the first degree, and carrying a pistol on his person without a permit, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield at Bridgeport and tried to the jury before Levister, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of conviction from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield at Bridgeport (Connecticut), for the crimes of attempted murder, attempted robbery in the first degree, and carrying a pistol without a permit. Defendant's appeal claimed only that the trial court gave an invalid instruction to the jury on intent.


OVERVIEW: Defendant fled the scene of a failed robbery attempt and was chased by a police officer. During an exchange of gunfire both the police officer and defendant were wounded. Defendant admitted the attempted robbery and the fact that he fired at the police officer, but claimed he had no intention to kill. The trial court's instructions on intent included a statement that every person was presumed to intend the natural consequences of his act. In his challenge to the instruction, defendant relied upon on a decision of the United States Supreme Court, which found a similar instruction was invalid because it violated due process rights in that a reasonable jury could interpret the instruction as a burden shifting presumption. The court pointed out that the use of the word "presume" did not itself render an instruction invalid. It was the lack of qualifying instructions as to the legal effect of the presumption, that made it possible for a reasonable jury to interpret the use of the word "presume" in an unconstitutional manner. The instruction in defendant's case was valid because it contained elaborate and precise language, which cured the otherwise ambiguous use of "presume."


OUTCOME: The court found no error.

 

572 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Shaw


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


186 Conn. 45; 438 A.2d 872; 1982 Conn. LEXIS 429


November 4, 1981, Argued  
January 12, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crime of risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before A. Armentano, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) for risk of injury to a child under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(1977).


OVERVIEW: A six-year-old boy told his mother that a man sexually molested him. The boy allegedly followed the man into his house after being invited in. The boy described details of the room where the incident took place and he pointed out the apartment to detectives, who defendant voluntarily let in. After placing defendant under arrest, one officer followed him into a back room to get shoes. His observations corroborated those of the victim. On appeal, the court affirmed the lower court's conviction of defendant for risk of injury to a child, concluding that an officer was constitutionally permitted to accompany defendant to another part of his apartment to forestall his access to weapons or to prevent his escape. That was so because defendant was under arrest and he voluntarily went into the other room. Similarly, there was no error in the lower court's refusal to charge the jury on fourth degree sexual assault because that was not a lesser-included offense of risk of injury to a child. The lesser offense required proof of an element that the greater did not. Accordingly, defendant was not entitled to the requested instruction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's conviction of defendant for risk of injury to a child.

Turcio v. Manson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


186 Conn. 1; 439 A.2d 437; 1982 Conn. LEXIS 423


October 14, 1981, Argued  
January 5, 1982, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, N. Levine, J.; judgment dismissing the petition, from which the plaintiff appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a decision from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which dismissed his petition for a writ of habeas corpus following his conviction for felony murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54c, assault in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59(a)(1), and robbery in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(1). Petitioner asserted that the trial court erred in its jury instructions.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner failed to raise the issue of improper jury instructions on direct appeal but initiated it in his habeas corpus action subsequent to the conclusion of his direct appeal. The court, however, agreed with the trial court's conclusion that petitioner's failure to raise the issue on appeal did not constitute a deliberate bypass of the appellate process. The petitioner claimed that the instructions given to the jury constituted error entitling him to a new trial. The commissioner argued that the challenged instructions contained other language that was sufficiently precise or elaborate to prevent the jury from applying the instructions in an unconstitutional manner. The court granted the writ of habeas corpus and set aside the petitioner's convictions, holding that the instructions on intent in all three counts were invalid because the language expressly used in the challenged and erroneously conclusive and presumptive instructions on the first count was incorporated by reference in the instructions on the other two counts and was repeated to the jury in response to a question regarding intent after deliberation had begun.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the superior court's judgment and remanded the case with directions to grant the writ of habeas corpus, set aside petitioner's convictions, and order a new trial.

Weil v. Miller


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


185 Conn. 495; 441 A.2d 142; 1981 Conn. LEXIS 624

November 17, 1981, Decided

DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which entered a judgment for defendant in plaintiff's action seeking a declaratory judgment that defendant's judgment against plaintiff was void, for injunctive relief from that judgment, for an order of mandamus requiring defendant to remove an attachment, and for an order releasing plaintiff's property.


OVERVIEW: Previously, plaintiff received a letter from defendant's attorney threatening a lawsuit. Defendant then initiated her action by an attachment and by a writ served on plaintiff through abode service at his place of residence. Stat. § 52-57, defendant denied having received the writ. A default judgment was entered against plaintiff. Plaintiff argued that defendant's delay in seeking execution on her judgment until more than four months had elapsed was an artful maneuver designed to keep plaintiff from taking advantage of the four-month period for the opening of judgments provided by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-212a. On appeal, the court held that plaintiff had not sustained his heavy burden of proof to establish the unconstitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-57. 576 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Just


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


185 Conn. 339; 441 A.2d 98; 1981 Conn. LEXIS 614


June 2, 1981, Argued  
August 18, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information in three counts charging the defendant with the crime of kidnapping in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield at Bridgeport and tried to the jury before Zarrilli, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court, Fairfield County (Connecticut), convicting him of kidnapping in the first degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-92(a)(2)(B).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of kidnapping in the first degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-92(a)(2)(B). Defendant appealed, arguing that the evidence did not establish his guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. The court ruled that the test which determined whether the evidence was sufficient to sustain a verdict was whether the jury could have reasonably concluded, upon the facts established and the reasonable inferences drawn therefrom, that the cumulative effect of the evidence was sufficient to justify the verdict of guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. Further, the court held that each essential element of the crime charged must be established by proof beyond a reasonable doubt. Also, the court found that although it was within the province of the jury to draw reasonable, logical inferences from the facts proven, they could not resort to speculation and conjecture. The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant, concluding that the evidence was sufficient to establish defendant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant was affirmed.

 

577 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gordon


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


185 Conn. 402; 441 A.2d 119; 1981 Conn. LEXIS 618


June 9, 1981, Argued  
August 18, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the jury before Driscoll, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.

The appellee filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions, after a jury trial, from the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) for sexual assault in the first degree and robbery in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: An assailant threatened the victim with a knife during the sexual assault. After defendant was convicted of sexual assault in the first degree and robbery in the first degree, he appealed. The court reversed and set aside the convictions for a new trial. The totality of the circumstances did not support the reliability of the victim's station house identification of defendant as her assailant. The circumstances did not reveal a need for a one man show-up with its attendant suggestiveness. There was no danger that the opportunity for an identification would have been lost unless a speedy show-up was held. The show-up was therefore unnecessarily suggestive. The corrupting effect of the suggestive procedure outweighed the factors favoring finding the identification reliable. The admission of the identification violated defendant's constitutional rights to due process. Sound judicial policy required reversal whenever the erroneous admission of an unnecessarily suggestive and unreliable identification violated constitutional rights. The tainted evidence included all the identifications of defendant by the only eyewitness to the crime, the victim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and set aside defendant's convictions for sexual assault in the first degree and robbery in the first degree and ordered a new trial.

 

578 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Johnson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


185 Conn. 163; 440 A.2d 858; 1981 Conn. LEXIS 597


June 4, 1981, Argued  
August 4, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information in four counts charging the defendant with the crimes of attempted murder, kidnapping in the second degree, robbery in the first degree, and sexual assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Burns, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, and appeal by the defendant to this court.

The appellant and the appellee filed motions for reargument which were denied.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which was entered on a jury verdict convicting him of attempted murder, kidnapping in the second degree, robbery in the first degree, and sexual assault in the first degree. Defendant claimed error in the trial court's instructions to the jury on the element of intent.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in connection with the sexual assault of a female victim and his act of throwing her over a bridge railing. The trial court gave the jurors a general instruction stating that a person's intention may be inferred from his conduct and every person was "conclusively presumed" to intend the natural and necessary consequences of his act. The court affirmed the judgment in part and set aside the judgment in part, and a new trial was ordered. The court held that the trial court's instructions to the jury in regard to the offenses of attempted murder and robbery were invalid because they contained an express conclusive presumption. Such a presumption denied an accused of a fair trial by failing to delineate the State's burden of proof on the element of intent and by directing the jury to find against him on that element. The trial court's specific instructions for the offenses of kidnapping and sexual assault did not incorporate and cured the invalid general instruction. Further, the trial court's action of having defendant removed from the courtroom due to disruptive behavior did not deny his right of self-representation under Conn. Const. art. I, § 8.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction as to the offenses of kidnapping in the second degree and sexual assault in the third degree. The court set aside defendant's convictions as to the offenses of attempted murder and robbery in the first degree, and a new trial was ordered.

State v. Lloyd


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


185 Conn. 199; 440 A.2d 867; 1981 Conn. LEXIS 598


June 12, 1981, Argued  
August 4, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information in four counts charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the second degree, injury or risk of injury to the morals of a minor, attempt to promote prostitution, and permitting prostitution, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Stodolink, J., accepted the state's nolle prosequi and denied the defendant's motions to dismiss, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which accepted the state's nolle prosequi and denied defendant's motion to dismiss on speedy trial grounds charges of sexual assault in the second degree, injury or risk of injury to the morals of a minor, attempting to promote prostitution, and permitting prostitution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with various crimes and on the morning of jury selection the State filed a nolle prosequi. Defendant objected on speedy trial grounds and filed a motion to dismiss the charges. The trial court denied his motion and granted the nolle. Defendant challenged the decision, and the court affirmed. Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-46 the State made a sufficient showing that a material witness was disabled because a physician had determined that her participation in a criminal trial would have caused her to revert to a psychotic state. The trial court was not required to receive evidence on the matter to determine the accuracy of the representation or decide whether the witness was truly disabled. Good faith disagreements about what constituted disability did not demonstrate a manifest abuse of prosecutorial discretion. The trial court properly decided defendant motion to dismiss regarding his speedy trial rights, which was an appealable order. The court found that his speedy trial rights were not violated because he failed to show prejudice to his defense and the 22-month delay was not sufficient for a finding of unconstitutional delay.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the entry of the nolle prosequi and the denial of defendant's motion to dismiss the various charges against him on speedy trial grounds.

DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Westport Planning and Zoning Commission appealed a decision from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield at Bridgeport (Connecticut), which sustained plaintiff developer's appeal from the commission denial of his application for site plan approval and ordered affirmative relief for the developer.


OVERVIEW: The developer applied to the commission for site plan approval to convert an abandoned gas station into an office building. The commission denied his application. The developer appealed the decision to the trial court pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8. The trial court sustained the appeal and ordered affirmative relief for the developer. Moscone v. Manson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


185 Conn. 124; 440 A.2d 848; 1981 Conn. LEXIS 595


June 11, 1981, Argued  
July 28, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Habeas corpus alleging unlawful imprisonment, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, O'Donnell, J.; judgment for the petitioner, and appeal by the defendant to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant corrections commissioner sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which granted petitioner prisoner's habeas corpus petition and ordered the calculation of his statutory good time credits under the law in effect at the time of his resentencing, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-7a, rather than that at the time of his first sentencing, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-7.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was originally sentenced on July 19, 1974, for rape. On appeal, his conviction was set aside and the case was remanded for new trial. Thereafter, the prisoner pled guilty to the same offense, and was, on April 12, 1977, resentenced. The commissioner calculated the prisoner's sentence as if it had commenced July 19, 1974. On appeal, the commissioner argued that the opening words of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-38(c) require that, for all purposes, and not just in relation to time-served credits, a resentence shall be calculated as if it had commenced at the time the vacated sentence was commenced. The trial court refused to accord so expansive a reading to § 53a-38, and upon review, the court agreed with the trial court's interpretation. The determination of statutory good time credits depended upon the date of the prisoner's valid sentence in relation to the provisions of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 18-7, 18-7a. The operative date for the prisoner's sentence, under §§ 18-7, 18-7a, was April 12, 1977. The prisoner was therefore entitled to good time credits according to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-7a.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of the prisoner's petition for a writ of habeas corpus, as well as its calculation of the prisoner's good time credits.

Sentner v. Board of Trustees


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


184 Conn. 339; 439 A.2d 1033; 1981 Conn. LEXIS 548


March 11, 1981, Argued  
June 9, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a mandatory injunction directing the defendant board to continue the plaintiff's employment with tenure, and for back pay, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, O'Brien, J.; judgment reinstating the plaintiff with tenure, and appeal by the defendant to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant board of trustees appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court, Hartford-New Britain district (Connecticut), which ordered the board to reinstate plaintiff teacher with tenure.


OVERVIEW: The teacher brought a complaint against the board seeking to continue his employment and seeking back pay. The trial court granted his request on the ground that the board had acted on the basis of insufficient evidence. The board appealed, arguing sovereign immunity and sufficiency of the evidence. The court affirmed, holding that the teacher was entitled to a hearing under the Due Process Clause of the United States Constitution before he was terminated and that sovereign immunity did not apply because the teacher had raised a constitutional issue. It was proper for the trial court to grant prospective injunctive relief because the trial court avoided undue interference with governmental functions. The teacher was tenured based on the board's personnel policies and the teacher's seven years of service. The trial court's conclusion that the teacher's years of service at another community college counted toward his tenure was not clearly erroneous because the board pointed to no evidence to show otherwise. Because the teacher was tenured, the board's dismissal procedures applied, and the board did not argue that it had cause for the dismissal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the teacher.

State v. Simmat


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


184 Conn. 222; 439 A.2d 915; 1981 Conn. LEXIS 518


April 9, 1981, Argued  
May 12, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with escape from a correctional institution, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Shea, J.; judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Tolland (Connecticut), which found him guilty of escape from a correctional institution in the first degree based on his failure to return from an authorized furlough in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-169(a)(3).


OVERVIEW: Defendant failed to return from furlough of his sentence to a term of life imprisonment for the crime of murder in the second degree. On appeal, he asserted that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-169(a)(3) was unconstitutional because it violated the Equal Protection and Due Process Clauses of the U.S. Constitution and that the superior court erred in denying his motions for discovery and for a delay in trial. The court found that the right to a furlough, granted by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-101a, was a matter of legislative grace rather than a fundamental right, which required rational basis review. The decision of the legislature to treat a failure to return from furlough as an escape had a rational basis. Defendant's argument under the Due Process Clause did not differ substantively from his equal protection argument. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by refusing to postpone defendant's trial pending the resolution of federal charges against defendant.


OUTCOME: The court found no error.
