State v. Stankowski


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


184 Conn. 121; 439 A.2d 918; 1981 Conn. LEXIS 519


December 3, 1980, Argued  
May 12, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex and tried to the jury before Naruk, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex (Connecticut) denied defendant's motions for acquittal and for a new trial, defendant challenged the trial court's judgment, which convicted him, after a jury trial, of murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction of murder. The court held that the evidence in the prosecution for murder, following the shooting of a victim by defendant with a shotgun, supported the finding that defendant did not "like" the victim, that defendant deliberately obtained shells and loaded the shot gun, and that defendant deliberately shot the victim. Thus, defendant's conviction was sustained; the record in the prosecution for murder showed that defendant was neither subjected to verbal questioning by police officers prior to the giving of the Miranda warnings, nor to conduct by the officers designed to elicit incriminating utterances from defendant. Thus, defendant's statements were not inadmissible merely because they were uttered prior to the time he was given the Miranda warnings; and the instruction, which included a charge to the effect that the jury pay proper respect to each other's opinions, adequately apprised the jurors of their individual responsibility both to reconsider their opinion, and to reach his or her own conclusion, and not merely to acquiesce to the conclusion of others. Thus, such charge, when read as a whole, was not prejudicial to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court found that no error was committed by the trial court, which convicted defendant, after a jury trial, of murder.

 

586 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


In re Juvenile Appeal


Docket No. 9268


Supreme Court of Connecticut


184 Conn. 157; 439 A.2d 958; 1981 Conn. LEXIS 527


January 8, 1981, Argued  
May 12, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition by the plaintiff for an order adjudging the defendant a delinquent, brought to the Superior Court for Juvenile Matters in the judicial district of Fairfield at Bridgeport and tried to the court, Glass, J.; judgment adjudging the defendant to be a delinquent, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment the Superior Court for Juvenile Matters, Judicial District of Fairfield at Bridgeport (Connecticut), that adjudicated him delinquent for causing physical injury to two people. The crime was defined by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-61. Defendant claimed that the defenses of duress and necessity applied.


OVERVIEW: At the time of the assaults, defendant was confined, and the assaults were committed on two youth-service officers. Defendant contended that the conditions and circumstances of his confinement were a defense. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-14 provided the defense of duress. The defense of necessity was not codified. These defenses were not available where there was a reasonable, legal alternative to violating the law: a chance both to refuse to do the criminal act and also to avoid the threatened harm. The court ruled that these defenses did not apply here. There was no indication that defendant had ever made an attempt to use administrative or judicial means to address the allegedly coercive conditions of detention or that the conditions of his confinement or situation were such so as to excuse. The court also rejected the contention that an illegal confinement was a defense. The court held that an illegal confinement was not a defense in either a criminal or juvenile-delinquency context to the crimes of assault on a detention officer and escape. Equally unavailing to defendant was his contention that hyperactive syndrome and epilepsy negated the element of intent to commit the assaults.


OUTCOME: Ruling against defendant, the court found no error.

 

587 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Brunswick Corp. v. Liquor Control Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


184 Conn. 75; 440 A.2d 792; 1981 Conn. LEXIS 514


February 4, 1981, Argued  
May 5, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision of the defendant commission denying the plaintiff's application for a liquor permit, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, Berdon, J.; judgment ordering the defendant commission to grant the application, from which the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Liquor Control Commission challenged a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut) ordering the commission to approve plaintiff company's application for a liquor permit, after the commission had denied the permit.


OVERVIEW: The company operated a bowling alley where there would be no prohibition against the sale of beer by a duly licensed druggist, hotel, package store, or by certain other establishments. The company applied to the commission for a permit to sell beer in its bowling alley. The commission rejected the application on the basis that only beer could be sold in that district and that under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 30-15, 30-37 the only permit which could be issued to a bowling alley was one for the sale of all alcoholic beverages. The company thereupon sought a declaratory ruling by the commission as to whether the commission could, under the statutes, issue a bowling establishment permit limited to the sale of beer only. On appeal from a ruling in favor of the company, the court held that the legislature could rationally make distinctions among establishments based upon the types of activities conducted there, for the purpose of regulating the sale and consumption of alcoholic beverages.


OUTCOME: The judgment in the company's favor was set aside and the case was remanded with direction to dismiss the appeal and to confirm the commission's decision.

 

588 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Manchester Envtl. Coalition v. Stockton


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


184 Conn. 51; 441 A.2d 68; 1981 Conn. LEXIS 515; 12 ELR 20650


December 11, 1980, Argued  
May 5, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction restraining the defendants from approving the development of a project which allegedly would contribute to air pollution, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Hull, J.; judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court and the defendants cross appealed.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizens appealed a decision by Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which denied their action for an injunction restraining defendants, who were a corporation, a municipality, and the chairman of a city planning commission, from approving a development project that allegedly would have increased air pollution. Defendants cross-appealed the finding that plaintiffs had standing.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff citizens brought an action under the Connecticut Environmental Protection Act of 1971 (act), Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 22a-14 to -20 (1971), to enjoin defendants, who were a corporation, a municipality, and the chairman of a city planning commission, from approving a project that allegedly would have contributed to local air pollution. The court reversed a judgment in defendants' favor and found that plaintiffs did not need to prove any pollution, impairment, or environmental destruction in order to have standing and therefore had standing to bring their action under the act. The court remanded the action and held that the trial court did not apply the act's required burden-shifting test and therefore did not decide whether defendants sufficiently rebutted plaintiffs' prima facie case. The court could not affirm the decision by holding that the same result would have been reached even if the trial court had applied the proper statutory standard because it was not clear that the same result would have been reached. The environmental impact statement in issue failed to consider air quality and was submitted to defendant commissioner after he already had approved the project.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision in favor of defendants, who were a corporation, a municipality, and the chairman of a city planning commission, and remanded for further proceedings because the trial court failed to apply the statutorily required burden-shifting test to determine whether defendants sufficiently rebutted plaintiff citizens' prima facie case for violation of a state environmental statute.

 

589 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Griswold Inn, Inc. v. State


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


183 Conn. 552; 441 A.2d 16; 1981 Conn. LEXIS 497; 27 A.L.R.4th 1144


January 9, 1981, Argued  
April 21, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment determining the validity of the statutes prohibiting the sale of alcoholic beverages on Good Friday, and for injunctive relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex and reserved by the court, Higgins, J., for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inn sought a declaratory judgment in the Superior Court in the Judicial Circuit of Middlesex (Connecticut) to determine the validity of statutes prohibiting the sale of alcoholic beverages on Good Friday, and the superior court reserved for advice two questions regarding the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 30-91, 30-74, and 30-77.


OVERVIEW: The court considered two questions on reservation from the superior court regarding the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 30-91, 30-74, and 30-77, which prohibited the sale of alcohol of Good Friday. The court held that §§ 30-91, 30-74, and 30-77 were unconstitutional under Conn. Const. art. VII, § 1 and U.S. Const. amends. I and XIV. The court found that the statutes violated the Establishment Clause because no clear secular purpose justified the prohibition of liquor sales on that day, and the primary effect of the Good Friday prohibition was an impermissible endorsement of the Protestant and Catholic faiths. The court found that Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 30-91, 30-74, and 30-77 resulted in an entanglement between religion and state because the statutes required an impermissible degree of inspection or monitoring of religious institutions or practices. The state was required to monitor the sale of alcohol on Good Friday and thereby required in effect to monitor and enforce observance of a religious holiday by permittees in order to enforce Conn. Gen. Stat. § 30-91(a) and (b).


OUTCOME: The court answered two questions of the superior court in the affirmative, and held that three statutes prohibiting the sale of liquor on Good Friday were in violation of the Establishment Clause and the Connecticut constitution.

 

590 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Conger


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


183 Conn. 386; 439 A.2d 381; 1981 Conn. LEXIS 484


January 7, 1981, Argued  
April 7, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information in three counts charging the defendant with the crime of larceny in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury and tried to the jury before Henebry, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment entered by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Danbury (Connecticut) of conviction of larceny in the second degree, contending that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence collected as a result of the searches of the truck which he was driving when arrested and of two vehicles at his residence.


OVERVIEW: Acting on a tip, police stopped a truck driven by defendant and found it, as well as two other vehicles located at defendant's residence, to be stolen. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress. Defendant was tried and found guilty on three counts of second-degree larceny by receiving and retaining stolen property. The trial court entered a judgment of conviction. On appeal, the court set aside the judgment and remanded the case. The court held that the trial court erred in denying the motion to suppress. The trial court failed to address the legality of the initial stop of defendant's truck. Defendant, as an occupant of the truck, had an interest in continuing his travels without government intrusion. Thus, even though the truck was stolen, his rights under U.S. Const. amend. IV could have been violated when the truck was stopped. Further, the trial court failed to resolve the issue as to whether the police lawfully entered defendant's property to conduct the inspection which resulted in the discovery of the other stolen vehicles. Thus, the court remanded the case.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the trial court's judgment of conviction of defendant of larceny in the second degree and remanded the case. On defendant's motion to suppress, the trial court failed to address whether the initial stop of the stolen truck driven by defendant was illegal and failed to address whether entry by police onto defendant's property was lawful.

 

591 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Burritt Mut. Sav. Bank v. Tucker


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


183 Conn. 369; 439 A.2d 396; 1981 Conn. LEXIS 487


December 5, 1980, Argued  
April 7, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for the foreclosure of a mortgage, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, N. O'Neill, J.; judgment of strict foreclosure and subsequent orders finding the named defendant in contempt, from which that defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant debtor sought review of the decision of the Hartford-New Britain Superior Court (Connecticut), which granted judgment for plaintiff lender in its foreclosure action and found the debtor in contempt.


OVERVIEW: The lender filed a foreclosure lawsuit against the debtor. The debtor failed to plead and the trial court entered a judgment of strict foreclosure and issued two contempt orders. The court affirmed the trial court's decision, but remanded for the purpose of ascertaining the amount of the debt. An erroneous but bona fide belief on the part of the debtor that he was not required to plead until the statutory continuance had expired would not have warranted the entry of a default. However, the utter worthlessness of the motion, which was filed the day before the scheduled hearing, indicated that the debtor's only purpose was to delay the proceeding. The trial court had an inherent power to disregard sham or frivolous pleadings that were interposed for the purpose of thwarting the orderly progress of a case. The court remanded for calculation of the debt because the debtor did raise a defense concerning the amount of the mortgage debt before the trial court, and under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 527 a mortgage debt could only be proved by an affidavit if no defense as to the amount of the debt was interposed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision granting judgment for the lender in its foreclosure action, but vacated the determination of the amount of the debt and remanded for the purpose of ascertaining the amount of the debt.

 

592 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


Maloney v. Pac


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


183 Conn. 313; 439 A.2d 349; 1981 Conn. LEXIS 474


December 12, 1980, Argued  
March 17, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a declaratory judgment to determine the constitutionality of a statute, and for injunctive relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford, where the defendant city of Hartford cross claimed against the defendants the state traffic commission and the Legislative Regulation Review Committee, and the issues were tried to the court, O'Brien, J.; judgment for the plaintiff on her complaint and for the defendant city of Hartford on its cross claim, from which the defendant Legislative Regulations Review Committee and the defendant Balf Company appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; judgment modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, legislative regulation review committee (LRRC) and company, challenged a decision of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which ruled for appellee resident that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-170 was unconstitutional in allowing a LRRC veto of a state traffic commission rule. The city argued that the Uniform Administrative Procedure Act (UAPA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-166 et seq., was inapplicable.


OVERVIEW: The commission adopted a regulation banning through truck traffic on two streets in the city. The regulation was submitted to the LRRC, which disapproved it. The resident sought declaratory and injunctive relief for damages from the trucks. The trial court was bound by a prior ruling that the traffic regulation was subject to LRRC review, but found for the resident that § 4-170 unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed the relief ordered, but vacated the finding that the statute was unconstitutional because the issue was governed by statute. The court ruled that the resident had standing to bring the action because she suffered direct injury from the noise and vibration of the trucks. The court found that the commission did not rely on its discretion when it removed the signs, but acted solely in response to the LRRC veto of the regulation. The court ruled that the regulation did not fall under the UAPA and was not subject to LRRC review because its impact was not sufficiently general in the state. The court found that the commission was authorized to regulate through truck traffic within a city's limits for public safety in cooperation and agreement with local authorities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment as to the injunctive relief ordered for the resident and the city on its cross-claim and vacated and set aside the portion of the judgment declaring the statute allowing legislative veto of administrative regulations unconstitutional.

Bencivenga v. Milford


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


183 Conn. 168; 438 A.2d 1174; 1981 Conn. LEXIS 459


November 5, 1980, Argued  
February 17, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for an injunction restraining the defendants from enforcing the Housing Code of the City of Milford as to certain buildings owned by the plaintiffs, and for damages, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford at Milford and tried to the court, O'Sullivan, J.; judgment for the defendants from which the plaintiffs appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners challenged a judgment from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Ansonia-Milford at Milford (Connecticut), which dissolved an ex parte temporary injunction and denied permanent injunctive relief to the owners after the owners brought an action seeking to restrain defendants, a city and its officials, from taking any action against the owners under a city housing code.


OVERVIEW: The owners alleged that the city housing code did not apply to their vacant dwellings. However, in reaching its conclusion to deny injunctive relief to the owners, the trial court passed upon the issue of whether the city housing code, pursuant to Milford, Conn., Housing Code § 11, was preempted by the State Building Code when it came to the issue of vacant dwellings. Thus, on appeal, the court held that the trial court erred in not deciding the issue of preemption as it related to the owner's properties. Specifically, the court held that the power of the city to enact the ordinance, which became the city housing code, depended primarily upon whether it was in conflict with, or inconsistent with, the State Building Code. As a result, the court, although noting that it did not undertake any detailed analysis of the two codes, pointed out that there were at least some apparent conflicts, which required that the trial court reach and resolve the issue of preemption. Thus, the court held that without having disposed of the threshold issue of preemption, the factual determination of the trial court could not stand. Accordingly, the court ordered a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the trial court's judgment, which had denied the owners injunctive relief. As a result, the court ordered a new trial.

Hartford Electric Light Co. v. Tucker


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


183 Conn. 85; 438 A.2d 828; 1981 Conn. LEXIS 447


December 4, 1980, Argued  
February 10, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for the acceptance of the report of a receiver of rents and for an award of attorney's fees, and application for the allowance of receiver's fees and costs, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, N. O'Neill, J.; judgment for the plaintiff, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner challenged a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain (Connecticut), which entered judgment for appellee utility company in its action for the acceptance of the report of a receiver of rents and for an award of attorney's fees and its application for the allowance of receiver's fees and costs. A receivership had imposed on the owner in accordance with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16-262f.


OVERVIEW: The property owner unsuccessfully challenged the utility company's appointment of a utility receivership to retain the rents from a number of apartment buildings owned by the owner. The owner was indebted to the utility company in excess of $ 9,000. The receivership was terminated and costs, and fees were assessed against the owner. The trial court awarded attorney's fees, fees to the receiver, and approved the report of the rent receiver. On appeal, the court noted that there was statutory authority in § 16-262f for the award of fees and that its review was limited to whether the trial court's determination was erroneous. There was no error in permitting the rent receiver to take the rent receipts as a first lien. The award to the rent receiver was permitted under the statute, and the amount was not excessive.

Heritage Sav. & Loan Asso. v. Schaller


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


183 Conn. 117; 438 A.2d 849; 1981 Conn. LEXIS 452


December 10, 1980, Argued  
February 10, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a foreclosure by sale, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, N. O'Neill, J.; judgment ordering that the conveyance be satisfied and that certain proceeds of the sale be distributed, from which the defendant state of Connecticut appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State appealed the decision from the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut), which granted judgment to plaintiff creditor in the creditor's action for a foreclosure by sale. The creditor was awarded an order that the conveyance be satisfied and that the proceeds of the sale be distributed.


OVERVIEW: The creditor brought a foreclosure proceeding wherein the State had an unrecorded tax lien it sought to enforce against the delinquent taxpayer. The State argued that the unrecorded lien was enforceable against the taxpayer because the taxpayer held the equity of redemption in the subject premises. The trial court ruled that the State's recovery was limited to the amount of the lien which was recorded before the notice of lis pendens was filed and that the State forfeited its rights to the balance for its failure to comply with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-325, the lis pendens statute. On appeal the court noted that § 52-325 had been held unconstitutional. The State's tax lien was statutorily created under § 14-420 as soon as the tax remained unpaid after the last day for filing the return. The lien existed whether or not it was recorded. Finding that the State was a proper party to the action, the court found error, and set aside the judgment, remanding for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court found reversed the judgment for the creditor and remanded the case for further proceedings.

State v. Smith


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


183 Conn. 17; 438 A.2d 1165; 1981 Conn. LEXIS 433


October 15, 1980, Argued  
January 27, 1981, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of injury or risk of injury to a minor child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Reynolds, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty on both counts and appeal by the defendant to this court.



DISPOSITION: Error; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which was entered on a jury verdict convicting him of two counts of injury or risk of injury to a minor child pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21. Defendant claimed error on the grounds including that § 53-21 was unconstitutionally void for vagueness and violated the guarantee of separation of powers.


OVERVIEW: The State charged defendant in connection with several incidents involving inappropriate touching in the genital area of his son's 12-year-old stepdaughter. Finding error, the court set aside the judgment and ordered a new trial. The court held that (1) § 53-21 was not unconstitutionally vague in relation to defendant's conduct that encompassed the deliberate touching of the private parts of a child under the age of 16 in a sexual and indecent manner, (2) § 53-21 did not contravene the doctrine of separation of powers because it did not represent any delegation of legislative powers, (3) the statute did not violate the prohibition on ex post facto laws pursuant to U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 because the type of acts for which defendant was convicted had long been considered violative of § 53-21, and (4) the trial court erred in instructing the jury in initial and supplemental instructions that it could have found defendant guilty if it believed beyond a reasonable doubt that the "scale" had been tipped in favor of conviction because the described standard was not the same as the standard of proof beyond a reasonable doubt that was required by the constitutional Due Process Clause.


OUTCOME: The court found error in defendant's conviction of two counts of injury or risk of injury to a minor child. The court set aside the trial court's judgment and ordered a new trial.

State v. Truppi


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


182 Conn. 449; 438 A.2d 712; 1980 Conn. LEXIS 1008


October 9, 1980, Argued  
December 16, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information in four counts charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree, assault in the first degree, robbery in the first degree, and kidnapping in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Zarrilli, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, and appeal by the defendant.

The appellant filed a motion for reargument which was denied.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut), which entered a verdict and judgment of guilty against defendant for sexual assault in the first degree, assault in the first degree, robbery in the first degree, and kidnapping in the second degree, and which denied his motion for reargument.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of sexual assault in the first degree, assault in the first degree, robbery in the first degree, and kidnapping in the second degree. The lower court imposed separate sentences under each count, to run consecutively. Defendant claimed error in an instruction on intent and in the consecutive sentences for assault and robbery. He argued that lower court's instructions to the jury violated his constitutional right to due process by shifting to him the burden of proof of intent. The court held that the lower court avoided the ambiguous terms "intent" and "act" in the unchallenged portion of the instructions related to sexual assault in the first degree. The court held that because an inference of intent to cause serious physical injury from proof of the circumstances of a multiple stabbing accords with reason, it did not offend due process to inform the jury that the law permitted them to so infer. The court held however that the lower court's instructions on robbery in the first degree and kidnapping in the second degree lacked the precision and comprehensiveness of those given on the crime of assault.


OUTCOME: The court held that there was no error and the judgment was affirmed as to the second and third counts charging sexual assault in the first degree and assault in the first degree, but that there was error as to the first and fourth counts of the information, charging kidnapping in the second degree and robbery in the first degree respectively, and as to those counts only, the judgment was set aside and a new trial was ordered.

State v. Hackett


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]

182 Conn. 511; 438 A.2d 726; 1980 Conn. LEXIS 1010

DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut) for murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54(a)(2) and robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134.


OVERVIEW: A restaurant owner was shot to death while sitting in his car. Defendant maintained that another man shot the victim, but the other man, who cooperated with the State, testified that defendant was the shooter. On appeal, defendant asserted 16 claims of error. In affirming the murder and robbery convictions, the court held that there was sufficient evidence from which a reasonable jury could have concluded that defendant was guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. As to defendant's claim regarding the trial judge's ex parte contact with a juror concerning an exhibit that was ruled to be inadmissible after the juror was allowed to look at it, the court held that even if the contact were improper, defendant failed to show that he was prejudiced by it.

State v. Zdanis


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


182 Conn. 388; 438 A.2d 696; 1980 Conn. LEXIS 1002


October 9, 1980, Argued  
December 2, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Indictment charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to a three-judge panel, Parskey, O'Brien and Covello, Js.; judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford (Connecticut) of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder. On appeal, defendant claimed that the trial court erred (1) in concluding that he failed to establish his defense of extreme emotional disturbance; (2) in concluding that he acted with the intent to cause death; and (3) in the instruction to the grand jury that every person is presumed to intend the natural and necessary consequences of his acts. The court ruled that the court did not err in refusing to find that the defendant had satisfied his burden of proving his defense of extreme emotional disturbance. The court noted that defendant claimed that the shooting was accidental and also that he acted under the influence of extreme emotional disturbance, and determined that that these two claims could not be reconciled. The court also ruled that a review of the circumstantial evidence including the testimony establishing the shot sequence by the neighbor and police officer supported the finding that defendant acted with intent to kill.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

600 of 2220 DOCUMENTS


State v. Theriault


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Connecticut


182 Conn. 366; 438 A.2d 432; 1980 Conn. LEXIS 997


October 8, 1980, Argued  
November 25, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with the crimes of robbery in the first degree, unlawful restraint in the first degree, burglary in the first degree and possession of burglary tools, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and tried to the jury before Daly, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty and appeal by the defendant.



DISPOSITION: Error in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut), which was entered on a jury verdict convicting him of robbery in the first degree, unlawful restraint in the first degree, burglary in the first degree, and possession of burglary tools. Defendant claimed error on the grounds including the trial court's refusal to suppress identification testimony.


OVERVIEW: The State charged that defendant was one of three men who committed an armed robbery of two employees at an insurance office. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress the out-of-court identifications of him made by both of the employees at the police barracks. Finding error in part, the court set aside defendant's conviction of robbery and remanded for a new trial on that offense, and affirmed defendant's conviction of the remaining offenses. The court held that although the show-up identification procedure used was unnecessarily suggestive, the identification evidence was reliable and the trial court did not err in refusing to suppress the evidence of the identifications. However, the trial court erred by instructing the jury that defendant had the "mental state" required for the commission of the robbery offense. The instruction effectively directed a finding of guilty on the issue of defendant's intent in being an accessory to robbery pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-8. The trial court's error related only to the robbery offense because separate instructions were given with regard to the other crimes charged.


OUTCOME: The court found error as to the trial court's conviction of defendant of robbery in the first degree, and the judgment was set aside and remanded for a new trial on that offense. The court found no error as to the trial court's conviction of defendant as to the remaining offenses.
